# LV_DCP — Developer Context Platform

**Local-first engineering memory.** Turns projects on macOS into a queryable context layer for Claude, IDE agents, and humans. Supports Python, TypeScript/JS, Go, Rust, Java, Kotlin, and Swift. Reduces token cost of repeated code reading, builds a relation graph, and makes agent edits safer.

[![Phase 9 Complete](https://img.shields.io/badge/phase-9%20complete-green)](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.61-obsidian-sync-all-json.md)
[![Version 0.8.61](https://img.shields.io/badge/version-0.8.61-blue)](pyproject.toml)
[![License: Apache 2.0](https://img.shields.io/badge/license-Apache%202.0-blue)](LICENSE)
[![Python 3.12+](https://img.shields.io/badge/python-3.12+-blue)](pyproject.toml)

## What it actually does

You ask a question in plain language — _"where is refresh token logic?"_ or _"change login validation"_ — and LV_DCP returns a **2–20 KB markdown pack** with the 2–5 most relevant files and symbols. Your LLM agent reads that pack instead of grep-walking the whole repository.

For edit tasks, the pack groups files by role — **target files**, **impacted tests**, **impacted configs** — and surfaces dependencies found through the relation graph, not just keyword matching. A test file gets included even if it doesn't contain the keywords, because the graph knows it imports the file you're changing.

```bash
$ ctx pack . "refresh token rotation" --mode edit

# Context pack — edit
**Project:** my-api
**Intent:** refresh token rotation
**Coverage:** high

## Target files
- app/services/auth.py (score 12.34)
- app/handlers/auth.py (score 8.21)

## Impacted tests
- tests/test_auth.py

## Impacted configs
- config/settings.yaml

## Candidate symbols
- app.services.auth.refresh_access_token
- app.services.auth.ACCESS_TTL
- app.handlers.auth.refresh

## Reminder: edit discipline
1. Build minimal plan before patching multiple files
2. Never touch write_protected_paths
3. Run lint + typecheck + tests after every change
4. Summarize the diff when done
```

## Core value proposition

- **10× fewer tokens** when Claude/Cursor/Cline works on a large Python codebase. The agent reads a 5 KB pack instead of 50–80 KB of raw files.
- **Automatic invocation via MCP.** Once `ctx mcp install` is run, Claude Code (CLI and VS Code extension) calls LV_DCP automatically before answering architectural or edit questions — zero ceremony for the user.
- **No context slips through.** Edit-mode packs include impacted tests and configs discovered via graph walk — the kind of files `grep` misses.
- **Local-only.** No network calls, no telemetry, no SaaS. Indexes live in `.context/` next to each project. Secrets in source files are detected by regex and excluded from the search index.
- **Deterministic and measurable.** A retrieval eval harness with 32 golden queries is a first-class citizen; every retrieval change must not regress the metrics.

## Status

**v0.8.61 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx obsidian sync-all --json` for nightly multi-project audit trails — the first multi-project iteration surface to ship `--json`, introducing a fifth shape pattern (fleet-iteration with summary counters + per-entry results array) on top of the v0.8.42-v0.8.60 single-object / bare-array / wrapper-with-null lineage. The `ctx obsidian sync-all` command has been the canonical "iterate every registered project, sync stale ones to the Obsidian vault, surface a `Done. Synced: N, skipped: M, failed: K` footer" surface since v0.8.28 shipped — but every nightly-cron / CI orchestrator wrapping it had to grep the human chrome (`[sync] / [skip] / [fail] / Done.`) to figure out which projects synced, which were skipped (and *why* — fresh under stale-hours? no cache.db? nonexistent root?), and which failed (with what error?). The text format is brittle (project paths containing the substring `[fail]` or `Done.` would collide with the per-project lines), and the per-project failure *reason* was on stderr while the per-project success was on stdout — no single place to assemble a structured audit trail per nightly run, leaving every fleet-orchestration automation (a nightly audit appender writing one JSONL row per cron firing for compliance / debugging / SLO tracking via `ctx obsidian sync-all --json | jq -c '{when: now, synced, skipped, failed, results: [.results[] | {project: .project_root, outcome, reason, error}]}' >> nightly_sync_audit.jsonl`, a failure-only pager that mails ops only when actual failures occurred and includes the per-project error so operators can act without re-running via `ctx obsidian sync-all --json | jq -e '.failed == 0' || ctx obsidian sync-all --json | jq -r '.results[] | select(.outcome == "failed") | "\(.project_root): \(.error)"' | mail -s "obsidian sync failures" ops@example.com`, a pre-flight "what would happen under force-re-sync" plan check that lists every project that would sync without committing to the fleet-wide run via `ctx obsidian sync-all --dry-run --stale-hours 0 --json | jq -r '.results[] | select(.outcome == "synced") | .project_root'`, a per-project dashboard tile fed from a single CLI invocation rather than per-project follow-ups via `ctx obsidian sync-all --json | jq -r '.results[] | "\(.project_root)\t\(.outcome)\t\(.reason // .error // "-")"' > /var/www/sync_dashboard.tsv`, a skipped-rate hygiene check tracking the "fresh skip" rate over time so an operator notices when the cron interval is too tight relative to `--stale-hours` via `ctx obsidian sync-all --json | jq '.skipped / (.synced + .skipped + .failed)'`) to brittle stdout/stderr stitching with no per-project provenance preserved across runs. `_run_plan` from `apps/cli/commands/obsidian_cmd.py` already executed the plan and tracked synced/skipped/failed counts since v0.8.28 — we just weren't surfacing the per-project outcome detail from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx obsidian sync-all` that emits a single JSON object with seven top-level fields locked by the new `_SYNC_ALL_JSON_KEYS` frozenset and a per-entry array locked by the `_SYNC_ALL_RESULT_KEYS` frozenset: `{vault (round-tripped from `obsidian.vault_path` so a script can confirm the run targeted the vault it intended without re-deriving from the config file; same v0.8.48-v0.8.60 "round-trip the actual input" precedent), stale_hours (round-tripped from the `--stale-hours` CLI flag so the consumer can reason about why some projects were skipped as "fresh"), dry_run (boolean — `true` when `--dry-run` was passed, `false` for a real execution; lets the consumer distinguish "what would happen" from "what did happen" within a single payload schema), synced/skipped/failed (counters that mirror the text view's `Done. Synced: N, skipped: M, failed: K` footer 1:1 — the canonical "did anything happen" signal; `jq -e '.failed == 0'` is the natural CI guard for "all-clean run"), results (per-project array with `{project_root, outcome, reason, error}` entries — `outcome` is exactly one of `"synced"` / `"skipped"` / `"failed"` so a `jq -r '.results[] | select(.outcome == "failed") | .project_root'` filter is unambiguous; `reason` populated only on `"skipped"` mirroring the text view's `[skip] <root>: <reason>` line; `error` populated only on `"failed"` mirroring `[fail] <root>: <err>`; both explicit `null` elsewhere so consumers can `jq -r '.results[] | .error // empty'` without a defined-key guard)}`. **First fleet-iteration shape** — prior surfaces split into per-row reads (bare arrays — v0.8.44 memory list, v0.8.49 watch list), single-result mutations with exception-on-absent (bare entry — v0.8.54 watch add, v0.8.57 memory accept, v0.8.58 memory reject, v0.8.59 timeline enable, v0.8.60 timeline disable), single-result mutations with no-op-on-absent (wrapper-with-null — v0.8.56 watch remove), and mutations with single count + invocation params (flat dict — v0.8.38 registry prune, v0.8.55 timeline prune); `sync-all` introduces a fifth pattern (summary counters + per-entry results array) natural for any future fleet-iteration surface (e.g. a hypothetical `ctx wiki update --all --json` or `ctx scan --all --json`). **Same payload covers every exit branch** — success path, dry-run plan path, `obsidian.enabled=false` no-op path, no-projects-registered no-op path all emit the same seven-key shape (with empty `results: []` and zero counters on the no-op paths), so a consumer's `jq` filter never needs to branch on which exit path fired; mirrors the v0.8.45/v0.8.49/v0.8.50 "no-work-done is still a successful run, surface the structured null rather than printing prose" discipline. **Dry-run path locked** — `--dry-run --json` emits the same schema with `dry_run: true` and every `outcome` reflecting the *plan* (would-sync / would-skip), zero subprocess invocations, no on-disk markers written; locked by `test_sync_all_json_dry_run_emits_plan_without_subprocess` which asserts `mock_run.call_count == 0` AND no marker files written — proves a regression that fired the sync subprocess in dry-run mode would defeat the dry-run safety net and break the test. **`_run_plan` refactored to surface per-project outcomes** — added a fourth tuple slot (`results: list[dict[str, object]]`) alongside the existing `(synced, skipped, failed)` counters; the text path ignores the new return slot and behaves identically (every existing test passes), the JSON path consumes it. Added `quiet=as_json` parameter that suppresses the `[sync] / [skip] / [fail]` per-project prose so stdout stays pure data in JSON mode; `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune / v0.8.56 watch remove / v0.8.57 memory accept / v0.8.58 memory reject / v0.8.59 timeline enable / v0.8.60 timeline disable: pure data on stdout, error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (missing config / empty `vault_path` → exit 1 with no JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON). CLI-only change at the command boundary — `_run_plan` is internal to `obsidian_cmd.py`, no library code touched (`ObsidianPublisher`, `_invoke_sync`, `load_config` all unchanged). Five new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy `[sync] / Done. Synced: N, ...` lines byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.60 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every nightly-cron consumer that greps for `Done.` or `failed:`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked seven-key set + four-key per-entry set with **mixed outcomes in one payload** (synced + skipped + failed all in one cross-checked test that asserts top-level counters match per-entry outcomes AND `[sync]/[fail]` chrome NOT on stdout — proves the `quiet=as_json` discipline AND the success-side marker is still written even in JSON mode), `--dry-run --json` emits `dry_run: true` with zero subprocess invocations and no marker writes (locks the dry-run safety net so a regression that fired sync in dry-run breaks this test), `obsidian.enabled=false` → exit 0 with empty `results: []` (locks the no-op-is-success discipline so a regression that exits 1 on disabled config breaks this test), missing config → exit 1 with no JSON success-shape payload on stdout (locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the validation error into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload breaks this test). All 23 tests in `test_obsidian_sync_all.py` pass (18 pre-existing + 5 new). All 170 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: omit the `vault` round-trip from the payload (consumer would have to re-derive from the config file path, defeating the "round-trip the actual input" precedent across v0.8.48-v0.8.60), use a sparse map keyed by project_root for `results` (loses iteration order which is meaningful for time-correlation in audit logs; the array preserves it; same v0.8.49 / v0.8.55 array-over-dict precedent), include a `duration_seconds` field per entry (recoverable via the per-project `obsidian sync --json` v0.8.53 payload if needed; out of scope for the fleet-iteration summary — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56-v0.8.60 argument against gratuitous per-entry metadata), surface `last_sync_marker_age_hours` on skipped entries (already in the `reason` string as `"fresh (3.2h old)"`; parseable but redundant to add a separate field), make `dry_run` an option that only takes effect with `--json` (would split the text/JSON parity contract; both paths honor `--dry-run` consistently), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.60 argument; the schema-locked frozenset tests catch accidental divergence). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `obsidian sync-all`), `obsidian sync` (already shipped v0.8.53) / `obsidian status` (already shipped v0.8.50) subcommands untouched, `_invoke_sync` library helper signature unchanged, on-disk side effects (per-project markers written on success) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `_run_plan` already mutates, no MCP surface (multi-project sync orchestration is an operator-driven nightly cron, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing sync-all test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.61-obsidian-sync-all-json.md).

**v0.8.60 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx timeline disable --json` closes the timeline-flag mutation surface end-to-end alongside v0.8.45-era `ctx timeline status --json` (read) and v0.8.59 `ctx timeline enable --json` (enable side). The `ctx timeline disable` command has been the canonical "turn off per-project timeline capture so the scanner runs without the SqliteTimelineSink wired in" surface since spec-010 shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `timeline: disabled for <root>` footer that collapsed both the post-mutation flag state and the on-disk artifact path into a single prose line, leaving every timeline-teardown automation (a per-project archival script that bulk-disables timeline capture before snapshotting and unmounting via `ctx registry ls --json | jq -r '.[] | select(.scanned == true) | .root' | xargs -I{} ctx timeline disable --project {} --json | jq -s 'map({project: .project_root, enabled: .enabled})'`, an IDE "disable timeline" toggle that needs to confirm the transition before re-rendering the daemon-status panel via `ctx timeline disable --project "$root" --json | jq -e '.enabled == false'`, a daemon-shutdown idempotent ensure-off step that gates re-runs via `ctx timeline status --project "$root" --json | jq -e '.enabled == false' || ctx timeline disable --project "$root" --json` so a project being unregistered doesn't re-trigger a noisy second flag-write, audit-trail appenders like `ctx timeline disable --project "$root" --json | jq '{when: now, project: .project_root, flag: .flag_path, decision: "disabled"}' >> teardown_audit.jsonl`) to brittle line-grepping over the `timeline: disabled for <root>` footer (which trips on project paths containing the substring "disabled for" or platform-specific quoting). `_write_flag` from `apps/cli/commands/timeline_cmd.py` already wrote the on-disk `.context/timeline.enabled` marker file with `off\n` content deterministically since the timeline feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx timeline disable` that emits a single JSON object with three fields locked by the v0.8.59 `_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS` frozenset (zero new helpers introduced — the entire shape is locked at the v0.8.59 declaration site): `{project_root (resolved absolute path of the project that was disabled — round-tripped so a script can confirm the call actually targeted the project root it intended without re-deriving from argv; same v0.8.48-v0.8.59 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), enabled (post-mutation boolean — always `false` after `disable`; lets a script `jq -e '.enabled == false'` to confirm the state transition without a follow-up `status --json` call — symmetric mirror of v0.8.59 enable's `enabled: true` round-trip), flag_path (absolute path of the `.context/timeline.enabled` marker file the daemon / scanner reads — surfaces the actual on-disk artifact so a debugging script can `cat $(jq -r .flag_path)` to inspect the raw `off` content; also lets fleet-management tools assemble a per-project flag-path inventory via `ctx registry ls --json | jq -r '.[].root' | xargs -I{} ctx timeline disable --project {} --json | jq -r .flag_path`)}`. **Single object, not a wrapper** — `timeline disable` is a single-result mutation that returns the post-mutation flag state directly; no `{disabled: {...}}` envelope (the `enabled` field IS the success signal, no need for a top-level discriminator parallel to v0.8.56 watch remove's `{removed: <entry|null>}` because the no-op-on-absent case here is `disable` itself which is unconditionally a success — there's no "absent" state, just "already off" which is idempotent and emits the same payload). **Cross-surface schema lock realized** — the v0.8.59-introduced `_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS = frozenset({"project_root", "enabled", "flag_path"})` and the `_flag_to_json` helper now span **both** flag-mutation surfaces (enable v0.8.59 + disable v0.8.60); one helper, two surfaces, one frozenset to bump if a future field appears on the flag (mirrors the v0.8.44 `_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS` → v0.8.57/v0.8.58 cross-surface pattern that closed the memory-review surface, and the v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56 `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` → `_project_to_json` pattern that closed the daemon-registration surface). **Idempotent re-disable semantic** — `disable_cmd` has no state-machine guard (calling it on an already-disabled project is a no-op-on-state-but-write-on-disk that returns the same payload), so the JSON contract is "always emit the post-mutation state" rather than "emit the diff"; locked by `test_timeline_disable_json_idempotent_re_disable` which double-disables and asserts the second emission is bytewise identical to the first — proves a script can safely re-run `disable --json` without branching on "was it already off", same render-switch-not-semantic-change discipline as v0.8.57's idempotent re-accept lock and v0.8.59's idempotent re-enable lock. **Cross-state flip semantic** — calling `enable` then `disable --json` flips the flag cleanly with a **stable** `flag_path` (same on-disk marker rewritten in place, no fresh file path); locked by `test_timeline_disable_json_overrides_enabled_state` which mirrors v0.8.59's `test_timeline_enable_json_overrides_disabled_state` cross-state flip — proves no duplicate file is created on the state transition, just an in-place rewrite of the existing `.context/timeline.enabled` marker. Together with the v0.8.59 enable counterpart this **locks the bidirectional flip semantic**: `enable` → `disable` → `enable` round-trips through the same on-disk artifact, no fresh writes on either edge — a fleet-toggle script will not leave behind orphaned marker files. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune / v0.8.56 watch remove / v0.8.57 memory accept / v0.8.58 memory reject / v0.8.59 timeline enable: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (this command has no validation failure path — `disable` always succeeds against any path Typer's argument layer accepts; the flag-write is a pure on-disk side effect with no failure mode beyond a filesystem error, which surfaces as exit 1 + stderr message in both modes). CLI-only change — no library code touched (`_write_flag` and `_flag_file` helpers unchanged; the `_flag_to_json` helper from v0.8.59 reused with `enabled=False`; no new helpers, no new imports). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `timeline: disabled for <root>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.59 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `disabled`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked three-key set (`_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS = {project_root, enabled, flag_path}` frozenset; `enabled is False` round-trip; cross-checked via on-disk `.context/timeline.enabled` content read confirms the file actually contains `off` matching the emitted payload — a regression that emitted `enabled: false` but failed to write the file would fail this cross-check), idempotent re-disable double-call returns bytewise-identical payloads (locks the no-state-machine-guard semantic so a regression that flipped `disable_cmd` into a "must-be-enabled" guard would break this test), enable-then-disable flips the flag cleanly with stable `flag_path` (locks the cross-state flip semantic so a regression that created a fresh file on the flip would break this test by changing the `flag_path`). All 24 tests in `test_timeline_cmd.py` pass (16 pre-existing + 4 v0.8.59 enable + 4 new disable). All 165 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: emit a wrapper object `{disabled: {project_root, flag_path}}` (over-engineered for a 3-field flat payload; the bare flat shape matches the v0.8.59 enable precedent for the symmetric mirror), include `previous_enabled: bool` in the payload (recoverable via `status --json` before/after diff if needed; out of scope for the per-command payload — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56-v0.8.59 argument against gratuitous metadata), include the raw flag-file content (`"off"` string) alongside the parsed boolean (redundant — the boolean IS the parsed content, and the consumer can `cat $(jq -r .flag_path)` if they want the raw string), require `--force` to re-disable an already-disabled project (would change the documented no-state-machine semantic; same "ship has sailed" argument as v0.8.55-v0.8.59's destructive-flag rejections), introduce a separate `_disable_to_json` helper instead of reusing `_flag_to_json` (would defeat the cross-surface schema-lock pattern; same "one helper, multiple surfaces" precedent as v0.8.54 reusing `_project_to_json` and v0.8.57 reusing `_memory_to_json`), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.59 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `timeline disable`), `timeline enable` (already shipped v0.8.59) / `status` / `reconcile` / `prune` / `backfill` subcommands untouched, `_write_flag` library helper signature unchanged, on-disk side effect (flag-file write with `off\n` content) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `_write_flag` already writes, no MCP surface (timeline-flag mutation is an operator-driven write, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing timeline test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.60-timeline-disable-json.md).

**v0.8.59 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx timeline enable --json` opens the timeline-flag mutation surface (the matching `disable --json` is queued for v0.8.60 to close the surface end-to-end alongside the pre-existing `ctx timeline status --json` for reads). The `ctx timeline enable` command has been the canonical "turn on per-project timeline capture so the scanner records symbol add/modify/remove events into the timeline DB" surface since spec-010 shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `timeline: enabled for <root>` footer that collapsed both the post-mutation flag state and the on-disk artifact path into a single prose line, leaving every timeline-bootstrap automation (a per-project setup script that bulk-enables timeline capture across all registered projects via `ctx registry ls --json | jq -r '.[] | select(.scanned == true) | .root' | xargs -I{} ctx timeline enable --project {} --json | jq -s 'map({project: .project_root, enabled: .enabled})'`, an IDE "enable timeline" toggle that needs to confirm the transition before re-rendering the daemon-status panel via `ctx timeline enable --project "$root" --json | jq -e '.enabled == true'`, a daemon-bootstrap idempotent ensure-on step that gates re-runs via `ctx timeline status --project "$root" --json | jq -e '.enabled == true' || ctx timeline enable --project "$root" --json` so a freshly registered project picks up timeline capture without a noisy second flag-write, audit-trail appenders like `ctx timeline enable --project "$root" --json | jq '{when: now, project: .project_root, flag: .flag_path, decision: "enabled"}' >> setup_audit.jsonl`) to brittle line-grepping over the `timeline: enabled for <root>` footer (which trips on project paths containing the substring "enabled for" or platform-specific quoting). `_write_flag` from `apps/cli/commands/timeline_cmd.py` already wrote the on-disk `.context/timeline.enabled` marker file deterministically since the timeline feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx timeline enable` that emits a single JSON object with three fields locked by the new `_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS` frozenset: `{project_root (resolved absolute path of the project that was enabled — round-tripped so a script can confirm the call actually targeted the project root it intended without re-deriving from argv; same v0.8.48/v0.8.50/v0.8.52-v0.8.58 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), enabled (post-mutation boolean — always `true` after `enable`, will round-trip as `false` after the v0.8.60 `disable --json` ship; lets a script `jq -e '.enabled == true'` to confirm the state transition without a follow-up `status --json` call — same single-object post-mutation discipline as v0.8.57 `memory accept --json`'s `status: "accepted"` and v0.8.58 `memory reject --json`'s `status: "rejected"` round-trip), flag_path (absolute path of the `.context/timeline.enabled` marker file the daemon / scanner reads — surfaces the actual on-disk artifact so a debugging script can `cat $(jq -r .flag_path)` to inspect the raw `on` / `off` content; also lets fleet-management tools assemble a per-project flag-path inventory via `ctx registry ls --json | jq -r '.[].root' | xargs -I{} ctx timeline enable --project {} --json | jq -r .flag_path`)}`. **Single object, not a wrapper** — `timeline enable` is a single-result mutation that returns the post-mutation flag state directly; no `{enabled: {...}}` envelope (the `enabled` field IS the success signal, no need for a top-level discriminator parallel to v0.8.56 watch remove's `{removed: <entry|null>}` because the no-op-on-absent case here is `enable` itself which is unconditionally a success — there's no "absent" state, just "already on" which is idempotent and emits the same payload). **Cross-surface schema lock prepared for v0.8.60** — the new `_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS = frozenset({"project_root", "enabled", "flag_path"})` and the `_flag_to_json` helper introduced this ship will be reused by the v0.8.60 `disable --json` slice; one helper, two surfaces, one frozenset to bump if a future field appears on the flag (mirrors the v0.8.44 `_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS` → v0.8.57/v0.8.58 cross-surface pattern that closed the memory-review surface, and the v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56 `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` → `_project_to_json` pattern that closed the daemon-registration surface). **Idempotent re-enable semantic** — `enable_cmd` has no state-machine guard (calling it on an already-enabled project is a no-op-on-state-but-write-on-disk that returns the same payload), so the JSON contract is "always emit the post-mutation state" rather than "emit the diff"; locked by `test_timeline_enable_json_idempotent_re_enable` which double-enables and asserts the second emission is bytewise identical to the first — proves a script can safely re-run `enable --json` without branching on "was it already on", same render-switch-not-semantic-change discipline as v0.8.57's idempotent re-accept lock. **Cross-state flip semantic** — calling `disable` then `enable --json` flips the flag cleanly with a **stable** `flag_path` (same on-disk marker rewritten in place, no fresh file path); locked by `test_timeline_enable_json_overrides_disabled_state` which mirrors v0.8.58's `test_memory_reject_json_overrides_accepted_status` cross-state flip — proves no duplicate file is created on the state transition, just an in-place rewrite of the existing `.context/timeline.enabled` marker. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune / v0.8.56 watch remove / v0.8.57 memory accept / v0.8.58 memory reject: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (this command has no validation failure path — `enable` always succeeds against any path Typer's argument layer accepts; the flag-write is a pure on-disk side effect with no failure mode beyond a filesystem error, which surfaces as exit 1 + stderr message in both modes). CLI-only change — no library code touched (`_write_flag` and `_flag_file` helpers unchanged; the new `_flag_to_json` helper is a thin pure shaper next to them in `apps/cli/commands/timeline_cmd.py`; no new imports). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `timeline: enabled for <root>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.58 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `enabled`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked three-key set (`_TIMELINE_FLAG_JSON_KEYS = {project_root, enabled, flag_path}` frozenset; `enabled is True` round-trip; cross-checked via on-disk `.context/timeline.enabled` content read confirms the file actually contains `on` matching the emitted payload — a regression that emitted `enabled: true` but failed to write the file would fail this cross-check), idempotent re-enable double-call returns bytewise-identical payloads (locks the no-state-machine-guard semantic so a regression that flipped `enable_cmd` into a "must-be-disabled" guard would break this test), disable-then-enable flips the flag cleanly with stable `flag_path` (locks the cross-state flip semantic so a regression that created a fresh file on the flip would break this test by changing the `flag_path`). All 20 tests in `test_timeline_cmd.py` pass (16 pre-existing + 4 new). All 161 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: emit a wrapper object `{enabled: {project_root, flag_path}}` (over-engineered for a 3-field flat payload; the bare flat shape matches the v0.8.57 memory accept and v0.8.58 memory reject precedents for single-result mutations with no ambiguous-null case), include `previous_enabled: bool` in the payload (recoverable via `status --json` before/after diff if needed; out of scope for the per-command payload — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56-v0.8.58 argument against gratuitous metadata), include the raw flag-file content (`"on"` / `"off"` string) alongside the parsed boolean (redundant — the boolean IS the parsed content, and the consumer can `cat $(jq -r .flag_path)` if they want the raw string), require `--force` to re-enable an already-enabled project (would change the documented no-state-machine semantic; same "ship has sailed" argument as v0.8.55-v0.8.58's destructive-flag rejections), ship `disable --json` in the same release (small-increment discipline says ship one thing at a time; the matching disable slice is a separate symmetric mirror in v0.8.60 reusing the same helper and frozenset, parallel to how v0.8.57 accept and v0.8.58 reject shipped as two separate slices closing the memory-review surface), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.58 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `timeline enable`), `timeline disable` / `status` / `reconcile` / `prune` / `backfill` subcommands untouched (the `disable` symmetric mirror is the v0.8.60 ship), `_write_flag` library helper signature unchanged, on-disk side effect (flag-file write) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `_write_flag` already writes, no MCP surface (timeline-flag mutation is an operator-driven write, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing timeline test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.59-timeline-enable-json.md).

**v0.8.58 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx memory reject --json` closes the memory-review operator surface end-to-end alongside v0.8.44 (read via `ctx memory list --json`) and v0.8.57 (accept via `ctx memory accept --json`). The `ctx memory reject` command has been the canonical "flip a proposed memory to rejected so it does not surface in retrieval" surface since the memory-review feature shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `rejected: <id>  <topic>` footer that collapsed both the post-mutation `Memory` shape and the state-transition signal into a single prose line, leaving every memory-review automation (a daily cron auto-rejecting all proposed memories older than 30 days that never got accepted via `for id in $(ctx memory list --status proposed --json | jq -r --arg cutoff "$(date -u -v-30d +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)" '.[] | select(.created_at_iso < $cutoff) | .id'); do ctx memory reject "$id" --json; done | jq -s 'map(.id)'`, a topic-filter cleanup pipeline that auto-rejects memories matching a deny-list regex like `ctx memory list --status proposed --json | jq -r '.[] | select(.topic | test("(?i)debug|temp|wip")) | .id' | xargs -I{} ctx memory reject {} --json | jq -s 'group_by(.topic) | map({topic: .[0].topic, count: length})'`, an IDE "reject" button that needs to confirm the state transition before re-rendering the review queue, an audit-log appender like `ctx memory reject "$id" --json | jq '{when: .created_at_iso, who: .created_by, topic, decision: "rejected"}' >> review_audit.jsonl`) to brittle line-grepping over the `rejected: <id>` footer (which trips on memory topics containing the substring "rejected:" or platform-specific quoting). `reject_memory` from `libs/memory/store.py` already returned the updated `Memory` dataclass since the memory feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx memory reject` that emits a single JSON object with the same seven-field schema as v0.8.44 `memory list --json` rows and v0.8.57 `memory accept --json` (mirrors the `Memory` dataclass minus `body`), with `status` round-tripping as `"rejected"` post-mutation — locks the symmetric mirror of v0.8.57 accept's `"accepted"` round-trip; the same `_memory_to_json` helper introduced in v0.8.44 emits it; cross-surface schema parity now spans **three** surfaces (list rows v0.8.44 read, accept single-object emission v0.8.57, reject single-object emission v0.8.58), so a future `Memory` field addition has **one** helper to bump and the shared `_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset locks the seven-field shape across all three surfaces. **Symmetric mirror of v0.8.57 accept** — implementation is a deliberate near-clone (same try/except shape, same JSON branch pattern, same docstring discipline); the two commands now read as obvious symmetric siblings in `apps/cli/commands/memory_cmd.py`. **Cross-state flip semantic** — `reject_memory` has no state-machine guard (rejecting an already-accepted memory is a no-op-on-state-but-write-on-disk that returns the entry with status flipped to `"rejected"`), locked by `test_memory_reject_json_overrides_accepted_status` which accepts a proposed memory then rejects the now-accepted memory then asserts both emissions share the same `path` (no fresh on-disk write — proves the cross-state flip mutates the existing file rather than creating a duplicate); mirrors v0.8.57's idempotent re-accept lock but cross-state instead of idempotent. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune / v0.8.56 watch remove / v0.8.57 memory accept: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (unknown memory id → exit 2 with `error: <msg>` on stderr, **no** JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.57 discipline). **Closes the memory-review operator surface** — read side via `memory list --json` (v0.8.44) bare-array of all entries with `--status` filter compose, accept side via `memory accept --json` (v0.8.57) single-object accepted entry, reject side via `memory reject --json` (this ship) single-object rejected entry. Together they let a script enumerate the review queue, accept the keepers, reject the noise, and verify the final state — all with `jq` and exit codes, no markdown parsing — the same triplet pattern as the timeline operator surface closed in v0.8.55 (status / reconcile / prune), the obsidian operator surface closed in v0.8.53 (status / sync), and the daemon-registration operator surface closed in v0.8.56 (list / add / remove). CLI-only change — no library code touched (`reject_memory` signature unchanged; `_memory_to_json` helper reused from v0.8.44; no new helpers, no new imports, no new test fixtures). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `rejected: <id>  <topic>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.57 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `rejected:`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked seven-key set (`_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS = {id, status, topic, tags, created_at_iso, created_by, path}` frozenset; `status == "rejected"` round-trip; cross-checked via `list --status rejected --json` follow-up read confirms the on-disk mutation matches the emitted payload — a regression that emitted "rejected" but failed to mutate the file would fail this follow-up read), unknown memory id → exit 2 with no JSON success-shape payload on stdout (locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the validation error into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload breaks this test), accept-then-reject cross-state flip succeeds with stable `path` (locks the no-state-machine-guard semantic so a regression that gated `reject_memory` behind "must-be-proposed" would break this test by raising `MemoryNotFoundError`-style or exiting non-zero on the reject — and proves the on-disk file is the same one across the cross-state flip, not a fresh write to a new location). All 16 tests in `test_memory_cmd.py` pass (12 pre-existing + 4 new). All 157 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: emit a wrapper object `{rejected: <entry>}` (no-op-on-absent case is exception-shaped here, not success-with-null; the bare entry shape matches the v0.8.54 watch add and v0.8.57 memory accept precedents for exception-on-absent mutations), include `previous_status` in the payload (recoverable via `list --json` before/after diff if needed; out of scope for the per-command payload — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56/v0.8.57 argument against gratuitous metadata), include a `decision_reason` field for richer audit (out of scope — the library `reject_memory` signature doesn't accept a reason; would require a multi-file change to plumb it through, separate ship if ever needed), require an explicit `--force` to reject an already-rejected memory (would change the documented `reject_memory` no-state-machine semantic; same "ship has sailed" argument as v0.8.55's `--yes` rejection), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.57 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `memory reject`), `memory list` / `memory accept` subcommands untouched (already done in v0.8.44 and v0.8.57), `libs/memory/store.py::reject_memory` library signature unchanged, on-disk side effect (status field rewrite in the markdown frontmatter) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `reject_memory` already mutates, no MCP surface (memory mutation is an operator-driven write, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing memory test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.58-memory-reject-json.md).

**v0.8.57 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx memory accept --json` for scriptable memory-review mutations (the accept side of the memory-review operator surface; v0.8.58 will close the surface end-to-end with the symmetric `ctx memory reject --json`). The `ctx memory accept` command has been the canonical "flip a proposed memory to accepted so it surfaces in retrieval" surface since the memory-review feature shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `accepted: <id>  <topic>` footer that collapsed both the post-mutation `Memory` shape and the state-transition signal into a single prose line, leaving every memory-review automation (a daily cron accepting all proposed memories matching a topic regex like `for id in $(ctx memory list --status proposed --json | jq -r '.[] | select(.topic | test("auth")) | .id'); do ctx memory accept "$id" --json; done | jq -s 'map(.id)'`, an IDE integration that flips a memory's status from a UI button click and renders the post-mutation state from the JSON payload directly without a follow-up `list --json` round-trip, an audit-log appender like `ctx memory accept "$id" --json | jq '{when: .created_at_iso, who: .created_by, topic, path}' >> accept_audit.jsonl`, batch-acceptance scripts walking a list of memory ids and aggregating the resulting topics for a per-week digest) to brittle line-grepping over the `accepted: <id>` footer (which trips on memory topics containing the substring "accepted:" or platform-specific quoting). `accept_memory` from `libs/memory/store.py` already returned the updated `Memory` dataclass since the memory feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx memory accept` that emits a single JSON object with seven fields mirroring the v0.8.44 `memory list --json` per-row schema 1:1: `{id (the canonical memory id like `mem_abc123` — round-trips so the consumer can confirm exactly which entry was just mutated), status ("accepted" post-mutation — the canonical state-transition signal; `jq -e '.status == "accepted"'` is the natural CI guard for "the accept actually landed"), topic (the human-readable summary the memory was proposed under — round-trips for audit-log enrichment), tags (JSON array of tags — empty list if none, never null; matches v0.8.44 list-row serializer behaviour for downstream consumers), created_at_iso (ISO timestamp of the original proposal — preserved across the accept, not overwritten by the mutation timestamp; the consumer can compute `now - created_at_iso` to surface "how long was this in review"), created_by (the proposing identity — typically `claude-opus` or a similar agent label; round-trips for provenance audit), path (the absolute on-disk markdown path — the canonical recovery handle for the intentionally-omitted `body` field via `cat $(jq -r .path)`)}`. **`body` intentionally omitted** — same v0.8.44 precedent: arbitrary-size markdown is recoverable via `cat $(jq -r .path)`; keeping the payload lean lets memory-review pipelines stay cheap on projects with hundreds of memories. **Single object, not a wrapper** — `memory accept` is a single-result mutation that returns the updated entity directly; no `{accepted: {...}}` envelope (the `status` field IS the success signal, no need for a top-level discriminator parallel to v0.8.56 watch remove's `{removed: <entry|null>}` because the no-op-on-absent case here is an exception path, not a success-with-null case — the unknown-id case raises `MemoryNotFoundError` and exits 2 with `error: <msg>` on stderr, the same exit-code gate the text mode uses). Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune / v0.8.56 watch remove: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (unknown memory id → exit 2 with `error: <msg>` on stderr, **no** JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.56 discipline). **Cross-surface schema parity** — the inner entry shape is locked by the existing `_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset (introduced v0.8.44) which now spans **two** surfaces (list rows + accept single-object emission); a future `Memory` field addition has **one** helper (`_memory_to_json`) to bump and **one** test frozenset to update, same pattern as v0.8.54 watch add reusing v0.8.49 watch list helper and v0.8.56 watch remove reusing both. **Helper reused, no new code** — `_memory_to_json` (introduced v0.8.44 for `memory list --json`) emits the single-object payload directly; no new helpers, no new imports, no library code touched. **Idempotent re-accept** — `accept_memory` has no state-machine guard (accepting an already-accepted memory is a no-op write that returns the same entry), so the JSON contract is "always emit the post-mutation state" rather than "emit the diff"; locked by `test_memory_accept_json_idempotent_re_accept_returns_accepted_entry` which double-accepts and asserts the second emission matches the first (same `path` across the idempotent re-write — proves no fresh on-disk file got created). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `accepted: <id>  <topic>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.56 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `accepted:`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked seven-key set (`_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS = {id, status, topic, tags, created_at_iso, created_by, path}` frozenset; `status == "accepted"` round-trip; cross-checked via `list --json` follow-up read confirms the on-disk mutation matches the emitted payload — a regression that emitted "accepted" but failed to mutate the file would fail this follow-up read), unknown memory id → exit 2 with no JSON success-shape payload on stdout (locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the validation error into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload breaks this test), idempotent re-accept (double-accept) round-trips the same entry with stable `path` (locks the no-state-machine-guard semantic so a regression that flipped `accept_memory` into a "must-be-proposed" guard would break this test by raising `MemoryNotFoundError`-style or exiting non-zero on the second accept). All 12 tests in `test_memory_cmd.py` pass (8 pre-existing + 4 new). All 153 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: emit a wrapper object `{accepted: <entry>}` (no-op-on-absent case is exception-shaped here, not success-with-null — unlike watch remove where the path-not-registered case is a no-op success; the bare entry shape matches the v0.8.54 watch add precedent for exception-on-absent mutations), include `previous_status` in the payload (recoverable via `list --json` before/after diff if needed; out of scope for the per-command payload — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54/v0.8.56 argument against gratuitous metadata), include `body` in the accept payload (would explode payload size on memories with long markdown bodies — recoverable via `cat $(jq -r .path)` if a script actually needs it, same v0.8.44 list-row precedent), require an explicit `--force` to re-accept an already-accepted memory (would change the documented `accept_memory` no-state-machine semantic; same "ship has sailed" argument as v0.8.55's `--yes` rejection and v0.8.56's `--force` rejection), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.56 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `memory accept`), `memory list` / `memory reject` subcommands untouched (the latter is the v0.8.58 ship's surface — symmetric mirror, will share the same helper and frozenset), `libs/memory/store.py::accept_memory` library signature unchanged, on-disk side effect (status field rewrite in the markdown frontmatter) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `accept_memory` already mutates, no MCP surface (memory mutation is an operator-driven write, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing memory test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.57-memory-accept-json.md).

**v0.8.56 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx watch remove --json` for scriptable daemon unregistration (closes the daemon-registration operator surface alongside v0.8.49 `ctx watch list --json` for reads and v0.8.54 `ctx watch add --json` for writes). The `ctx watch remove` command has been the canonical "unregister a project from the daemon's watch list" surface since spec-006 shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `removed <path>` footer that printed unchanged whether the entry actually existed or had already been pruned, leaving every teardown script (CI hook unregistering a worktree on PR-close, fleet-rebalancing tool moving a project between hosts, operator's "decommission project X" cron job, bulk-cleanup tools iterating over `decommission_list.txt`) without a machine-readable signal for "the path was already absent" — `removed <path>` printed identically for both the actual-deletion case and the no-op-on-absent case, so audit logs got false positives counting "decommissioned" entries that were already gone. `remove_project` from `apps/agent/config.py` already implemented the silent-filter-by-inequality semantic (registered → list shrinks; unregistered → list unchanged) since the daemon shipped — we just weren't surfacing the "did this remove do work" distinction from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx watch remove` that emits a single JSON object with one top-level key: `{removed: <ProjectEntry|null>}` where the inner value is either a `ProjectEntry`-shape dict (path was registered — captured **before** `remove_project` mutates the config so the consumer sees what was just deleted, not a vanished read-after-write `null`) or `null` (path was not registered — no-op success, same v0.8.45/v0.8.49/v0.8.55 "no work done is still a successful run, surface the null/zero rather than erroring out" discipline; `jq -e '.removed != null'` is the natural CI guard for "the unregistration actually freed a slot", parallel to v0.8.55 prune's `jq -e '.deleted > 0'`). The inner entry mirrors the v0.8.49 `watch list --json` row schema 1:1 (`root` stringified, `registered_at_iso`, `last_scan_at_iso`, `last_scan_status`) — the same `_project_to_json` helper introduced in v0.8.54 emits it; cross-surface schema parity now spans `list` (v0.8.49 read), `add` (v0.8.54 single-result write), and `remove` (v0.8.56 single-result mutation), so a future `ProjectEntry` field addition has **one** helper to bump and the shared `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset locks the four-field shape across all three surfaces. **Wrapper object, not bare entry** — a bare `ProjectEntry` would be ambiguous with `null` semantics (an empty `{}` and a `null` would both signal "no entry", confusing consumers); the `{removed: <entry|null>}` wrapper makes the no-op case unambiguous and lets future fields (e.g. a `reason` for richer audit) extend the wrapper without disturbing the inner entry shape. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add / v0.8.55 timeline prune: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (unregistered path → exit 0 with `{"removed": null}` — never a non-zero exit for the "no work to do" case; resolved-path resolution failure → propagated through Typer's `resolve_path=True` argument handling, non-zero exit, no JSON success-shape payload on stdout — same v0.8.42-v0.8.55 discipline). **Capture-then-mutate ordering matters** — the entry is read **before** `remove_project` rewrites the config, after which the entry is gone; read-after-write would always emit `removed: null` and lose the audit signal (locked by `test_watch_remove_json_emits_removed_entry`'s assertion that the captured `root` ends with the project name AND the post-command `load_config` shows the entry has vanished — both invariants in one test, so a refactor that swapped the order would fail at least one of them). **Closes the daemon-registration operator surface** — read side via `watch list --json` (v0.8.49) bare-array of all registered projects, add side via `watch add --json` (v0.8.54) single-object idempotent registration, remove side via `watch remove --json` (this ship) wrapper-object capturing the removed entry. Together they let a script manage the daemon's project registry end-to-end with `jq` and exit codes, no markdown parsing — the same triplet pattern as the timeline operator surface closed in v0.8.55 (status / reconcile / prune) and the obsidian operator surface closed in v0.8.53 (status / sync). CLI-only change — no library code touched (`remove_project` signature unchanged; the `_project_to_json` helper and `list_projects` import were already in scope, used by `add` and `list`; no new helpers, no new imports). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `removed <path>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.55 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `removed`), JSON mode emits a single wrapper object with the schema-locked one-top-level-key set (`_WATCH_REMOVE_JSON_KEYS = frozenset({"removed"})`) whose inner value matches the v0.8.49 `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset (cross-surface lock spans three surfaces now: `list` v0.8.49, `add` v0.8.54, `remove` v0.8.56), unregistered path → exit 0 with `{"removed": null}` (no-op success — locks the discipline so a regression that exits 1 on already-absent paths breaks this test), multi-project registry isolation locked via `test_watch_remove_json_isolated_when_other_projects_present` which removes one of two registered projects then asserts (a) only the targeted entry surfaces in the payload, (b) the other entry survives in the config (no fan-out, no collateral damage — same scope-discipline guard as v0.8.55 prune's deleted-count assertion). All 14 tests in `test_watch_cmd.py` pass (10 pre-existing + 4 new). All 149 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: emit a bare `ProjectEntry` and use `null` directly for the no-op case (ambiguous with empty-object semantics; the wrapper disambiguates and is future-extensible), require `--force` to no-op on absent paths (would change the documented `remove_project` semantic that already silently no-ops; same "ship has sailed" argument as v0.8.55's `--yes` rejection), exit 1 when removing an absent path (would conflate "no work to do" with "validation failure" — same v0.8.45/v0.8.49/v0.8.50/v0.8.55 discipline of "no work done is still a successful run, surface the null rather than erroring out"), include a `was_registered: bool` field alongside `removed` (redundant with `removed != null` — derivable in one `jq` expression; keeping the schema tight at one top-level key matches v0.8.55's restraint), echo the resolved config-file path as a sibling field (recoverable from `ctx config show` if needed; out of scope for the per-command payload — same v0.8.49/v0.8.54 argument against gratuitous metadata in the per-row payload), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.55 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence), capture-after-mutate (would always emit `removed: null` and lose the audit signal — explicitly locked by the test). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `watch remove`), `watch add` / `list` / `start` / `install-service` / `uninstall-service` subcommands untouched (the latter three are operator-driven daemon-lifecycle ops, not retrieval-surface scriptability targets), `apps/agent/config.py::remove_project` library signature unchanged, hard-mutation side effect (config-file rewrite) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `remove_project` already mutates, no MCP surface (daemon registration is an operator-driven mutation, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing watch test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.56-watch-remove-json.md).

**v0.8.55 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx timeline prune --json` for scriptable timeline maintenance (closes the timeline operator surface alongside pre-existing `ctx timeline status --json` and v0.8.45 `ctx timeline reconcile --json`). The `ctx timeline prune` command has been the canonical "permanently delete old events from the timeline DB" surface since spec-010 shipped — but stayed text-only with a single-line `prune: deleted N events (orphaned only|orphaned + live, older than Nd)` footer that collapsed both the deletion count and the round-tripped flags (`older_than_days`, `include_live`) into a single prose line, leaving every timeline-maintenance script (nightly retention cron `for proj in $(ctx watch list --json | jq -r '.[].root'); do ctx timeline prune --project "$proj" --older-than 90 --json; done | jq -s 'map({project: .project_root, freed: .deleted}) | sort_by(-.freed)'` surfacing top-N projects by deletion volume, fleet retention-policy enforcement folding per-project deletion counts into a hygiene dashboard, post-reconcile cleanup hook gating on "did this prune actually remove the orphans we just flagged" via `ctx timeline reconcile --project P --json | jq -e '.orphaned_newly_flagged > 0' && ctx timeline prune --project P --older-than 30 --json | jq -e '.deleted > 0'`, operational dashboards charting per-project rolling `deleted` counts to spot timeline-DB growth anomalies) to brittle line-grepping over the `deleted N events` footer (which trips on project paths containing the substring "events" or platform-specific quoting). `prune_events` from `libs/symbol_timeline/reconcile.py` already returned the raw deletion count as an `int` since the timeline feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx timeline prune` that emits a single JSON object with five fields: `{project_root (resolved absolute path of the project root that was pruned — round-tripped so a script can confirm the run actually targeted the project root it intended; same v0.8.48/v0.8.50/v0.8.52/v0.8.53/v0.8.54 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), store_path (resolved absolute path of the timeline DB that was mutated — `LVDCP_TIMELINE_DB` env var, `--store` override, or platform default; round-tripping it means a script can verify "this prune actually targeted the DB I think it did" without re-deriving the resolution rules), older_than_days (the cutoff in days that was actually used — round-tripped so a future change to the default `90` would surface in the JSON output rather than silently changing cron behavior), include_live (the destructive-vs-routine flag — round-tripped so audit logs can distinguish "routine prune of orphaned tombstones" from "hard purge of live history"; `jq -e '.include_live == false'` is the natural CI gate for "this was a safe routine prune"), deleted (the canonical "did this prune do work" signal — `jq -e '.deleted > 0'` is the natural CI guard for "the prune actually removed events"; locked by both `test_prune_json_emits_well_formed_object` for the orphaned-only default mode and `test_prune_json_include_live_round_trips_flag_and_count` for the destructive `--include-live` mode that catches all four seeded events including the three live ones)}`. **Single object, not a bare array** — `timeline prune` is a single-result terminal mutation with one deletion count plus the round-tripped invocation parameters; same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command), v0.8.50 `obsidian status` (tri-state vault contract), v0.8.51 `pack --json` (single-result retrieval call), v0.8.52 `eval --json` (single-result measurement call with aggregate `summary` + per-query `query_results`), v0.8.53 `obsidian sync --json` (single-result mutation call), and v0.8.54 `watch add --json` (single-result registration call). Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no top-level metadata. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync / v0.8.54 watch add: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (`--older-than 0` → exit 2 with `prune: --older-than must be positive` on stderr, **no** JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.54 discipline). **Inline dict, not a helper** — unlike v0.8.45 reconcile (which has a `ReconcileReport` dataclass mirrored 1:1 by a `_reconcile_report_to_json` helper), `prune_events` returns a bare `int`, so the JSON dict is built inline at the command site in `apps/cli/commands/timeline_cmd.py::prune_cmd` next to the existing text-mode emission — same inline-dict pattern as v0.8.38 `registry prune --json`. Schema-as-source-of-truth lives at the command site, not in a separate library helper. **Closes the timeline operator surface** — read side via pre-existing `timeline status --json` (tri-state event-counts contract), reconciliation side via `timeline reconcile --json` (v0.8.45) flagging orphans, write side via `timeline prune --json` (this ship) freeing DB space. Together they let a script manage timeline DBs end-to-end with `jq` and exit codes, no markdown parsing. CLI-only change — no library code touched (`prune_events` signature unchanged; `_TIMELINE_PRUNE_JSON_KEYS` schema lock lives in the test file alongside the existing `_RECONCILE_JSON_KEYS` frozenset). The `store.db_path` read happens inside the `try` block before `store.close()` in the `finally` — capturing inside the with-resource discipline so a future refactor that invalidates the attribute on close doesn't silently break the JSON shape. Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `prune: deleted N events (orphaned only|orphaned + live, older than Nd)` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.54 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `deleted`), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked five-key set (`_TIMELINE_PRUNE_JSON_KEYS = {project_root, store_path, older_than_days, include_live, deleted}` frozenset; `project_root` and `store_path` round-trip exactly; `older_than_days == 1`, `include_live is False`, `deleted == 1` for the orphaned-only default mode against the 4-event seed), `--include-live --json` round-trips the flag as `True` in the payload (locks the schema-as-source-of-truth contract — a regression that drops the flag from the payload would silently lose the "this prune included live events" signal that drives the destructive-vs-routine distinction in audit logs) and reports the full deletion count of 4 events not just the 1 orphaned (cross-checks the v0.8.55 schema against the existing `test_prune_include_live_removes_everything` text-mode invariant), `--older-than 0` exits 2 in JSON mode with `must be positive` on stderr and stdout that does NOT parse as a success-shape `prune` payload (no `"deleted"` key — locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the validation error into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload breaks this test). All 16 tests in `test_timeline_cmd.py` pass (12 pre-existing + 4 new). All 145 tests in `tests/unit/cli/` pass (no regressions). Rejected alternatives: derive `scope` ("orphaned only" / "orphaned + live") as a separate field instead of round-tripping the `include_live` boolean (`scope` is a derived render-time string for human consumption — keeping the raw flag matches the v0.8.48/v0.8.50/v0.8.52-v0.8.54 "round-trip raw inputs, derived strings are recoverable" precedent; consumers wanting the prose form can `jq -r 'if .include_live then "orphaned + live" else "orphaned only" end'`), include `cutoff_ts` (the resolved POSIX timestamp the older_than_days math produced) in the payload (recoverable as `now - older_than_days * 86400` with one `jq` expression; keeping the schema tight at 5 fields matches v0.8.49/v0.8.54's restraint), wrap in `{"prune": {...}, "summary": {...}}` (over-engineered nesting for a flat 5-field payload; same v0.8.45 / v0.8.49 / v0.8.50 / v0.8.51 argument against gratuitous envelopes — `deleted` IS the summary), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.54 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence), echo the resolved `LVDCP_TIMELINE_DB` env var separately from `store_path` (redundant with `store_path` which is the resolved value the command actually used; env-var introspection is `ctx config show`'s job, not `prune`'s), include per-event-type deletion breakdown like reconcile's `orphaned_by_event_type` (would require library changes to `prune_events` to surface per-type counts — out of scope for a CLI-only ship; the aggregate `deleted` count is the natural CI signal, and consumers wanting per-type breakdowns can call `timeline status --json` before and after to compute the diff), require explicit `--yes` to mutate (would change the documented v0.8.x destructive semantic of `timeline prune` — that ship has already sailed in spec-010; adding `--yes` here would be a separate breaking-UX change, orthogonal to scriptability), make the JSON output exit 1 when `deleted == 0` (would conflate "no work to do" with "validation failure" — same v0.8.45/v0.8.49/v0.8.50 discipline of "no work done is still a successful run, surface the zero count not an error"). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `timeline prune`), `timeline enable` / `disable` / `status` / `reconcile` / `backfill` subcommands untouched, `libs/symbol_timeline/reconcile.py::prune_events` library signature unchanged, hard-delete side effect (DB row removal) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `prune_events` already mutates, no MCP surface (timeline maintenance is an operator-driven mutation, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing timeline test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.55-timeline-prune-json.md).

**v0.8.54 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx watch add --json` for scriptable daemon registration (closes the watch operator surface alongside v0.8.49 `watch list --json`). The `ctx watch add` command has been the canonical "register a project with the auto-indexing daemon" surface since the watch feature shipped, and v0.8.49 closed the read side with `ctx watch list --json` returning a bare array of per-project `ProjectEntry` rows — but the write side stayed text-only with a single-line `added <path>` footer that collapses two semantically distinct outcomes into the same string (fresh registration vs. idempotent re-add of an already-watched path), leaving every fleet provisioning script (`for d in projects/*; do ctx watch add "$d" --json | jq -r '.root'; done` to capture exactly what the daemon will watch normalized to absolute paths), idempotent-reprovisioning workflow (a script that re-runs `add --json` on every boot can detect "this was already registered" via `registered_at_iso` against `now - boot_time` without an extra `list --json` round-trip), and `ctx scan` follow-on automation (CI hook running `ctx scan && ctx watch add --json | jq -e '.last_scan_status == "pending"'` to confirm the daemon will pick up the next scheduled scan) to brittle line-grepping over the `added X` footer. `ProjectEntry` from `apps/agent/config.py` already returned a clean 4-field dataclass (`root` / `registered_at_iso` / `last_scan_at_iso` / `last_scan_status`) since the watch feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the write side. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx watch add` that emits a single JSON object mirroring `ProjectEntry` 1:1 — the **same** schema as one row of `ctx watch list --json`: `{root (absolute path of the project root that was just registered — Typer's `resolve_path=True` argument gate normalizes symlinks, `..`, and relative paths so the consumer sees what the daemon will actually watch, not what was typed; same v0.8.48/v0.8.50/v0.8.52/v0.8.53 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), registered_at_iso (ISO 8601 timestamp string of when this project was first registered — the duplicate-add detector; a consumer comparing against wall-clock can distinguish "first registration" from "already-watched, no-op" without an extra `list --json` call; on idempotent re-add the original timestamp is preserved, **not** refreshed), last_scan_at_iso (always `null` on fresh registration since the daemon hasn't scanned yet — explicit `null` not absent key, so `jq -e '.last_scan_at_iso == null'` works unconditionally), last_scan_status ("pending" on fresh registration; flips to "ok" / "error" once the daemon runs — lets a script gate "is this project ready to query" without inspecting timestamps)}`. **Cross-surface schema reuse, not duplication** — the v0.8.49 `_project_to_json` helper renders both surfaces (`watch list --json` rows AND `watch add --json` results), so no shape drift between read and write paths is possible by construction; the test invariant reuses the v0.8.49 `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset on **both** emissions so a future `ProjectEntry` field addition requires bumping ONE frozenset and the test catches divergence on both surfaces simultaneously. **Idempotent re-add semantic preserved in JSON** — `add_project` is silently idempotent (skips duplicates via `if any(p.root == root_resolved for p in cfg.projects): return`), and the JSON contract preserves this: first add returns the freshly-written entry with the just-now `registered_at_iso`, second add of the same path returns the **same** entry with the **original** `registered_at_iso` (not a fresh timestamp). Stronger contract than text mode (which emits an indistinguishable `added X` line either way). Locked by `test_watch_add_json_idempotent_returns_existing_entry`. **`allow_transient=True` preserved unchanged** — per v0.8.35 (existing behavior): `ctx watch add` is an explicit user intent so the CLI passes `allow_transient=True` to `add_project` (the daemon will follow ship-ceremony worktrees and the `sample_repo` fixture if the user explicitly asks); only implicit auto-registration from `ctx scan` on an unregistered path filters transient roots; explicit invocation wins; no path filtering changes between text and JSON modes. **Single object, not a bare array** — `watch add` registers a single project per invocation with one `ProjectEntry` payload; same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command), v0.8.50 `obsidian status` (tri-state vault contract), v0.8.51 `pack --json` (single-result retrieval call), v0.8.52 `eval --json` (single-result measurement call), and v0.8.53 `obsidian sync --json` (single-result mutation call). Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no top-level metadata. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval / v0.8.53 obsidian sync: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (path-not-found → exit 2 via Typer's `exists=True` argument-validation gate, **no** JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; defensive `next(...)` lookup guards against the vanishingly rare case of read-back failure with exit 1 + stderr message, ensuring the JSON contract never emits a malformed payload; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.53 discipline). **Closes the watch operator surface** — read side via `watch list --json` (v0.8.49) tells you what the daemon is currently watching; write side via `watch add --json` (this ship) tells you whether the just-issued `add` was a fresh registration or a no-op duplicate. Together they let a script manage daemon registrations end-to-end with `jq` and exit codes, no text parsing. CLI-only change — no library code touched (`ProjectEntry`, `add_project`, `list_projects` all unchanged; `as_json` parameter and the readback branch live next to the existing `add` Typer command in `apps/cli/commands/watch_cmd.py`, reusing the v0.8.49 `_project_to_json` helper as the single source of truth for the JSON shape on both surfaces). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy single-line `added <path>` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.53 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that greps for `added`), JSON mode emits a single object with the reused `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` schema lock and the locked fresh-registration field invariants (root suffix matches input project name, `registered_at_iso` non-empty ISO string, `last_scan_at_iso is None`, `last_scan_status == "pending"`), JSON mode preserves the documented "consumer can compare `registered_at_iso` against wall-clock to detect duplicate-add" contract via the idempotent-re-add round-trip (second `add --json` of the same path returns the SAME entry with the SAME `registered_at_iso` — a regression that silently re-creates the entry on duplicate-add overwriting the original timestamp breaks this test), nonexistent-path error path exits non-zero in JSON mode with stdout that does NOT parse as a success-shape `ProjectEntry` JSON object (locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the path-not-found error into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload breaks this test). All 10 tests in `test_watch_cmd.py` pass (6 pre-existing + 4 new). Full CLI suite 141 tests pass (no regressions).
