Rejected alternatives: ship `ctx watch remove --json` in the same release (destructive command, different shape decision — return removed entry vs. `{root, removed: bool}`; small-increment discipline says ship one thing at a time; the read-side and additive-write-side surface is sufficient for the v0.8.x scriptability rollout), define a separate `_WATCH_ADD_JSON_KEYS` frozenset for the write-side test (would invite shape drift between read and write paths — the whole point of cross-surface schema reuse is that the test catches divergence on BOTH surfaces simultaneously when `ProjectEntry` gains a field), distinguish "fresh" from "duplicate" registration with a top-level `created: bool` field (over-engineered envelope for a 4-field payload — the consumer can derive freshness from `registered_at_iso` against wall-clock with one `jq` expression; adding a `created` field would also force the read side `watch list --json` to grow an analogous field for symmetry, breaking the cross-surface schema reuse), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.53 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence), echo the full `watch_config` block in the payload (config introspection is `ctx config show`'s job, not `watch add`'s; would couple `add`'s payload shape to every new config knob), include `daemon_pid: int` to surface "this is the PID that will pick up the registration" (the daemon's PID is mutable across `ctx watch start` cycles; the per-registration payload should not encode runtime state that's invalidated on the next daemon restart), make the JSON output exit non-zero on idempotent re-add to distinguish from fresh registration (would change the documented idempotent semantic of `add_project` and break shell pipelines that rely on exit 0 for "registration is in place"; the `registered_at_iso` round-trip is the right signal). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `watch add`), `watch list` / `watch remove` / `watch start` / `watch install-service` / `watch uninstall-service` subcommands untouched, `apps/agent/config.py::ProjectEntry` / `add_project` / `list_projects` library signatures unchanged, registration side effect (config write) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `add_project` already writes, no MCP surface (watch registration is an operator-driven mutation, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing watch test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.54-watch-add-json.md).

**v0.8.53 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx obsidian sync --json` for scriptable vault writes (closes the Obsidian operator surface alongside v0.8.50 `obsidian status --json`). The `ctx obsidian sync` command has been the canonical "publish a scanned project's structure into an Obsidian vault" surface since the obsidian feature shipped — but stayed text-only with a three-line human footer (`Synced X to Y` / `Pages written: N` / `Duration: T.TTs`), leaving every operational use case (nightly cron with structured logging via `for p in ~/code/*/; do ctx obsidian sync --vault $V "$p" --json; done | jq -s '.[] | select(.errors != [])'`, post-scan automation hook gating CI on "scan results actually propagated to the vault" via `ctx scan && ctx obsidian sync --vault $V . --json | jq -e '.pages_written > 0'`, per-project rolling page-count and duration dashboards, multi-project hygiene sweep folding per-project `errors` arrays into a single anomaly inventory) to brittle prose-grepping over the three-line footer (which trips on vault paths containing the substring `Pages` or vault names with embedded duration-like strings). `SyncReport` from `libs/obsidian/models.py` already returned a clean 5-field dataclass (`project_name` / `pages_written` / `pages_deleted` / `duration_seconds` / `errors`) since the obsidian feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx obsidian sync` that emits a single JSON object mirroring `SyncReport` 1:1 plus the invocation-parameter round-trip fields: `{vault (absolute path of the Obsidian vault root that was targeted — round-tripped so a script can confirm the run actually targeted the vault it intended without reconstructing it from `--vault`; same v0.8.48 / v0.8.50 / v0.8.52 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), project (absolute path of the project root that was synced — round-tripped for the same reason; a nightly script that fans out across N projects can confirm per-result which project produced each row), project_name (the basename used as the vault subdirectory — same string the text view echoes in "Synced X to Y" and the same string the publisher used internally to write `vault/Projects/<project_name>/`; mirroring it separately lets a consumer locate the written subdirectory without re-deriving the basename), pages_written (count of vault pages newly written or rewritten — the canonical "did this sync actually do work" signal; `jq -e '.pages_written > 0'` is the natural CI guard), pages_deleted (count of vault pages removed because the source files no longer exist — separate from `pages_written` so dashboards can split "drift cleanup" from "fresh write" load; will surface meaningfully once incremental drift detection lands; currently always `0` for full-resync semantics), duration_seconds (float seconds the publisher ran for — useful for the "did this sync slow down" hygiene track via `jq '.duration_seconds'`; float so 1.83s isn't silently truncated to 1s), errors (array of human-readable error messages collected during sync — empty array (never `null`) for a clean sync; `jq -e '.errors == []'` works as the CI gate without a None-guard; `len(errors) > 0` does **not** flip the exit code: the publisher swallows per-page errors into the report rather than crashing, and the JSON contract preserves that semantic so consumers see the partial-success case as `exit 0` + non-empty errors array, mirroring v0.8.50 `obsidian status` "missing Projects/ is exit 0 + structured signal" discipline)}`. **Single object, not a bare array** — `obsidian sync` is a single-result terminal mutation with one `SyncReport` payload; same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command), v0.8.50 `obsidian status` (tri-state vault contract), v0.8.51 `pack --json` (single-result retrieval call), and v0.8.52 `eval --json` (single-result measurement call with aggregate `summary` + per-query `query_results`). Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no top-level metadata. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack / v0.8.52 eval: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error-vs-success boundary stays at the exit-code gate (`cache.db` missing → exit 1, `error: no cache.db found at ...` on stderr, **no** JSON payload on stdout — the `--json` flag is a render switch, not a semantic change; never `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.52 discipline). **Closes the Obsidian operator surface** — read side via `obsidian status --json` (v0.8.50) tells you which projects exist in the vault; write side via `obsidian sync --json` (this ship) tells you whether the last sync did meaningful work. Together they let a script manage an Obsidian vault end-to-end with `jq` and exit codes, no markdown parsing. CLI-only change — no library code touched (`SyncReport`, `ObsidianPublisher`, `sync_project` all unchanged; `_sync_report_to_json` lives next to the `sync` Typer command in `apps/cli/commands/obsidian_cmd.py`, sister-helper to v0.8.46-v0.8.52 CLI-shell payload shapers). The helper reads `SyncReport` fields via `getattr(report, "field", default)` rather than importing the dataclass and accessing attributes directly, so the helper's sole input contract is "object with the documented fields" — survives a future `SyncReport` move or rename without import-graph churn (same shape discipline as v0.8.45 `ReconcileReport` shaping). `obsidian sync-all` subcommand **untouched** — the multi-project fan-out has its own per-project rollup and exit-code aggregation that benefits from a separate ship with the streaming-vs-terminal `--json` question (NDJSON one event per project vs. single terminal summary with per-project array). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy three-line `Synced X to Y` / `Pages written: N` / `Duration: T.TTs` footer byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.52 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked seven-key set (`_SYNC_JSON_KEYS = {vault, project, project_name, pages_written, pages_deleted, duration_seconds, errors}` frozenset; `vault` / `project` / `project_name` round-trip exactly; scalar field types locked; `errors == []` for a clean sync), JSON mode reports `pages_written > 0` for a first-time sync and cross-checks the count against an actual `vault/Projects/<project_name>/` directory on disk (locks the canonical "did this sync actually do work" signal so a regression that short-circuits the publisher into a no-op breaks this test), `cache.db` missing exits 1 in JSON mode with `cache.db` mentioned in stderr and stdout that does NOT parse as a success-shape JSON object (locks the error-vs-success boundary so a refactor that swallows the hard-error case into a "fake clean" payload breaks this test). All 28 obsidian CLI tests pass (24 pre-existing + 4 new). Rejected alternatives: include a `pages_changed` array of per-page diffs (would require library changes to `ObsidianPublisher` to surface per-page deltas; out of scope for a CLI-only ship; consumers wanting per-page detail can `find $vault/Projects/$project_name -newer ...`), include the absolute path each page was written to in the payload (filesystem-recoverable via `find`; pure render-shape ship preserves the `SyncReport` 1:1 mirror), wrap in `{"sync": {...}, "summary": {...}}` (over-engineered nesting for a flat 7-field payload; `pages_written` / `errors` ARE the summary), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.52 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence), echo the full `obsidian` config block in the payload (config introspection is `ctx config show`'s job, not `sync`'s; would couple `sync`'s payload shape to every new config knob), include `vault_path_was_created: bool` to surface "this sync had to mkdir Projects/" (rare event; orthogonal to the SyncReport shape; `obsidian status --json` already surfaces the post-sync state), add `--json` to `obsidian sync-all` in the same release (keep increments small; `sync-all` deserves its own analysis of streaming-vs-terminal `--json` semantics — a 50-project sync-all should probably emit NDJSON one event per project rather than buffer the entire run into a single terminal payload), make the JSON output exit 1 when `errors` is non-empty (would change the documented partial-success semantic of the publisher; the JSON contract preserves "exit 0 + non-empty errors array = partial success" so consumers see the same exit-code gate text mode has always exposed). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `obsidian sync`), `obsidian status` / `obsidian sync-all` subcommands untouched, `libs/obsidian/publisher.py::ObsidianPublisher.sync_project` and `libs/obsidian/models.py::SyncReport` library signatures unchanged, file-write side effect (vault page generation) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what the publisher already writes, no MCP surface (sync is an operator-driven mutation, not retrieval context for LLMs — vault content itself is accessible via the file system), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing obsidian test passes), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.53-obsidian-sync-json.md).

**v0.8.52 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx eval --json` for scriptable retrieval-quality metrics (the measurement surface that closes the v0.8.51 loop). The `ctx eval` command runs the retrieval eval harness against an indexed project — surfacing per-query expected-vs-retrieved diffs, aggregate `recall_at_5_files`, `precision_at_3_files`, `recall_at_5_symbols`, `mrr_files`, and `impact_recall_at_5` metrics that are the canonical "is our retrieval pipeline healthy" signal — but stayed text-only, leaving every retrieval-quality dashboard, regression gate, and trend tracker (CI guard asserting "this PR doesn't drop recall@5 below 0.7" via `jq -e '.summary.recall_at_5_files >= 0.7'`, per-query trend tracker surfacing "which queries regressed this week" via `jq -c '.query_results[] | {q: .query_id, hit: ((.retrieved_files - .expected_files) | length == 0)}'`, cross-project quality sweeps folding per-project `summary.recall_at_5_files` into a fleet retrieval-quality dashboard via `for proj in ~/code/*/; do ctx eval "$proj" --queries "$proj/queries.yaml" --json; done | jq -s 'map({project: .project, recall: .summary.recall_at_5_files})'`, weekly regression report tracking the v0.8.51 `pack --json` pipeline's quality drift) to brittle markdown-table parsing. `EvalReport` and `QueryResult` dataclasses already returned the full structured payload via `libs/eval/runner.py` since the eval harness shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape from the CLI. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx eval` that emits a single JSON object mirroring the `EvalReport` dataclass 1:1 plus the invocation-parameter round-trip fields: `{project (absolute path of the project root that was evaluated — round-tripped so a script can confirm the run actually used the project root it intended), queries_path (absolute path of the navigate queries YAML — same v0.8.48/v0.8.50 "round-trip the actual input to catch typos" precedent), impact_queries_path (absolute path of the impact queries YAML, or `null` when `--impact-queries` was not passed — distinguishes "no impact queries supplied" from "impact queries supplied but yielded zero results"; both would collapse to `impact_recall_at_5=0.0` without this distinguishing field), summary (nested dict of aggregate metrics — `recall_at_5_files`, `precision_at_3_files`, `recall_at_5_symbols`, `mrr_files`, `impact_recall_at_5`; nested rather than flat top-level so `query_results` array sits cleanly alongside without ambiguity about which fields are aggregates vs. invocation parameters; the schema-locked test asserts both `_EVAL_JSON_KEYS` for the top-level and `_EVAL_SUMMARY_KEYS` for the nested aggregate so adding a metric forces a reviewed update to both frozensets), query_results (array of per-query rows, one entry per query in the input YAMLs in input file order — navigate first then impact, lets dashboards correlate per-query rows across runs by index without re-keying on `query_id`; each row is a 1:1 mirror of the `QueryResult` dataclass: `query_id` / `mode` / `retrieved_files` / `retrieved_symbols` / `expected_files` / `expected_symbols` — same key set as the v0.8.51 `pack --json` `retrieved_files` / `retrieved_symbols` lists, lets dashboards bridge eval-vs-production retrieval signals trivially)}`. **The `--baseline` deferred decision** — `--json` is **not yet supported with `--baseline`**; the combination exits 2 with a helpful error message ("error: --json is not yet supported with --baseline. Run without --baseline to get the structured payload, or omit --json for the markdown comparison report.") because the comparison-report mode produces two `EvalReport`s plus diff metrics, which would force either a single object with conditional fields (ugly schema split) or a schema bump in this ship without a real consumer driving the design; same scope discipline as v0.8.42-v0.8.51 ("keep increments small"). When a real consumer needs comparison `--json`, the right factoring is a separate ship that designs the comparison shape against the actual use case (drift detection? regression gate? both?). The test locks the rejection so a refactor that silently accepts the combo breaks the test instead of shipping a half-defined payload. **`--output` composition** — without `--json`, `--output` writes the markdown report to the file (existing behavior, unchanged); with `--json`, `--output` writes the JSON payload to the file. The `wrote: ...` confirmation goes to **stderr** in JSON mode (not stdout) — keeps stdout pure for scripts that want the byte-identical "redirect-then-read" pattern; markdown mode keeps the confirmation on stdout for byte-identical text-mode preservation. **Single object, not a bare array** — `eval` is a single-result measurement call with aggregate metadata (`summary`) plus a per-query sub-array (`query_results`); same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command), v0.8.50 `obsidian status` (tri-state vault), and v0.8.51 `pack --json` (single-result retrieval call). Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no top-level metadata. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status / v0.8.51 pack: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; `structlog` routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error path identical in both modes (un-indexed project → stderr message + exit 2, **never** `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.51 discipline of "exit code is the gate, structured payload is for the success path"). CLI-only change — no library code touched (`EvalReport`, `QueryResult`, `run_eval`, and the report generators all unchanged; `_eval_report_to_json` lives next to `eval_cmd` in `apps/cli/commands/eval_cmd.py`, sister-helper to v0.8.46-v0.8.51 CLI-shell payload shapers). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy markdown `# Eval Report` header byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.51 "text path untouched" promise; a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that pipes `ctx eval` to `pandoc` or another markdown processor), JSON mode emits a single object with the schema-locked top-level key set (`_EVAL_JSON_KEYS = {project, queries_path, impact_queries_path, summary, query_results}` frozenset) AND the nested aggregate-metrics key set (`_EVAL_SUMMARY_KEYS = {recall_at_5_files, precision_at_3_files, recall_at_5_symbols, mrr_files, impact_recall_at_5}` frozenset, all values asserted as floats in `[0, 1]` so a refactor that returns ints or out-of-range values breaks the test) AND the per-row schema (`_EVAL_QUERY_RESULT_KEYS = {query_id, mode, retrieved_files, retrieved_symbols, expected_files, expected_symbols}` frozenset, ordering asserted to match input file order so dashboards can correlate by index across runs), `--json --output` writes the JSON payload to the file (not markdown — schema-locked when read back; the file-write side effect is a render switch, not a behavior switch), `--json --baseline` rejects cleanly with exit 2 and a helpful error message naming both flags (locks the deferred-decision boundary so a refactor that silently accepts the combo breaks the test; stdout asserted to **not** parse as a success-shape JSON object — the gate is exit code 2 plus stderr message, never a half-defined payload). All 9 tests in the file pass (5 pre-existing + 4 new). **This is the natural follow-up to v0.8.51 `ctx pack --json`** — `pack` is the **production retrieval surface**, `eval` is the **measurement surface for that retrieval**. Both now expose structured payloads, and the closed loop "ship a retrieval change → run eval → gate on metric drop" pipeline finally has a clean Unix surface. Rejected alternatives: support `--json` with `--baseline` in the same ship using a comparison shape like `{primary: {...}, baseline: {...}, diff: {...}}` (out of scope for this ship without a real consumer driving the design — when a comparison-`--json` consumer surfaces, the right factoring is a separate ship designing the shape against the actual use case), flatten `summary` to top-level fields (mixes aggregate metrics with invocation parameters in a single namespace — adding a `total_query_count` field would be ambiguous about whether it belongs to the run config or the run results; nested `summary` makes the boundary explicit), include per-query metric breakdowns (`per_query_recall_at_5`) in `query_results` rows (would require library changes to `QueryResult` to expose computed metrics — out of scope for a CLI-only ship; consumers wanting per-query metrics can compute `(retrieved_files & expected_files | length) / (expected_files | length)` from the existing fields), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.51 argument; the schema-locked frozenset tests catch accidental divergence), strip `query_results` from the JSON payload to keep it lightweight (loses the per-query trend-tracking and debugging use cases that motivate this ship; `summary`-only payload is recoverable via `jq 'del(.query_results)'` for the rare consumer that wants only aggregates), echo invocation parameters or eval-pipeline timing (brittle — schema would change with every new eval flag; `project`, `queries_path`, `impact_queries_path` are the round-tripped triplet that makes the run reproducible without echoing the entire invocation), include `eval_run_at_iso` timestamp in the payload (out of scope — `ctx history` is the right surface for run-level metadata; consumers wanting timing can wrap the call in `time ctx eval ... --json`). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `eval`), no library code touched (`libs/eval/runner.py::EvalReport` / `QueryResult` / `run_eval` and `libs/eval/report.py` signatures unchanged; `libs/eval/loader.py` unchanged; `libs/eval/metrics.py` unchanged), no new on-disk artifacts (no extra trace records — `--json` is a pure render switch over the existing run), MCP surface unchanged (eval is a CLI/operator surface, not retrieval context for LLMs — the eval pipeline already runs against the same retrieval that MCP `lvdcp_pack` calls), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing eval test passes; markdown mode preserved; `wrote: ...` confirmation in markdown-mode `--output` stays on stdout for byte-identical text-mode preservation), `structlog` routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.52-eval-json.md).

**v0.8.51 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx pack --json` for scriptable structured pack payload (CLI/MCP parity for the primary retrieval surface). The `ctx pack` command is the **primary retrieval interface** of LV_DCP — every script, dashboard, retrieval-quality benchmark, hash-comparison drift detector, and LLM-on-LLM evaluation harness ultimately calls `ctx pack` to get the ranked context. Until this release, the CLI emitted only the human-readable assembled markdown — automation could see the rendered pack body, but had no access to `coverage` (the high/medium/ambiguous confidence signal that drives `lvdcp_explain` and edit-mode gating), `trace_id` (the retrieval trace ID for `ctx history` lookup and F1.B sparkline correlation), or the ranked `retrieved_files` / `retrieved_symbols` lists (the structured signals that downstream re-ranking heuristics, hash-comparison workflows, and evaluation judges actually consume). The MCP `lvdcp_pack` tool already returned the full structured payload via its `PackResult` schema since the MCP feature shipped — we had two transports for the same retrieval pipeline emitting two contracts (markdown-only vs. structured-object), inviting drift every time the pipeline added a field. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx pack` that emits a single JSON object **mirroring the MCP `PackResult` schema 1:1**: `{markdown (the assembled pack body — the same string the text view prints; included so a consumer that wants the rendered pack still gets it via `jq -r .markdown` and a consumer that wants only the structured signals can ignore the field; stripping it would create a third contract divergent from MCP — wrong tradeoff), trace_id (the retrieval trace ID — round-trips into `ctx history` / `lvdcp_explain` lookup and F1.B sparkline correlation; persisted via `idx.save_trace(trace_with_project)` so CLI-originated queries land in the same trace store as MCP-originated ones), coverage (one of `"high"` / `"medium"` / `"ambiguous"` — the confidence signal that gates edit-mode workflows; `jq -e '.coverage == "high"'` is the natural CI gate for "the pack is confident enough to act on"), retrieved_files (ranked list of file paths — converted to a list from the `ContextPack` tuple because JSON has no tuple type; `jq -r '.retrieved_files[]'` feeds directly into hash-comparison drift detection and per-query coverage analysis), retrieved_symbols (ranked list of fully-qualified symbol names — same tuple→list conversion; `jq '.retrieved_symbols | length'` surfaces symbol-density signal for the eval harness)}`. **Single object, not a bare array** — `ctx pack` is a single-result retrieval call with a body (`markdown`) plus structured metadata (`trace_id`, `coverage`) plus two ranked sub-arrays. Same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command with run-level summary fields) and v0.8.50 `obsidian status` (tri-state vault contract). Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no top-level metadata to encode. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list / v0.8.50 obsidian status: pure data on stdout (no human chrome; structlog routed to `sys.stderr` since v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged), error path identical in both modes (un-indexed project → stderr message + exit 1, **never** `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — same v0.8.42-v0.8.50 discipline of "exit code is the gate, structured payload is for the success path"), trace persistence preserved across both modes so F1.B sparklines and `lvdcp_explain` see CLI-originated queries identically to MCP-originated ones. **CLI/MCP parity is the design goal** — two contracts for the same retrieval pipeline would invite subtle drift; one shared schema (`apps.mcp.tools.PackResult` ↔ `apps.cli.commands.pack._pack_to_json`) forces every shape change to be reviewed against both consumers. CLI-only change — no library code touched (no mutation to `libs/context_pack/`, `libs/project_index/`, or any retrieval pipeline code; `_pack_to_json` lives next to `pack` in `apps/cli/commands/pack.py`, sister-helper to v0.8.46-v0.8.50 CLI-shell payload shapers). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy markdown body byte-identically with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.50 "text path untouched" promise; a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer that pipes `ctx pack` to `pandoc` or another markdown processor), navigate-mode JSON emits a single object with the schema-locked key set (`_PACK_JSON_KEYS = {markdown, trace_id, coverage, retrieved_files, retrieved_symbols}` frozenset; `coverage` asserted in `_VALID_COVERAGE_VALUES = {high, medium, ambiguous}`; markdown body still carries the navigate-template signature `Context pack`; expected file `auth.py` surfaces from the seeded `login endpoint` query in the fixture), edit-mode JSON emits the **same** schema as navigate (locks render-mode-invariance of the JSON contract — only the markdown body shape differs, schema is invariant; markdown body asserted to carry the `Target files` edit-template signature so a refactor that accidentally routes edit mode through the navigate template breaks this test), error path under `--json` mode does **not** swallow into a `{"error": "..."}` stdout payload (un-indexed project exits 1 in both text and JSON modes; if any output parses as JSON, asserted **not** to be the success-shape dict — same discipline shared with v0.8.42-v0.8.50). All 7 tests in the file pass (3 pre-existing + 4 new). This unblocks workflows that the rolling `--json` rollout's earlier ticks couldn't reach: retrieval-quality dashboards (`for q in queries.txt; do ctx pack . "$q" --json | jq -c '{q: $q, cov: .coverage, files: (.retrieved_files | length)}'; done > eval.ndjson`), hash-comparison drift detection (store `retrieved_files` per query, alert when set diff exceeds threshold across reindexes), cross-project benchmark sweeps (same pack call across N projects, fold `coverage` distribution into hygiene reports), LLM-on-LLM evaluation (feed the structured pack to a judge model without re-parsing markdown), agentic re-ranking heuristics (downstream callers can re-rank `retrieved_files` against task-specific signals without a markdown-parsing step). Rejected alternatives: strip the `markdown` field from the JSON output (would create a third contract divergent from MCP — wrong tradeoff; consumers that don't want it can `jq 'del(.markdown)'`), wrap in `{"pack": {...}, "summary": {coverage, files_count, symbols_count}}` (over-engineered nesting for a flat 5-field payload; counts are trivially recoverable via `jq '.retrieved_files | length'`; same v0.8.45 / v0.8.49 / v0.8.50 argument against gratuitous envelopes), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.50 argument; the schema-locked frozenset test catches accidental divergence), include retrieval pipeline timing or per-stage breakdowns (out of scope for a render-shape ship — `ctx history` and `lvdcp_explain` are the right surfaces for trace deep-dives; `trace_id` round-trips the link), expose the full `ContextPack` dataclass (would leak internal fields like `pipeline_version`, `size_bytes` that aren't part of the MCP contract — mirroring `PackResult` 1:1 is the discipline), bare-array of file paths matching v0.8.46/v0.8.47/v0.8.49 shape (pack is a single-result retrieval call, not a per-row read; bare-array would force loss of `coverage`, `trace_id`, and the markdown body), add `--json` to `ctx pack` and a separate `ctx pack-trace --json` query in the same release (keep increments small; `pack` is the primary retrieval surface, trace-deep-dive is `lvdcp_explain`'s job and `ctx history --json` if the surface ever needs a CLI mirror). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `pack`), no library code touched (`libs/context_pack/builder.py::build_navigate_pack` / `build_edit_pack` and `ContextPack` dataclass signatures unchanged; `libs/project_index/index.py::ProjectIndex.retrieve` / `save_trace` signatures unchanged), no new on-disk artifacts (no extra trace records, no extra cache writes — `--json` is a pure render switch), MCP `lvdcp_pack` tool **untouched** (`apps.mcp.tools.PackResult` is the canonical schema this release mirrors — schema flows MCP→CLI, never CLI→MCP, to preserve the LLM-facing contract as the source of truth), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing pack test passes; `make typecheck` strict-mode 393 source files clean), trace persistence semantic preserved across both modes so F1.B sparklines and `lvdcp_explain` see CLI-originated queries identically. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.51-pack-json.md).

**v0.8.50 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx obsidian status --json` for scriptable enumeration of Obsidian-vault project state. The `ctx obsidian status` command has been the canonical "what does the Obsidian sync target currently contain" surface since the obsidian feature shipped — but stayed text-only with three different sentinel paths (`No Projects/ directory found in vault.` for the vault-never-set-up case, `No project directories found.` for the configured-but-empty case, and `Projects in vault (N):\n  - <name>` indented bullet list for the populated case), leaving every automation use case (CI guard asserting "the vault was synced for the project under test" via `ctx obsidian status --vault $VAULT --json | jq -e --arg p "$PROJECT_NAME" '.projects | any(. == $p)'`, multi-vault hygiene sweep folding per-vault project counts into a fleet inventory via `for v in /Volumes/*/vaults/*; do ctx obsidian status --vault "$v" --json; done | jq -s 'map({vault: .vault, count: (.projects | length)})'`, onboarding script that creates the missing `Projects/` directory before the first sync via `jq -e '.projects_dir_exists == false'`, dashboard surfacing the per-vault sync coverage gap via `jq -r '.projects | length'`) to brittle prose-grepping over three different output formats. The `Projects/` directory enumeration was always trivially structured (`sorted(p.name for p in projects_dir.iterdir() if p.is_dir())`) — we just weren't exposing the structured shape. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx obsidian status` that emits a single JSON object: `{vault (absolute path of the vault root — stringified for `find -exec` workflows), projects_dir (absolute path the command actually inspected — `<vault>/Projects` round-tripped so a script can confirm the run examined the path it intended without reconstructing the join), projects_dir_exists (boolean — the **critical** tri-state-distinguishing field that lets a script tell "vault was never set up" from "vault is configured but no projects synced yet" — both would collapse to `projects=[]` without it; onboarding scripts gate on `jq -e '.projects_dir_exists == false'` to know whether to `mkdir Projects/` before first sync), projects (always an array, sorted alphabetically, of subdirectory names — never `null`, never the prose sentinel; loose files at the projects root are excluded since the text view's existing `is_dir()` filter applies in both modes)}`. **Single object, not a bare array** — `obsidian status` has a tri-state contract (Projects/ missing vs. present-but-empty vs. populated) that a bare array of project names cannot encode without a sentinel value (e.g. `null` or `["__no_projects_dir__"]` would split the contract by render switch); the object cleanly distinguishes the states via `projects_dir_exists`. Compare with the bare-array siblings (`wiki status` v0.8.46 per-module, `wiki lint` v0.8.47 per-finding, `watch list` v0.8.49 per-project): those are pure per-row reads with no meta-state to encode. Same single-object discipline as v0.8.48 `wiki cross-project` (single-result generate command with run-level summary fields) — the right shape follows the underlying data, not a precedent. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project / v0.8.49 watch list: pure data on stdout (no human chrome), error path identical in both modes (vault path missing → Typer `--vault exists=True` validation rejects with non-zero exit before the command body runs; `--json` mode never tries to wrap it; same v0.8.42-v0.8.49 discipline of "exit code is the gate, structured payload is for the success path"), missing `Projects/` cleanly emits `projects_dir_exists=false` and exits 0 (a missing `Projects/` is a valid vault configuration where no syncs have happened yet — same semantic as v0.8.49 `last_scan_status="pending"` for an unscanned project; not an error condition that would force an exit-1 contract split). CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_vault_status_to_json` lives next to `status` in `apps/cli/commands/obsidian_cmd.py`, the only consumer; sister-helper to `_module_to_json` (v0.8.46), `_issue_to_json` (v0.8.47), `_cross_project_to_json` (v0.8.48), `_project_to_json` (v0.8.49) — same pattern of CLI-shell payload shaping, single-object variant). `obsidian sync` and `obsidian sync-all` subcommands **untouched** — these have mutation semantics with subprocess fan-out, sync timing, and per-project success/failure rollup that benefit from a separate ship with the streaming-vs-terminal `--json` question (NDJSON one event per project vs. single terminal summary for sync-all). Six new test invariants lock the contract — three text-mode invariants pin the legacy three-state output byte-for-byte (no JSON leak via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` asserted in the no-projects-dir and populated cases; locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.49 "text path untouched" promise so a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks these tests instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer), three JSON invariants lock the tri-state contract (`projects_dir_exists=false` + `projects=[]` for the vault-never-set-up case, `projects_dir_exists=true` + `projects=[]` for the configured-empty case — these two states **must remain distinguishable** in the JSON output or the scriptability promise breaks; populated case asserts sorted-alphabetical ordering, schema-locked frozenset `_OBSIDIAN_STATUS_JSON_KEYS = {vault, projects_dir, projects_dir_exists, projects}`, and that loose files at the projects root are excluded). Existing `obsidian sync-all` tests pass byte-identically — neither sync semantics nor the text-mode status output changed. Rejected alternatives: emit a bare array of project names matching v0.8.46/v0.8.47/v0.8.49 shape (loses the tri-state distinguishability — would force a sentinel string like `["__no_projects_dir__"]` or a `null` payload that splits the contract), wrap in `{"vault": {...}, "projects": [...]}` (over-engineered nesting for four flat fields; same v0.8.45 / v0.8.49 argument against gratuitous envelopes), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.49 argument), include per-project metadata (last-sync-time, file count, size on disk) in each entry (would require library plumbing into `libs/obsidian/` to surface per-project file metadata; out of scope for a CLI-only ship and a `obsidian inspect <project>` deep-dive subcommand is the cleaner factoring), exit 1 when `Projects/` is missing (changes the semantic — "missing Projects/" is a valid pre-first-sync state where the onboarding script wants to know to create the directory, not an error to halt the pipeline), add a `--include-loose-files` flag to surface loose files at the projects root (degrades signal-to-noise for the dominant use case and the tri-state contract focuses on the project-directory enumeration, not arbitrary vault content; a separate `obsidian ls` would be the cleaner factoring if needed), add `--json` to `obsidian sync` / `obsidian sync-all` in the same release (keep increments small; sync commands deserve their own analysis of streaming-vs-terminal `--json` semantics — a 50-project `sync-all` should probably emit NDJSON one event per project rather than buffer the entire run into a single terminal payload). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `obsidian status`), `obsidian sync` / `obsidian sync-all` subcommands untouched, no library code touched (helper lives in the CLI shell), no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (vault enumeration is an operator/automation surface, not retrieval context for LLMs — the vault content itself is already accessible via the file system), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing obsidian test passes), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.50-obsidian-status-json.md).

**v0.8.49 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx watch list --json` for scriptable enumeration of registered watch projects. The `ctx watch list` command has been the canonical "what does the auto-indexing daemon currently track" surface since v0.8.35 (when the `allow_transient` worktree-registration wiring landed) — but stayed text-only, leaving every automation use case (CI guard asserting "the daemon is watching the project under test" via `ctx watch list --json | jq -e --arg p "$PWD" 'any(.[]; .root == $p)'`, workspace-onboarding script that registers missing projects via `comm -13 <(ctx watch list --json | jq -r '.[].root | @text' | sort) <(ls -d ~/code/*/)`, dashboard surfacing "projects registered N days ago but never scanned" via `jq -r '.[] | select(.last_scan_at_iso == null) | .root'`, fleet-wide hygiene sweep folding per-host registration sets into a single inventory) to brittle prose-grepping over the indented path list (which trips on paths containing two leading spaces or matches the `no projects registered` sentinel as a literal path). `list_projects()` from `apps.agent.config` (re-export of `libs.core.projects_config.list_projects`) already returned a typed `list[ProjectEntry]` since the registry feature shipped — we just weren't exposing the structured shape. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx watch list` that emits a bare JSON array, one object per registered project, schema 1:1 mirror of `ProjectEntry`. Per-row schema: `root` (stringified absolute path — `Path` is not JSON-native, stringification matches the v0.8.48 `wiki_dir` precedent and lets `jq -r '.[].root'` feed straight into `find -exec`, `xargs`, or path comparison without quoting headaches), `registered_at_iso` (ISO-8601 UTC timestamp of when the project was added to the registry — required field, never null; round-trips into age-since-registration math via `jq -r '.[] | (now - (.registered_at_iso | fromdateiso8601))'`), `last_scan_at_iso` (ISO-8601 of the most recent successful scan, or `null` until the first scan completes — distinguishes "registered but unscanned" from "stale" without a sentinel-string convention; `jq 'map(select(.last_scan_at_iso == null))'` is the natural unscanned-project filter), `last_scan_status` (raw enum-like string `pending` / `success` / `failed` — pass-through from the `ProjectEntry.last_scan_status` field with `pending` as the registration default, lets dashboards `jq 'group_by(.last_scan_status) | map({key: .[0].last_scan_status, value: length}) | from_entries'` for at-a-glance fleet health). Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint / v0.8.48 wiki cross-project: bare array (not wrapped `{"projects": [...], "count": N}` — matches every read-side ship since v0.8.32; counts are trivially recoverable via `jq length`), empty registry returns `[]` (never `null`, never the text-mode `no projects registered` prose sentinel — `jq length`, `jq 'map(...)'` work without a None-guard), no human-prose markers leak (no leading two-space indent, no path-list dressing). **Bare array, not single object** — `wiki cross-project` (v0.8.48) emitted a single object because it's a generate command with one result payload; `watch list` is a per-row read whose natural shape is "a sequence of project rows", same unit of analysis as `wiki status` (per-module) and `wiki lint` (per-finding) — the right shape follows the underlying data, not a precedent. Same `_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset discipline as the wiki triad: schema-locked surface where adding a `ProjectEntry` field forces an explicit, reviewed update to both the helper and the test invariant — accidental field-leak (e.g. an internal `_resolved` cache field sneaking into the payload) breaks the test, not the consumer. CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_project_to_json` lives next to `list_cmd` in `apps/cli/commands/watch_cmd.py`, the only consumer; sister-helper to v0.8.46 `_module_to_json`, v0.8.47 `_issue_to_json`, v0.8.48 `_cross_project_to_json` — same pattern of CLI-shell payload shaping). `watch add` / `watch remove` / `watch start` / `watch install-service` / `watch uninstall-service` subcommands **untouched** — these have mutation semantics (registry write, daemon lifecycle, launchd integration) that benefit from separate ships with the streaming-vs-terminal `--json` question for service installation, where output ordering and progress events have render-policy implications. Four new test invariants lock the contract — text-mode empty-registry sentinel preserved (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.48 "text path untouched" promise; tests that `no projects registered` still appears literally on stdout for human consumers), text-mode populated indented path list preserved with **no JSON leak** asserted via `pytest.raises(json.JSONDecodeError)` (matches the v0.8.46 wiki status invariant; a future refactor that promotes JSON to the default render breaks this test instead of silently degrading every shell-pipeline consumer), empty registry under `--json` returns the empty array `[]` (locks the empty-state contract; consumers can rely on `jq length`, `jq 'map(...)'`, and array-shape array-iteration without special-casing the empty path), populated registry under `--json` emits a bare array of objects with the schema-locked key set on every row (`_WATCH_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset = `{root, registered_at_iso, last_scan_at_iso, last_scan_status}`; `root` stringified, `registered_at_iso` non-empty ISO string, `last_scan_at_iso` is `None` and `last_scan_status` is `"pending"` for fresh registrations — round-trips the registration defaults). All 6 tests in the file pass (2 pre-existing add-flow + 4 new list-flow). Existing `watch add` tests pass byte-identically — neither registration semantics nor the text-mode add output changed. Rejected alternatives: format `registered_at_iso` and `last_scan_at_iso` as POSIX floats matching the v0.8.46 `last_generated_ts` shape (mismatched with `ProjectEntry`'s native ISO-8601 storage; would force a parse-then-emit round-trip that loses sub-second precision; ISO strings are also script-friendlier for `date -d` cross-tool workflows than epoch math), wrap in `{"projects": [...], "summary": {pending: N, success: M, failed: K}}` (breaks bare-array precedent for zero benefit; `jq` recovers all counts), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.48 argument), add a `--status pending` / `--status success` / `--status failed` filter flag (trivially recoverable via `jq 'map(select(.last_scan_status == "pending"))'`; promote to a flag only if the pattern repeats across multiple consumers), include `is_transient` derived field per row (`is_transient` is computed at registration time and discarded; would require library plumbing to re-derive on read — out of scope for a CLI-only ship), add `--json` to `watch add` / `watch remove` in the same release (keep increments small; mutation commands deserve their own analysis of "did the registry actually change" semantics), echo invocation parameters or daemon PID (brittle — daemon liveness is `ctx watch start`'s concern, not `list`'s; schema would change with every new daemon-state knob). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `watch list`), `watch add` / `watch remove` / `watch start` / `watch install-service` / `watch uninstall-service` subcommands untouched, `apps.agent.config.list_projects` and `libs.core.projects_config.ProjectEntry` library signatures unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (registry enumeration is an operator/automation surface, not retrieval context for LLMs — pack assembly already knows the project root from its own argument), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing watch test passes), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.49-watch-list-json.md).

**v0.8.48 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx wiki cross-project --json` for scriptable cross-project run summary. The `ctx wiki cross-project` command aggregates wiki INDEXes across all registered projects, builds a global INDEX at `~/.lvdcp/wiki/INDEX.md`, and (when Claude CLI is available) detects cross-project patterns into `~/.lvdcp/wiki/patterns/` — but the CLI emitted only a single human-readable line (`Cross-project wiki generated: 3 pattern(s) written to /Users/me/.lvdcp/wiki`), leaving every automation use case (nightly cron warning on regressions like "you have 8 registered projects but only 3 patterns written — Claude CLI may have failed midway" via `jq -e '.patterns_written < (.projects_registered / 2)'`, multi-config sweep folding per-run results into a workspace-level dashboard via `for cfg in workspace_*/config.yaml; do ctx wiki cross-project --config "$cfg" --json; done | jq -s 'map({cfg: .config_path, patterns: .patterns_written})'`, pre-deploy gate asserting "the cross-project wiki is non-empty before publishing" via `jq -e '.patterns_written > 0'`, workspace-onboarding script surfacing the gap between registered projects and pattern coverage) to brittle `awk '{print $4}'` over the prose. `generate_cross_project_wiki()` already returned the patterns count and `list_projects()` is the canonical read for the registered-projects count — we just weren't composing them into a structured CLI payload. This release **completes the wiki subgroup read-side scriptability triad**: `wiki status` ✓ v0.8.46, `wiki lint` ✓ v0.8.47, `wiki cross-project` ✓ this release. A `--json` flag on `ctx wiki cross-project` emits a single JSON object: `{wiki_dir (absolute path the global INDEX and pattern articles were written to — stringified for `find -exec` workflows), config_path (absolute path to the config that was read — round-tripped so a script can confirm the run actually used the config it intended, catching `--config` typos without echoing back arbitrary input flags), projects_registered (total count from `list_projects(config_path)` — useful for the "is this run healthy?" gate `jq -e '.patterns_written < .projects_registered'` flagging Claude-CLI-degradation cases), patterns_written (pass-through of `generate_cross_project_wiki()`'s return value — same int the text view interpolates into the prose line; zero is a valid healthy state when only one project is registered)}`. **Single object, not a bare array** — `wiki status` (v0.8.46) and `wiki lint` (v0.8.47) emit bare arrays because they're per-row reads (one entry per module / one entry per finding); `wiki cross-project` is a generate command with one result payload. Schema-locked frozenset (`_WIKI_CROSS_PROJECT_JSON_KEYS`) still applies; the only difference is array-vs-object — the right shape for the underlying data, not a precedent break. Why a single object instead of `{"summary": {...}, "patterns": [{name, file}, ...]}`: requires a library signature change to expose pattern names from `generate_cross_project_wiki` (currently returns `int`); pattern names are filesystem-recoverable (`ls $(jq -r '.wiki_dir')/patterns/*.md` — no need to bake into the payload); summary-level fields are the higher-leverage gate (answer "did the run produce useful output? did it cover all my projects?"); per-pattern inspection is a deeper-dive workflow that benefits from `wiki lint` or direct file reading, and if a real consumer surfaces the natural follow-up is a separate `cross-project ls --json` read-side subcommand cleaner than overloading the generate command's payload. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status / v0.8.47 wiki lint: pure data on stdout (no human chrome), error path identical in both modes (missing config → `load_config` raises with a Typer traceback, `--json` mode never tries to wrap it; same v0.8.42-v0.8.47 discipline of "exit code is the gate; structured payload is for the success path"), Claude-CLI-missing case cleanly emits `patterns_written=0` and exits 0 (scripts gate on `patterns_written == 0 && projects_registered > 1` to detect "Claude CLI failed silently" — same shape as v0.8.42 `qdrant_warnings == []` for embedding-disabled). CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_cross_project_to_json` lives next to `cross_project` in `apps/cli/commands/wiki_cmd.py`, the only consumer; sister-helper to `_module_to_json` from v0.8.46 and `_issue_to_json` from v0.8.47 — same pattern of CLI-shell payload shaping, but emits a single object instead of a per-row dict because cross-project is a single-result generate command, not a per-row read). `wiki update`, `wiki status`, `wiki lint` subcommands **untouched** — status / lint already shipped JSON in v0.8.46 / v0.8.47; `update` deserves its own ship with the streaming-vs-terminal `--json` question (NDJSON one event per module vs. single terminal summary). Three new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy `Cross-project wiki generated: N pattern(s) written to ...` single-line format byte-identically with no JSON braces leak (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.47 "text path untouched" promise; a future refactor that accidentally promotes JSON to the default breaks this test), bare JSON object with exact key set per payload (`_WIKI_CROSS_PROJECT_JSON_KEYS` frozenset = `{wiki_dir, config_path, projects_registered, patterns_written}`; counts match the seeded fixture; `wiki_dir` asserted via suffix match `endswith("/.lvdcp/wiki")` since the absolute path is user-home-dependent; no human-prose markers leak), empty registry returns sensible payload (`projects_registered=0`, `patterns_written=0`, schema invariant still holds — locks the empty-state contract: scripts can detect "no work to do" via `jq -e '.patterns_written == 0'` without a None-guard; same discipline as v0.8.46 wiki status `[]` and v0.8.47 wiki lint `[]`). Existing 4 wiki status + 4 wiki lint tests pass byte-identically — text path untouched. Rejected alternatives: wrap in `{"run": {...}, "patterns": [{name, file}, ...]}` (requires library signature change to expose pattern names from `generate_cross_project_wiki`; pattern names are trivially filesystem-recoverable), emit a bare array of per-pattern entries matching v0.8.46/v0.8.47 shape (wrong unit of analysis — cross-project is a single-result generate command, not a per-row read; would either wrap every payload field in a single-element array or lose run-level summary fields like `projects_registered`), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.47 argument), include `claude_cli_available: bool` in the payload (would require library changes to surface the swallowed `RuntimeError` from `_detect_patterns_via_claude`; inferable from `patterns_written == 0 && projects_registered > 1`), echo invocation parameters (brittle — schema would change with every new flag; `config_path` is already round-tripped because it's the most useful field for "did this run use the config I intended"), add a `--dry-run` flag emitting JSON without performing file writes (cross-project is fundamentally a generate command — can't know `patterns_written` without invoking Claude; would degenerate to `{wiki_dir, config_path, projects_registered, patterns_written: null}`), separate `ctx wiki cross-project status --json` read-side subcommand (plausible follow-up but out of scope here — current need is the run-level structured result), add `--json` to `wiki update` in the same release (keep increments small; `update` deserves its own analysis of streaming-vs-terminal `--json` semantics). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `wiki cross-project`), `wiki update` / `wiki status` / `wiki lint` subcommands untouched, `libs/wiki/cross_project.py::generate_cross_project_wiki` and `libs/core/projects_config.py::list_projects` library signatures unchanged, file-write side effect (global INDEX + pattern articles) unchanged in both modes (`--json` is a render switch, not a behavior switch), no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `cross-project` already writes, no MCP surface (cross-project is an operator-driven aggregation, not retrieval context for LLMs — pattern articles themselves are accessible via the file system), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing wiki test passes), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.48-wiki-cross-project-json.md).

**v0.8.47 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx wiki lint --json` for scriptable wiki hygiene gating. The `ctx wiki lint` command has been the deterministic-pre-LLM hygiene check for wiki state since the wiki feature shipped — surfacing five issue classes (orphaned articles, missing articles, stale articles, empty articles, INDEX mismatch) — but stayed text-only, leaving every automation use case (pre-commit hook asserting `jq -e 'all(.[]; .severity != "error")'` over the lint payload, multi-project hygiene dashboard folding per-project per-severity counters, nightly CI surfacing "stale wiki articles per module" via `jq -r '.[] | select(.severity == "warning" and (.message | startswith("Stale"))) | .module_path'`, targeted `ctx wiki update --module $(jq -r '.[] | select(.message | startswith("Missing")) | .module_path')` pipeline) to brittle prose-grepping over the bullet list (which trips on module paths that happen to contain the substring `ERROR` or `WARN`). `lint_wiki()` in `libs/wiki/lint.py` already returned a clean `list[LintIssue]` (3-field dataclass: `severity` / `module_path` / `message`) since the wiki feature shipped — we just weren't exposing it. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx wiki lint` that emits a bare JSON array — one entry per finding, schema 1:1 mirror of `LintIssue`. Per-entry schema: `severity` (raw enum-like string `error` / `warning` — pass-through from the dataclass field; the text view's `[WARN]` / `[ERROR]` formatted prefixes are render concerns), `module_path` (whatever `lint_wiki` puts there — `(project)` sentinel for project-level findings like missing-`cache.db`, an article stem like `pkg.alpha` for per-article findings), `message` (unformatted human string — same string the text view shows minus the `  [WARN] <module>: ` prefix; consumers can parse the leading word `Orphaned` / `Missing` / `Stale` / `Empty` / `INDEX` for issue-class bucketing without needing a separate enum field). **The deliberate exit-code choice**: this release **preserves the exit-code gate unchanged across both modes** — error rows exit 1 in both text and JSON; warnings-only and clean exits 0 in both. The v0.8.46 release note flagged this as the open question for the lint slice (*"whether `--json` should also exit 1 on error rows or only emit the structured payload"*); the answer this release commits to is "preserve the gate" because (1) the exit code is the script's gating mechanism (a CI guard like `ctx wiki lint . --json | jq ... && echo "ok"` works because `set -e` short-circuits on the lint exit — stripping the gate would force every consumer to duplicate `jq -e 'all(.[]; .severity != "error")'`); (2) splitting the contract by render switch is a code-smell — `--json` is a render concern (how the data is shaped on stdout), the exit-code gate is a semantic concern (does this command succeed or fail), and render switches must not change semantics (same v0.8.42-v0.8.46 discipline that keeps the missing-`cache.db` error path identical in both modes); (3) the structured payload IS the error detail — keeping the gate gives the clean pattern of "exit code is the gate, payload is the diagnostic" matching `eslint` / `mypy` / `ruff` and every other lint tool with a JSON output mode. The single subtle difference vs. v0.8.42-v0.8.46: in those releases the error path emitted stderr + exit 1 + empty stdout (the missing-`cache.db` path); here the error path emits a **valid JSON payload** on stdout (the structured findings) AND exits 1 — that's not a contract split, it's a different error class (`cache.db` missing is an environment error with no data to render → stderr + exit 1; `error`-severity lint findings are a data error with data to render → payload + exit 1). Same gate, different stdout shape — the right Unix discipline. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore / v0.8.42 scan / v0.8.43 inspect / v0.8.44 memory list / v0.8.45 reconcile / v0.8.46 wiki status: bare array (not wrapped `{"issues": [...], "summary": {...}}` — matches the v0.8.32 `ls --json` precedent; summary counts are trivially recoverable via `jq 'group_by(.severity) | map({key: .[0].severity, value: length}) | from_entries'`), empty list `[]` for "no issues found" (never `null`, never the `No issues found.` prose marker — `jq length` works without a None-guard), no human-prose markers leak into the JSON output (no `warning(s)`, no `error(s)`, no totals line). CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_issue_to_json` lives next to `lint_cmd` in `apps/cli/commands/wiki_cmd.py`, the only consumer; sister-helper to `_module_to_json` from v0.8.46 — same pattern of per-row JSON shaping in the CLI shell). `wiki update`, `wiki status`, `wiki cross-project` subcommands **untouched** — `update` has mutation semantics with per-module progress streaming that benefits from a separate ship (the streaming-vs-terminal question for `--json` deserves its own analysis); `status` shipped in v0.8.46; `cross-project` is the next read-side slice but reads from a different layer (`libs/wiki/cross_project.py`). Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy bullet list byte-identically (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.46 "text path untouched" promise), bare JSON array with exact key set per entry (schema-locked surface — `_WIKI_LINT_JSON_KEYS` frozenset = `{severity, module_path, message}`, warnings-only seeded data → exit 0 in both modes locking the "warnings don't fire the gate" half of the exit-code contract; also asserts no human-prose markers leak into the JSON output), empty `[]` contract (clean project returns `[]`, not `null`, not the `No issues found.` prose marker), exit-code gate preservation on errors (sub-50-byte article triggers the `Empty article` error rule; exits 1 in **both** text and JSON modes — locks the deliberate exit-code preservation choice so a refactor that strips the `if errors: raise typer.Exit(code=1)` from the JSON path breaks this test instead of silently degrading every CI guard). Existing 4 wiki status tests + every other wiki test pass byte-identically — text path untouched. Rejected alternatives: strip the exit-code gate in `--json` mode ("only emit the structured payload" — would force every consumer to duplicate the gate logic and produce a contract split where `--json` and the text mode disagree on what "this command succeeded" means; render switches must not change semantics), wrap in `{"issues": [...], "summary": {error: N, warning: M, total: K}}` (breaks bare-array precedent for zero benefit — `jq` recovers all counts), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.46 argument), add a structured `class` field per row (string-prefix protocol on `message` is enough for current consumers — promote to a `class` field only when a real consumer needs the explicit enum), add a `--severity error` / `--severity warning` filter flag (trivially recoverable via `jq 'map(select(.severity == "error"))'`), make the JSON output suppress warnings unless `--include-warnings` is passed (breaks symmetry with the text view and conflates "what to render" with "how to render" — filter in `jq` if needed), echo `errors_count` / `warnings_count` totals in the JSON shape (inflates the payload with derived data; `jq length` and `jq 'group_by(.severity) | length'` recover both for free). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `wiki lint`), `wiki update` / `wiki status` / `wiki cross-project` subcommands untouched, `libs/wiki/lint.py::lint_wiki` and the `LintIssue` dataclass unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (wiki lint is a hygiene/observability surface for operators and CI, not retrieval context for LLMs), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing wiki test passes), exit-code gate preserved unchanged (error rows → exit 1 in both modes; warnings/empty → exit 0 in both modes), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.47-wiki-lint-json.md).

**v0.8.46 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx wiki status --json` for scriptable wiki state per module. The `ctx wiki status` command has been the human-readable per-module wiki-state report (`module / status / last-generated`) since the wiki feature shipped, but stayed text-only — leaving every automation use case (pre-commit hook asserting "no dirty wiki modules accumulated since the last `ctx wiki update`" via `jq -e 'all(.[]; .status == "current")'`, workspace-sweep dashboard folding per-project wiki-staleness counters into a single hygiene view, nightly CI surfacing "wiki articles older than N days" via `jq -r '.[] | select(.last_generated_ts < (now - 7*86400)) | .module_path'`, targeted `ctx wiki update --module $(jq -r '.[] | select(.status == "dirty") | .module_path')` pipeline) to brittle prose-grepping over the table render. `get_all_modules()` in `libs/wiki/state.py` already returned a structured per-row payload (`module_path`, `wiki_file`, `last_generated_ts`, `source_hash`, `status`) since the wiki feature shipped — we just weren't exposing it. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx wiki status` that emits a bare JSON array — one entry per tracked module, schema 1:1 mirror of the `wiki_state` row. Per-entry schema: `module_path`, `wiki_file`, `status` (raw enum-like string `current` / `dirty` — pass-through from the SQL `status` column so `jq 'map(select(.status == "dirty"))'` works without nested object access), `last_generated_ts` (raw POSIX float — **not** the formatted `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` the text view shows; dashboards do age math `now - last_generated_ts` directly without re-parsing a formatted string back to epoch seconds; `0` is the sentinel for "never generated", matching the text view's `never` rendering; formatted view trivially recoverable via `jq -r '.[].last_generated_ts | strftime(...)'` or shell `date -r`), `source_hash` (full hex digest — the text view doesn't show it; consumers wanting a short prefix can `jq -r '.[].source_hash | .[0:8]'`; full hex enables hash-comparison workflows like "did the wiki source change between PRs?"). Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune, v0.8.40 restore, v0.8.42 scan, v0.8.43 inspect, v0.8.44 memory list, v0.8.45 reconcile: bare array (not wrapped `{"modules": [...]}` — matches v0.8.32 `ls --json` precedent), empty list `[]` for "no modules tracked" (never `null`, never the human-prose `No modules tracked.` marker — `jq length` works without a None-guard), error path is identical in both modes (missing `cache.db` → stderr message + exit 1, **never** `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — splitting that contract would force every consumer to parse-then-check-keys instead of just relying on `set -e`), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged so JSON consumers benefit automatically. CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_module_to_json` lives next to `status_cmd` in `apps/cli/commands/wiki_cmd.py`, the only consumer; sister-helper to `_memory_to_json` from v0.8.44 — same pattern of per-row JSON shaping in the CLI shell). `wiki update`, `wiki lint`, `wiki cross-project` subcommands **untouched** — `update` has mutation semantics with progress streaming that benefits from a separate ship; `lint` has its own exit-code gating (`exit 1` when errors exist, `exit 0` with warnings) that needs careful thought on whether `--json` should also exit 1 on error rows or only emit the structured payload; `cross-project` is the natural next read-side slice. Four new test invariants lock the contract — text path emits the legacy table format byte-identically (locks the v0.8.42-v0.8.45 "text path untouched" promise), bare JSON array with exact key set per entry (schema-locked surface — `_WIKI_STATUS_JSON_KEYS` frozenset = `{module_path, wiki_file, status, last_generated_ts, source_hash}`, adding a key requires bumping the frozenset + the helper at the same time; `status='current'` rows have non-zero `last_generated_ts` (raw POSIX float), `status='dirty'` rows have `last_generated_ts=0`), empty `wiki_state` table returns `[]` not `null` and not the prose marker (locks the empty-list contract so consumers can do `jq length` without a None-guard), missing `cache.db` exits 1 in both text and JSON modes with `no cache.db` on the merged stderr/stdout output and **never** emits a `{"error": "..."}` payload (no `"error"` key, `json.loads(output)` raises — locks the discipline shared with v0.8.42-v0.8.45). Rejected alternatives: format `last_generated_ts` as the same `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` string the text view shows (loses script-side ergonomic of doing age math directly; forces consumers to re-parse a formatted string back to epoch seconds — text view's formatting is a render concern, JSON contract is data), truncate `source_hash` to 8 chars (loses the full hex digest that enables hash-comparison workflows; truncation is trivially recoverable via `jq -r '.[].source_hash | .[0:8]'` for display), wrap in `{"modules": [...], "summary": {dirty: N, current: M}}` (breaks the v0.8.32 / v0.8.40 / v0.8.44 bare-array precedent — summary counts are trivially recoverable via `jq 'group_by(.status) | map({key: .[0].status, value: length}) | from_entries'`, no value in baking it into the payload shape), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.45 argument), add `--status dirty` / `--status current` filter flag (trivially recoverable via `jq 'map(select(.status == "dirty"))'`; promote to a flag only if the pattern repeats across multiple consumers), add `--json` to `wiki update` / `wiki lint` / `wiki cross-project` in the same release (keep increments small; `status` is the natural read-side companion mirroring the v0.8.45 read-side-first pattern), make the error path emit `{"error": "...", "exit_code": 1}` JSON in `--json` mode (would split the contract — exit code is the script gate, stderr carries the human message, stdout is exclusively the success payload). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `wiki status`), `wiki update` / `wiki lint` / `wiki cross-project` subcommands untouched, `libs/wiki/state.py::get_all_modules` and the `wiki_state` SQL schema unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (wiki state is a hygiene/observability surface for operators, not retrieval context for LLMs — the wiki content itself is already accessible via the file system), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing wiki test passes), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.46-wiki-status-json.md).

**v0.8.45 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx timeline reconcile --json` for scriptable orphan-flagging. The `ctx timeline` subgroup has had `status --json` since spec-010 T034, but its read-side companion `reconcile` (which walks `git rev-list --all` + `git reflog` and flags symbol-timeline events whose `commit_sha` is no longer reachable as orphaned) stayed text-only — leaving every cron-driven hygiene pipeline (nightly `reconcile` after `git gc --prune=now` posting Slack alerts when `orphaned_newly_flagged > 50`, multi-project sweep folding per-project payloads into a workspace-hygiene dashboard, CI guard asserting "reconcile didn't accidentally orphan more than N events on this branch") to brittle prose-grepping. `ReconcileReport` already carried every field a script needs (`project_root`, `git_available`, `reachable_commit_count`, `orphaned_newly_flagged`, `orphaned_by_event_type`) since spec-010 T033 — we just weren't exposing it. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx timeline reconcile` that emits a 1:1 mirror of the dataclass. `orphaned_by_event_type` is alphabetically sorted (the dataclass `dict[str, int]` carries whatever insertion order the SQL `GROUP BY` emits — implementation-dependent across SQLite versions and table statistics; the CLI helper explicitly sorts so consumers can `jq -r '.orphaned_by_event_type | keys[]'` without an explicit `sort` filter — the script-side ergonomic that matches v0.8.43's `most_common()` ordering for inspect counts). Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.42/v0.8.43/v0.8.44: pure data on stdout, no human chrome, error path is identical in both modes (`git unavailable` → stderr message + exit 1, **never** `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — splitting that contract would force every consumer to parse-then-check-keys instead of just relying on `set -e`). CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_reconcile_report_to_json` lives next to `reconcile_cmd`, the only consumer; sister-helper to the `_event_counts` and `_orphaned_count` private helpers already in the same module — keeps render-shape concerns in the CLI shell layer where they belong). `enable` / `disable` / `status` / `prune` / `backfill` subcommands **untouched** — `enable` / `disable` are pure side-effect side-effects with no payload to emit (`cat $project/.context/timeline.enabled` recovers the state); `status` already has `--json` since the subgroup shipped; `prune` is destructive and deserves its own ship with the v0.8.38 dry-run-vs-apply discipline. Three new test invariants lock the contract — exact key set on JSON payload (schema-locked surface, `_RECONCILE_JSON_KEYS` frozenset; injected `ReconcileReport` via monkeypatch avoids the cost of spinning up a real git repo for a pure render-layer test), `git unavailable` mode never emits `{"error": ...}` payload (no leading `{`, no `"error"` key, `json.loads(output)` raises — locks the discipline shared with v0.8.42-v0.8.44), `orphaned_by_event_type` keys land alphabetically (insertion order intentionally non-alphabetical in the fixture; locks the explicit sort so a refactor that drops it breaks this test instead of silently reshuffling consumer dashboards). Existing 9 timeline tests pass byte-identically — text path untouched. Rejected alternatives: schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38-v0.8.44 argument), make the error path emit `{"error": "...", "exit_code": 1}` JSON in `--json` mode (would split the contract — exit code is the script gate, stderr carries the human message, stdout is exclusively the success payload), sort `orphaned_by_event_type` by descending count instead of alphabetically (different semantic from v0.8.43's `most_common()`: there the dimension is *cardinality* — which language has the most files; here it's *typology* — added/modified/removed/renamed/moved are a closed enum-like set, alphabetic ordering reads more predictably), bundle `--json` on `reconcile` + `prune` + `enable` + `disable` in the same release (keep increments small — `reconcile` is the natural read-side companion to the already-`--json`-enabled `status`; `prune` deserves its own ship with destructive discipline), include `elapsed_seconds` in the payload (reconcile timing is observable via shell `time ctx timeline reconcile`; adds noise without serving a script-side use case), echo invocation parameters in the JSON (brittle — schema would change with every new flag; `project_root` already round-trips the resolved scan target). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `reconcile_cmd`), `libs/symbol_timeline/reconcile.py::reconcile` and `ReconcileReport` library signatures unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (reconcile is a hygiene operation triggered by operators / cron, not by an LLM session asking for context), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing timeline test passes), no embedding / Qdrant / git / wiki behavior change. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.45-reconcile-json.md).

**v0.8.44 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx memory list --json` for scriptable memory review queue. The memory subcommand group has been the human-readable interface to project memory proposals (`ctx memory list` / `accept` / `reject`) since the feature shipped, but `list` stayed text-only — leaving every automation use case (weekly digest of unreviewed proposals, CI guards over the queue, multi-project review-queue dashboards, pre-commit hooks that surface "this branch has unreviewed memories") to brittle prose-grepping. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx memory list` that emits a bare JSON array — one entry per memory, schema 1:1 mirror of the `Memory` dataclass minus `body` (recoverable via `cat $(jq -r '.[].path')` for the rare consumer that needs the markdown source). Per-entry schema: `id`, `status` (enum value: `proposed` / `accepted` / `rejected`), `topic`, `tags` (JSON array — eagerly converted from the dataclass `tuple[str, ...]` so downstream serializers see a list), `created_at_iso`, `created_by`, `path` (absolute on-disk markdown path). Composes with `--status` — `--status accepted --json` returns only accepted entries, render switch (`--json`) is orthogonal to the filter axis. Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune, v0.8.40 restore, v0.8.42 scan, v0.8.43 inspect: bare array (not wrapped `{"memories": [...]}` — matches v0.8.32 `ls --json` precedent), empty list `[]` for "no memories matched" (never `null`, never the human-prose `(no memories)` marker — `jq length` works without a None-guard), structlog routing introduced in v0.8.42 carries forward unchanged so JSON consumers benefit automatically. CLI-only change — no library helpers added (`_memory_to_json` lives next to `list_cmd` in `apps/cli/commands/memory_cmd.py`, the only consumer; premature to extract until a future `ctx memory show --json` needs it). `accept_cmd` and `reject_cmd` **untouched** — no current consumer needs structured confirmation of the mutation, and `list --status accepted --json` after the call is the right script-side contract for "did the accept land". Three new test invariants lock the contract — exact key set per entry (schema-locked surface — adding a key requires bumping the test's `_MEMORY_LIST_JSON_KEYS` frozenset + the helper at the same time), empty project returns `[]` (not `null`, not the prose marker), `--status` composition (`--status accepted --json` returns `[]` before accept, returns the row after `accept_memory()` flips it, `--status proposed --json` returns `[]` after the flip — locks render-vs-filter orthogonality). Existing 5 memory tests pass byte-identically — text path untouched.
