Rejected alternatives: include `body` in the JSON output (inflates list payload — bodies are often hundreds of lines of markdown, exact use case `--json` exists to support; future `ctx memory show <id> --json` is the right surface for body-level access), wrap in `{"memories": [...]}` (breaks bare-array precedent for zero benefit — `jq length` already gives the count), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38–v0.8.43 argument), add `--json` to `accept` / `reject` too (premature — no current consumer needs structured mutation confirmation; symmetry-for-symmetry's-sake adds CLI surface for zero use case), make path field relative (absolute path is more useful for `find -exec` / multi-project sweeps; basename trivially recoverable via `jq '.path | split("/") | last'`), sort the array by `created_at_iso` descending (changing order here splits the source of truth with the text path; order-sensitive consumers can `jq 'sort_by(.created_at_iso) | reverse'`). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json` on `list_cmd`), `accept_cmd` / `reject_cmd` untouched, `libs/memory/models.py::Memory` and `libs/memory/store.py::list_memories` library signatures unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (`lvdcp_memory_list` already returns structured data — duplicating with `--json` flag would split source of truth), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing memory test passes). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.44-memory-list-json.md).

**v0.8.43 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx inspect --json` for scriptable index stats. v0.8.42 brought scan results into the scriptable surface; the read-side inspect command stayed text-only, leaving a gap for any monitoring or dashboard that wants to track index health (file counts per language, symbol-type distributions, relation-graph density) without parsing human prose. This release adds a `--json` flag on `ctx inspect` that emits a schema-locked payload — `path` (resolved scan target, absolute), `files` (total int), `language_counts` (dict of lang → count, **insertion-ordered by descending count** so `jq '.language_counts | to_entries[0].key'` yields the most-frequent language without an explicit sort), `symbols` + `symbol_type_counts` (function/class/method distribution), `relations` + `relation_type_counts` (calls/imports/specifies distribution). Same scriptability discipline as v0.8.38 prune, v0.8.40 restore, v0.8.42 scan: pure data on stdout, no human chrome, error path is identical in both modes (un-indexed project → stderr message + exit 1, **never** `{"error": "..."}` swallowed into stdout JSON — splitting that contract would force every consumer to parse-then-check-keys instead of just relying on `set -e`). Library / CLI layering: a new `InspectPayload` TypedDict gives mypy strict catch on field-name typos in the renderer and gives JSON consumers a documented contract — adding a field to the dataclass is the single point that surfaces it in both text and JSON outputs by design. `_collect_inspect_payload(idx, *, path)` is the pure-data builder; `_render_text(payload, *, name)` is the text renderer that walks the same payload — single source of truth for row order and labels keeps text and JSON paths in lockstep. `inspect()` signature also dropped its `typer.Argument` defaults in favor of plain `Path` + keyword-only `as_json: bool = False`, same direct-call ergonomics the scan command adopted in v0.8.42 (the inner function is called from `apps/cli/main.py::inspect`, not by Typer itself). Five test invariants (1 existing + 4 new) lock the contract — exact key set on JSON payload (`{path, files, language_counts, symbols, symbol_type_counts, relations, relation_type_counts}`), JSON-only output on stdout (`json.loads(result.stdout)` succeeds against the entire stdout — confirms no structlog or human-prose leak, same guarantee v0.8.42 introduced), `*_counts` dicts are descending-ordered (locks the `most_common()` semantic so a refactor that drops it breaks this test instead of silently reshuffling consumer dashboards), un-indexed project surfaces error on stderr + exit 1 in BOTH text and JSON modes (no `{"error": ...}` leak into stdout). Existing 1 inspect test passes byte-identically — text path untouched. Rejected alternatives: include `relations` graph adjacency in the JSON (different consumer pattern — `ctx pack` is the right surface, not `inspect`), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38 / v0.8.40 / v0.8.42 argument), expose `path` as the project name only (the resolved absolute path is more useful for `find -exec` workflows binding multiple inspects back to their roots), make the error path emit `{"error": "..."}` JSON in `--json` mode (would split the contract — exit code is the script gate, stderr carries the human message, stdout is exclusively the success payload), add `--no-counts` flag to suppress the per-type breakdowns for compactness (premature — `jq 'del(.language_counts, .symbol_type_counts, .relation_type_counts)'` does this without a flag). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag (`--json`), no library signature changes (`ProjectIndex.iter_*` untouched), no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (the MCP `lvdcp_inspect` tool already returns structured data; duplicating with `--json` flag would split source of truth), text output **byte-identical** byte-by-byte (every existing inspect test passes), no embedding / Qdrant / git / wiki behavior change. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.43-inspect-json.md).

**v0.8.42 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx scan --json` for scriptable scan results. The full / incremental scan surface has been the foundation of every other LV_DCP feature since day one, but its CLI output has stayed text-only: `scanned 42 files in /path (3 reparsed, 0 stale removed), 187 symbols, 12 reparsed / 64 total relations in 0.31s`. That's fine for humans, useless for scripts that want to gate on counters (cron-driven daily full re-scan that posts a Slack alert when `files_reparsed` spikes; CI guard that asserts a bulk refactor reparses ≥N files; `find -exec ctx scan --json` over a workspace bundling per-project `ScanResult`s into a single dashboard payload). Up until now the only path was a brittle regex over the human prose. This release adds a `--json` flag that emits a 1:1 mirror of the `ScanResult` dataclass plus three CLI-side fields the library doesn't know about: `path` (resolved scan root, for binding multiple results back to their source), `mode` (`"full"` or `"incremental"`, so a script can defensively assert intent — e.g. a daily `--full --json | jq -e '.mode == "full"'`), and `qdrant_warnings` (list[str], empty list when embedding config is healthy — same ergonomic discipline as v0.8.38: `payload.qdrant_warnings | length` works without a None-guard). The full schema: `path`, `mode`, `files_scanned`, `files_reparsed`, `stale_files_removed`, `symbols_extracted`, `relations_reparsed`, `relations_cached`, `elapsed_seconds`, `wiki_dirty_count`, `qdrant_warnings`. Pure data — no hints, no headers, no advisory text. Side effects (auto-register in `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml`, `CLAUDE.md` discipline section update) still run on `--json` because they're part of "scan" semantics, not output rendering. Bundled discovery: structlog defaulted to `PrintLoggerFactory` (which writes to **stdout**), so timeline / wiki / embedding diagnostics interleaved with `typer.echo` JSON and broke `jq` parsing. Fix is a one-line `structlog.configure(logger_factory=WriteLoggerFactory(file=sys.stderr))` at the CLI entry point — applied before any subcommand module imports because structlog caches the factory at `get_logger()` time. Logs now go to stderr uniformly across every CLI subcommand (not just `--json` ones), which is the right Unix discipline anyway. Same internal refactor as v0.8.38 prune / v0.8.40 restore: `_collect_qdrant_warnings()` and `_scan_result_to_json()` are extracted helpers (the warning-collection logic was already in `scan()`, now it's a named function reused by both text and JSON paths). `scan()` signature also dropped its `typer.Argument` / `typer.Option` defaults in favor of plain `bool` — direct callers (other CLI commands invoking it) and tests that omit kwargs no longer trip on `typer.OptionInfo` truthiness ambiguity (the inner function is called from `apps/cli/main.py::scan`, not by Typer itself). Four new test invariants lock the contract — exact key set on the JSON payload, JSON-only output on stdout (no human prose leaks — `json.loads(result.stdout)` succeeds against the entire stdout), `--full --json` echoes `mode=full` so scripts can assert intent, `qdrant_warnings == []` (empty list, not `null`) when Qdrant is disabled. Existing 4 scan tests continue to pass byte-identically — the text path is untouched. Rejected alternatives: emit JSON only when piped to non-tty stdout (magic; `--json` is explicit), include the resolved `.context/` artifact paths in the JSON (scripts can derive them from `path` — adds noise), schema-version the JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38 / v0.8.40 argument), separate `--json-pretty` vs `--json-compact` flags (premature — `jq -c` handles compaction and the default 2-space indent reads fine in cron logs), exit non-zero when `qdrant_warnings` is non-empty (warnings are advisory, not errors — same v0.8.41 discipline of not promoting nudges to gates). Scope locks: only one new CLI flag, no library signature changes (`scan_project` untouched), no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface (the MCP scan tool already returns structured data — duplicating with `--json` flag would split the source of truth), text output unchanged byte-identically (every existing scan test passes), no embedding / Qdrant behavior change (best-effort upsert still runs on incremental scans with `changed_for_embed` populated). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.42-scan-json.md).

**v0.8.41 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx registry ls` surfaces backup-availability footer for prune-undo discoverability. v0.8.40 added `ctx registry restore` as the first-class inverse of `prune --yes`, but discoverability stayed implicit: a user who didn't read the `prune --yes` output (or who ran `prune` weeks ago and forgot) had no way to learn from the `ls` view that a `*.bak` recovery handle existed beside their live config. The CLI surface that users naturally reach for first ("show me what's in my registry") was silent about the recovery handle that protects them. This release adds a one-line footer on the `ctx registry ls` text output when (and only when) `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml.bak` exists: `(backup: /path/to/.bak — Nh old — \`ctx registry restore\` to undo last prune)`. Footer fires regardless of which `--kind / --stale / --missing` filter was used (the backup is a property of the live config, not of any particular slice — and a user filtering by `--missing` finding zero rows still benefits from knowing recovery is available). Footer absent when no `*.bak` exists (default for fresh users — no clutter). Library layer: new `backup_status(config_path, *, backup_suffix=".bak", now=None) -> tuple[Path | None, float | None]` in `libs/status/registry_audit.py` — pure read, returns `(None, None)` when no backup, `(path, age_seconds)` otherwise. Age is `mtime`-delta clamped to non-negative for clock-skew safety (NFS / dual-boot / virtualization can transiently skew mtime ahead of `time.time()`). `now` kwarg injectable for deterministic tests. `backup_suffix` kwarg matches the same default as `prune_stale` / `restore_from_backup` and keeps the door open for a future `--backup-suffix` flag without a library signature change. CLI layer: `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py::ls_cmd` calls `backup_status` after `_render_text`, appends a one-line `(backup: ...)` footer when present, with a new `_format_backup_age_seconds` helper that uses the same compact `<1h` / `Nh` / `Nd` vocabulary as the table's `LASTSCAN` column. JSON output (`ls --json`) **unaffected** — bare array of audit rows; backup info reachable via `restore --json` for scripts (which already returns `backup_path`). Eight new test invariants lock the contract — 4 library-layer (no `*.bak` returns `(None, None)`, present `*.bak` returns path + accurate mtime-derived age, future-dated mtime clamps to age 0, custom suffix kwarg honored) and 4 CLI-layer (no footer when no backup, footer present with path + `<1h` tag + restore command name when backup exists, JSON output stays bare array with no backup keys leaking into row schema, footer composes with `--kind` / `--stale` / `--missing` filters). Rejected alternatives: emit backup info in the `ls --json` output too (would force a wrapped `{projects: [...], backup: {...}}` schema and break every existing JSON consumer — restore --json already provides this surface), surface backup status only when the `ls` table is empty (creates a "footer disappears when you have rows" UX confusion — the recovery handle is equally relevant whether you have 0 or 50 entries), color the footer differently (same TTY/`NO_COLOR` global decision deferred since v0.8.37), add a `--no-backup-footer` opt-out flag (premature — only suppress when there's a complaint), expose backup info on `ctx status` instead of `ls` (status is a cross-feature dashboard; users investigating registry state are already in `ls`), add a separate `ctx registry status` overview command (CLI surface bloat for one-line of info that fits naturally on `ls`). Scope locks: only one new function added to `registry_audit.py` (no removed/renamed fields, no signature change on `audit_registry` / `is_stale` / `is_missing`), `ls --json` output schema unchanged (every existing JSON consumer still passes byte-identically), text output above the footer unchanged (table renderer untouched), no registry schema change, no new on-disk artifacts, no MCP surface, no new CLI flags, dashboard UI untouched (CLI-side discoverability is the right surface for a CLI-only recovery operation — explicitly per v0.8.40 deferral of dashboard backup widget). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.41-ls-backup-footer.md).

**v0.8.40 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx registry restore` for prune undo. `ctx registry prune --yes` has written a sibling `*.bak` snapshot before every mutation since v0.8.33. The recovery story has always been documented as a manual one-liner: `mv ~/.lvdcp/config.yaml{.bak,}`. That works, but it's brittle (typo a brace and you've moved the wrong file or lost the live config), invisible to scripts (no JSON contract for "the prune was rolled back"), and missing from the `ctx registry` subcommand surface (`ls`, `prune` exist; `restore` did not — users discovered the undo handle only by reading `prune --yes` output and noticing the `backup saved to ...` line). The v0.8.38 release note explicitly listed `ctx registry restore` as a follow-up — now blocking enough, since every other piece of the registry-hygiene quartet (write/read/script/UI) shipped in v0.8.36–v0.8.39, leaving restore as the last asymmetry. This release adds a `ctx registry restore` subcommand: defaults to dry-run with entry counts and a signed `delta`, `--yes` to apply atomically, `--json` for scripts (1:1 mirror of `RestoreResult` — same discipline as v0.8.38). Library layer: `libs/status/registry_prune.py` gains `RestoreResult` dataclass + `restore_from_backup(config_path, *, apply=False, backup_suffix=".bak")` — reads both `.bak` and live config to compute counts, on `apply=True` writes through the same atomic `save_config` writer used everywhere else; raises `FileNotFoundError` with a `prune --yes` hint when no backup exists. CLI layer: `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py::restore_cmd` is a thin Typer shell with `--yes` and `--json` flags + `_restore_result_to_json` helper. The `*.bak` is intentionally **left in place** after a successful restore — same content now lives in both files, giving the user a re-undo handle and costing nothing (next `prune --yes` overwrites it with a fresh snapshot anyway). The `delta = backup_entry_count - current_entry_count` field is signed in the human output (`+2`, `-1`, `+0`): positive = restore adds entries back (typical undo case), negative = restore *removes* entries the user added since the backup (surfaced in dry-run preview so the user knows they're about to lose work — explicitly **not** blocked behind a confirmation gate, the dry-run already shows the loss and a gate would make `--json` harder to script). Ten new test invariants lock the contract — 5 library-layer (dry-run is pure read, apply replaces config and keeps backup, no-backup raises, missing live config gracefully handled, negative delta correctly computed) and 5 CLI-layer (dry-run is default, `--yes` applies and keeps backup, no-backup exits 1 with hint, JSON dry-run shape, JSON `--yes` apply shape — schema invariant across both). Rejected alternatives: delete `.bak` after restore (asymmetrically destroys recovery info — next prune overwrites it anyway), block negative-delta restores behind a second flag (dry-run already shows the loss), rename live config to `*.before-restore` before swapping (two backup files instead of one — confusing), `restore --to <path>` for arbitrary destinations (premature — only documented backup is the sibling `.bak`), make `restore` an alias for `prune --restore` (conflates inverses — symmetric top-level subcommands beat flag-stuffing), schema versioning JSON output (premature ceremony, same v0.8.38 argument), auto-restore on prune failure (would hide failure modes — explicit restore is the right primitive). Scope locks: only one new dataclass and one new function added to `registry_prune.py`, no removed/renamed fields, no signature change on `prune_stale` / `plan_prune` / `PruneResult`, no registry schema change, no new on-disk artifacts beyond what `*.bak` already provides, no public signature change on read-side helpers, default behavior of `ctx registry prune` unchanged (every existing prune test passes byte-identically), no MCP surface (destructive operations and their inverses stay CLI-only — same lock as v0.8.33). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.40-registry-restore.md).

**v0.8.39 (2026-04-25)** — Dashboard surfaces tombstone counter on the "projects active" card. v0.8.36 added `ctx registry prune --missing` and v0.8.37 added `ctx registry ls --missing`, but both live in the CLI — a user opening the dashboard at `localhost:8765` had no signal that their registry had accumulated tombstones (orphaned entries pointing at deleted worktrees or moved project folders). The hygiene loop was "remember to run a CLI command", which is exactly the kind of friction we already solved for the transient-vs-real classification in v0.8.31. This release adds a fourth additive segment to the existing "projects active" card subtext: `12 files indexed · +3 transient · +2 tombstones`. The `+2 tombstones` span carries a tooltip naming the right cleanup command (`ctx registry prune --missing`), closing the discovery loop without needing a separate UI element. Library layer: `ValueMetrics` gets one new default-zero field, `projects_missing_count: int = 0`; the aggregator's existing `for entry in projects` loop adds one branch (`if not entry.root.exists(): missing_count += 1`) — single `stat` per registered root, amortized inside a loop that already does per-entry work. UI layer: extend the existing transient-subtext conditional to chain a second optional segment — single line of Jinja with two independent `{% if %}` blocks (neither, one, the other, or both — four cases, no template bloat). Single counter (not split by kind) — tombstone classification is independent of why-it-was-registered classification, and the prune action is the same for both kinds (`prune --missing` ignores `--kind` and `--older-than`). Splitting the counter would force the user to learn a distinction before acting on a fix that doesn't care about it. Four new test invariants: zero-missing happy path (default-safe field stays at 0), counts a single missing root (`not entry.root.exists()` predicate fires), counts missing regardless of kind (a gone transient and a gone real project both contribute), empty registry returns zero (guards against divide-by-zero or sentinel surprises). Rejected alternatives: split the counter (cognitive surface vs zero UX win), separate "Registry hygiene" card (real estate cost without a payoff), show count when zero (visual noise — passive nudge only fires when there's something to act on), make the tombstone span clickable to trigger prune (violates v0.8.33 lock — destructive operations stay CLI-only), color the tombstone segment red (premature visual design — wait for usage feedback first). Scope locks: only one default-zero field added to `ValueMetrics` (no removed/renamed fields, no signature change on `collect_value_metrics`), no new SQL or file walks (FS check rides inside the existing per-entry loop), CLI surface unchanged (the dashboard surfaces the data; the CLI commands already shipped in v0.8.36–v0.8.38), no MCP surface (dashboard nudges, CLI mutates — same lock as v0.8.33), no new card / no grid reflow / no width change (the new segment composes inline). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.39-dashboard-tombstones.md).

**v0.8.38 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx registry prune --json` for scriptable cleanup. `ctx registry ls` has had `--json` since v0.8.32, but `ctx registry prune` has been text-only across v0.8.33 → v0.8.37 — an asymmetry CI hygiene scripts trip over: a nightly job that wants to detect registry drift and warn (`prune --kind transient | grep "would remove"`) is brittle to copy changes, and there's no clean way to count or process candidate roots without `awk`/`sed` parsing of human-readable output. The `PruneResult` dataclass has had every field a script needs (`kept`, `removed`, `applied`, `backup_path`, `config_path`) since v0.8.33; we just weren't exposing it. This release adds a `--json` flag on `prune_cmd` that emits the result as a JSON object — pure data, no hint text, no header lines, no "nothing to do" message. Composes with every existing flag: `prune --json` (preview), `prune --json --yes` (live result with `applied=true` and `backup_path` populated), `prune --json --missing` (tombstone preview), `prune --json --kind real --older-than 60` (custom-policy preview). Schema is a 1:1 mirror of `PruneResult` — no flag echo, no derived fields, no metadata — giving scripts the smallest stable surface to bind against. CLI layer only: `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py::prune_cmd` adds `as_json: bool` flag and a new `_prune_result_to_json` helper that string-converts `Path` fields. Library layer **untouched** — `prune_stale` already returned the structured result; the JSON layer is purely a CLI rendering concern. Five new test invariants lock the contract: dry-run shape (exact key set + null backup), `--yes` shape (applied=true + backup_path populated + kept reflects post-mutation YAML), nothing-to-do (well-formed JSON with empty `removed`, no special-case empty stdout for scripts to guard), `--missing --json` composition, hint-text suppression (no `dry-run`, no `Pass --yes`, no `REMOVED`, no `nothing to do` — `json.loads(stdout)` succeeds on a single object). Rejected alternatives: echo invocation parameters in the JSON (brittle — schema would change with every new flag), NDJSON output (forces consumers to handle two record types — `.removed[]` already gives streaming row access in `jq`), separate `prune --plan` flag (conflates output format with semantics — `--json` is render switch, `--yes` is dry-run/apply axis), make `--json` imply `--yes` (scripts want **both** preview and apply — preview is the more common scripting case for CI checks), YAML output (worse scripting target than JSON — whitespace-sensitive, no canonical streaming parser in shell). Scope locks: library layer untouched, no registry schema change, no public signature change on `prune_stale` / `plan_prune` / `audit_registry` / `is_missing` / `is_stale`, default text output behavior unchanged (every existing assertion still holds), no new on-disk artifacts (JSON goes to stdout), no MCP surface (destructive operations stay CLI-only, same lock as v0.8.33). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.38-prune-json.md).

**v0.8.37 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx registry ls --missing` for tombstone audit. v0.8.36 shipped `ctx registry prune --missing` so users can clean up tombstones (registry entries whose root directory no longer exists on disk) — but there was no matching **read** surface to preview which entries would be removed before running the destructive command. Users had to shell out (`ctx registry ls --json | jq` → `test -d` loop). And in the default text output, a tombstone was indistinguishable from a merely-unscanned project — both showed `SCAN=no`. This release adds: (1) a `--missing` flag on `ctx registry ls` that filters to absent-root entries; (2) an additive `missing: bool` field on every `ProjectAudit` / `ls --json` row; (3) a `MISS` marker in the `SCAN` column of the default text table so tombstones are visible without the flag. `--missing` on `ls` **composes** with `--kind` and `--stale` as AND (`ls --missing --kind transient` = transient tombstones; `ls --missing --stale` = intersection of both predicates) — intentionally different from `prune --missing` which ignores those flags for safety. Justified asymmetry: read-only composability is strictly additive value with no footgun, while a mutation command with silently-compositional flags risks a stray `--kind real` in shell history leaving transient tombstones behind. Library layer: `libs/status/registry_audit.py` — `ProjectAudit` gains `missing: bool = False`; `audit_registry` sets it via `not entry.root.exists()` and short-circuits `scanned`/`packs_*` so a tombstone row doesn't stat inside a ghost parent; new `is_missing(row) -> bool` helper mirrors the `is_stale(row)` shape. CLI layer: `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py::ls_cmd` adds `--missing`; `_apply_filters` gains a `missing: bool` parameter composed as AND; `_render_text` surfaces `MISS` in the `SCAN` column when `missing=True`. Nine new test invariants lock the contract: 4 library-layer (missing flag populated for absent roots, tombstone row reports `scanned=False` + zero packs, `is_missing` returns the flag, missing/stale are independent), 5 CLI-layer (`ls --missing --json` filters to tombstones, text `MISS` marker, composes with `--kind`, empty when all roots exist, every `ls --json` row carries the `missing` field). Rejected alternatives: dedicated `MISS` column (extra width for a ~1 % signal — overloading `SCAN=MISS` reads at a glance and keeps the table in 120 cols), `--kind missing` overload (same v0.8.36 argument — `--kind` is a classification axis, not eligibility), making `prune --missing` also compose with `--kind` (rejected in v0.8.36 for safety, stays rejected — asymmetry is correct), lazy `Path.exists()` recomputation in `_apply_filters` (would stat twice per render — storing once in `audit_registry` keeps `is_missing` O(1) and gives JSON the signal for free), `missing_count` summary header (rare information doesn't justify a header line — trivial to compute with `jq length`). Scope locks: no registry schema change, `ProjectAudit.missing` has a safe default so existing code paths see no behavior change, default `ls` output unchanged except for the additive `MISS` marker (same layout, same column width), no mutation path touched, no MCP surface (CLI-only, same lock as v0.8.32). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.37-ls-missing.md).

**v0.8.36 (2026-04-25)** — `ctx registry prune --missing` for absent-root cleanup. v0.8.33 gated pruning on staleness (`packs_total=0 AND last_scan>30d`) and kind (real/transient/all) — which works for entries whose *scanning* is dormant but whose *directory* still exists on disk. It misses a common failure mode: a worktree deleted the same day (`git worktree remove`, `rm -rf /tmp/scratch`, a project folder moved across a drive) turns into a **tombstone** — path gone, staleness gate doesn't fire for 30 days, `ctx status` keeps pinging a dead filesystem root. v0.8.35 prevents *new* transient accrual, but existing tombstones still need a catch-up command. This release adds a `--missing` flag on `ctx registry prune` that treats root-directory absence (`Path(entry.root).exists() is False`) as an **independent** eligibility predicate — ignores `--older-than` (a gone root is gone regardless of age), ignores `--kind` (a gone transient and a gone real project are equally dead), preserves the v0.8.33 safety contract (dry-run default, `--yes` gate, pre-mutation `*.bak` sidecar, atomic `save_config`). Layering kept: library-layer logic in `libs/status/registry_prune.py` (`plan_prune` and `prune_stale` gain a `missing_only: bool = False` kwarg — when `True`, the candidate filter checks `Path(row.root).exists()` and short-circuits past the `older_than_days` / `kind` branches), thin Typer shell in `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py::prune_cmd` adds `--missing` alongside `--older-than` / `--kind` / `--yes`, output copy reports `missing root` vs `>Nd` on the nothing-to-do / candidates path. Eight new test invariants lock the contract (5 library-layer, 3 CLI-layer): `test_plan_prune_missing_lists_absent_roots` (the predicate catches deleted paths while sparing live directories), `test_prune_missing_ignores_older_than_gate` (a worktree registered this morning, scanned at 9 a.m., deleted at noon: staleness-mode returns `[]`, missing-mode returns it), `test_prune_missing_ignores_kind_filter` (both a gone-real and a gone-transient entry are caught even with `kind="transient"`), `test_prune_missing_applies_with_backup` (`apply=True` mutates exactly the gone entries and writes `*.bak` with the pre-mutation bytes), `test_prune_missing_no_candidates_is_graceful` (when every root exists, missing-mode is a pure read), `test_registry_prune_missing_dry_run_lists_deleted_root` (CLI dry-run prints `missing root` + `dry-run` and leaves config untouched), `test_registry_prune_missing_yes_removes_and_backs_up` (CLI `--yes` applies + reports `REMOVED` + `backup saved`), `test_registry_prune_missing_nothing_to_do` (CLI no-op path prints the `missing root` variant of the nothing-to-do message). Rejected alternatives: auto-prune on every `ctx status` / daemon wake (hidden destructive behavior — the v0.8.33 dry-run-by-default contract is the right UX, the user chooses when to apply), `.context/cache.db` existence instead of root directory (a user who runs `rm -rf /path/to/proj/.context` but keeps the project would lose their entry — root-directory absence is the correct signal), combined `--stale-or-missing` mode (overspecified — two independent flags, compose-mode added only if driven by a real use case), `Path(root).is_dir()` instead of `.exists()` (a regular-file tombstone from a stray `touch` is still a dead entry — `.exists()` catches both), gating `--missing` behind `--kind all` (friction for the common case with no safety win — `--yes` is already the mutation gate). Scope locks: no registry schema change, no public signature change on read-side helpers (`audit_registry`, `is_stale`, `list_projects`, `save_config`), default behavior of `ctx registry prune` without `--missing` is unchanged, no new on-disk artifacts (only the v0.8.33 `*.bak` sidecar), no `ctx registry ls --missing` yet (symmetric read-side surface is a plausible follow-up, but `ls --json | jq '.[] | select(...)'` already handles the use case). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-25-v0.8.36-prune-missing-roots.md).

**v0.8.35 (2026-04-24)** — Skip transient paths on auto-registration. Structural follow-up to v0.8.31 (which classified transient projects on the dashboard), v0.8.32 (`ctx registry ls` to audit them), and v0.8.33 (`ctx registry prune` to clean them): this release prevents the pollution at the write path instead of forever chasing it at the read path. `_is_transient` moves from the private status helper to public `is_transient` in `libs/core/projects_config` (pure pathlib, still stdlib + pydantic-only so the core-layer contract holds), and `apps.agent.config.add_project` gains an `allow_transient: bool = False` kwarg — when `False` (the default) and the resolved path matches `.claude/worktrees/*` or basename `sample_repo`, registration silently returns. `ctx scan`'s `_auto_register` keeps the default and therefore stops growing the registry from inside ship-ceremony worktrees or when tests happen to auto-register the `sample_repo` fixture. `ctx watch add` explicitly passes `allow_transient=True` because that command is explicit user intent — silently refusing the user's own command would be a worse UX bug than the audit noise we're preventing. Layering respected: classifier in `libs/core` (shared by the write path and the audit/metrics readers — `libs/status/value_metrics.py` and `libs/status/registry_audit.py` now import the canonical name, with `_is_transient` kept as a one-line backward-compat alias inside `value_metrics`); domain helper in `apps/agent/config` where the single-writer rule lives. Six new test invariants: `add_project` default-off drops worktree paths, default-off drops `sample_repo`, `allow_transient=True` overrides the filter, normal paths still register without the flag, `ctx scan._auto_register` silently skips worktrees, `ctx watch add <worktree>` still registers when invoked explicitly. Rejected alternatives: silently tag entries as `kind=transient` (still pollutes YAML, still needs periodic prune), filter only worktrees and leave fixtures alone (both patterns produce identical noise), hard-block transient paths with a stderr warning (breaks the legitimate `ctx watch add <worktree>` debugging workflow), require `.git` for every registration (too strict — LV_DCP supports non-Git projects by design). No registry schema change, no public signature change on `list_projects` / `save_config` / `remove_project` / `update_last_scan`, no migration (existing transient entries can be cleaned with `ctx registry prune --yes` which already shipped in v0.8.33). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.35-skip-transient-auto-register.md).

**v0.8.34 (2026-04-24)** — single atomic write path for `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml`. While shipping v0.8.33's `ctx registry prune` I noticed two `save_config()` implementations — the v0.8.33 one in `libs/core/projects_config.py` (atomic: tmp + `fsync` + `rename`) and an older one in `apps/agent/config.py` (non-atomic `path.write_text`). The older one was the actual writer for every code path except prune: daemon scan completion via `update_last_scan`, `add_project`/`remove_project`, CLI setup wizard, UI settings form. So the registry was being written non-atomically dozens of times per day while the atomic path was used once a month during prune. A crash or OOM kill mid-write could leave truncated YAML and wipe out the user's entire project registry on next boot. This release unifies to a single atomic writer: `apps/agent/config.py` now re-exports `save_config` from `libs/core`, the chmod 0o600 moves into the shared impl wrapped in `contextlib.suppress(OSError)` (skips on filesystems without POSIX perms instead of crashing), and `yaml.safe_dump(..., allow_unicode=True)` from the v0.8.33 path propagates — so Cyrillic / emoji project names like `/Users/me/Проект_X5` now render as readable YAML instead of `\uXXXX` escapes. Five new test invariants lock the contract: chmod 0o600 on POSIX, original file preserved on simulated `Path.replace` failure, unicode round-trip, save survives chmod failure, and `apps.agent.config.save_config is libs.core.projects_config.save_config` — a one-liner that catches any future regression reintroducing a second writer. Full unit suite: **1289 passing** (+5 vs v0.8.33 baseline 1284). Rejected: keeping both implementations (divergence invites drift), promoting the non-atomic one (loses the property v0.8.33 needed), `fcntl.flock()` (overkill — registry is single-writer, atomic-rename is enough), moving the domain helpers down to `libs/core` (would pull `datetime.now()` and "register a project" semantics into the core layer, violating CLAUDE.md "libs/core зависит только от stdlib + pydantic"). No schema change, no public signature change, no migration needed — first write after upgrade is atomic. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.34-atomic-config-write.md).

**v0.8.33 (2026-04-24)** — `ctx registry prune` with dry-run default. v0.8.32 surfaced the pruning candidates via `ctx registry ls --stale`, but the user still had no safe remediation command — abandoned worktree entries had to be cleaned up via ad-hoc `yq`/`sed` scripts and the daemon kept waking up for dead projects. This release closes the loop: new `ctx registry prune` subcommand, gated by three independent safety layers — dry-run is the default (must pass `--yes` to mutate), the default `--kind` is `transient` (worktree artifacts and test fixtures — near-zero false-positive cost — real user projects require explicit `--kind real`), and a pre-mutation `*.bak` sidecar is written before the atomic rewrite starts so recovery is always a one-liner (`mv ~/.lvdcp/config.yaml{.bak,}`). Layered per CLAUDE.md: mutation logic lives in a new `libs/status/registry_prune.py` (`plan_prune`, `prune_stale`, `PruneResult`) so `registry_audit.py` stays read-only per its docstring invariant; `libs/core/projects_config.py` gains a new `save_config()` helper with atomic tmp + `fsync` + `rename` + temp-file cleanup on error; `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py` appends the thin Typer shell. 16 new tests across three test files — 8 library-layer cases (dry-run is a byte-level no-op, `apply=True` removes matching entries and writes `*.bak` with the pre-mutation bytes verbatim, `--kind real` spares transient, `--kind all` prunes both buckets, `--older-than` respects recent scans, invalid kind raises `ValueError`, empty registry is graceful), 5 CLI-layer cases (default is dry-run, `--yes` applies, invalid `--kind` exits 2, `--older-than 0` exits 2, `--kind real` against transient-only stale set reports "nothing to do"), 3 core-layer cases for `save_config` (round-trips, no `*.tmp` leak, overwrites existing atomically). Full unit suite: **1284 passing**. Scope locks: only registry entries are removed (no filesystem mutation on the project roots themselves), no `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml` schema change, no MCP surface (destructive operations should never be reachable via a Claude-invokable tool), survivor entries keep their original ordering. Rejected alternatives: auto-prune on scan (too invasive — the user should decide what leaves the registry), `--force` instead of `--yes` (`--yes` matches `apt` / `brew` muscle memory), in-place rewrite without backup (one 2 KB sidecar is free insurance), `typer.confirm` prompt (breaks non-interactive CI / hook usage), cascade-delete of `.context/` dirs of pruned projects (separate concern — future `ctx registry clean`). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.33-registry-prune.md).

**v0.8.32 (2026-04-24)** — `ctx registry ls` for auditing registered projects. v0.8.31 surfaced the real-vs-transient split on the dashboard but left operators without a terminal-native way to audit the registry — no scripting, no staleness filter, no JSON export. This release adds a `ctx registry ls` command group with one subcommand and three flags: `--kind real|transient|all` (filter by classification), `--stale` (surface dormant candidates — packs_total=0 AND last_scan>30d, or never scanned), `--json` (machine-readable for scripts). Output columns: `NAME  KIND  SCAN  7D  TOTAL  LASTSCAN  PATH`. Each row combines the registry entry with live signals (`.context/cache.db` existence, retrieval_traces counts, ISO-parsed scan age). Layered correctly per CLAUDE.md: pure logic in `libs/status/registry_audit.py` (`audit_registry(config_path)` → `list[ProjectAudit]`, `is_stale(row, older_than_days=30)`), thin Typer shell in `apps/cli/commands/registry_cmd.py` renders text/JSON and applies filters. Reuses the v0.8.31 `_is_transient` classifier as single source of truth. 12 new tests cover the lib layer (6, deterministic with injected `now`) and the CLI layer (6, via `typer.testing.CliRunner`). Scope locks: **no mutation** (no prune, no rm, no update — those need an explicit ACK release), no schema change to `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml`, no MCP surface (operator CLI, not a tool for Claude), ordering follows the YAML file to preserve user mental map. Rejected alternatives (see design note): `ctx project ls` (name clash), `ctx scan --dry` (wrong surface), putting logic in `value_metrics.py` (single-responsibility violation), `--prune --yes` (deferred — pruning is destructive). See [v0.8.32 design note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.32-ctx-registry-ls.md) for dogfood output and follow-up list.

**v0.8.31 (2026-04-24)** — Value metrics: separate transient from real projects. The dashboard "projects active" card has been reading straight off `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml`, so every ship-ceremony `.claude/worktrees/*` clone and every `tests/fixtures/sample_repo` scan inflated the denominator. On my own workspace that produced `18/79 active`, which made the card useless for reading adoption. This release adds four additive fields to `ValueMetrics` — `projects_real_active`, `projects_real_total`, `projects_transient_active`, `projects_transient_total` — and a narrow `_is_transient(root)` classifier (two rules: `.claude/worktrees/*` segment pair, or basename `sample_repo`). The dashboard card now binds to the real-project counters and, when any transient entries exist, appends a `· +N transient` subtext so the noise stays auditable without leading. Existing `projects_total` / `projects_active` semantics unchanged — purely additive, no downstream consumer breaks. Six new `tests/unit/status/test_value_metrics.py` asserts cover the classifier and the counter split. Scope locks: no registry pruning (destructive, needs user confirmation — flagged as follow-up), no MCP contract change (no user story yet for exposing these fields on `lvdcp_status`), per-project coverage table still shows every row (transient rows are useful when debugging scans). See [v0.8.31 design note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.31-value-metrics-transient-split.md) for the rejected classifiers (path-age heuristic, registry-flag-at-scan-time) and the explicit follow-ups.

**v0.8.30 (2026-04-24)** — VS Code extension activation-event narrowing. Phase 10 polish item from the v0.8.29 roadmap. The extension always declared `"activationEvents": ["onStartupFinished"]`, which fires on every VS Code cold start — so the "LV_DCP" status bar item appeared in every window, even for projects that had nothing to do with LV_DCP (a web frontend scratch repo, a friend's Elm project, a dotfiles folder). This release narrows activation to `workspaceContains:**/.context/cache.db` — the canonical LV_DCP marker every indexed project has and no non-indexed project has. Indexed workspaces keep everything (status bar, sidebar, commands); non-indexed workspaces see nothing until the user runs a command. Command Palette invocation still works everywhere thanks to VS Code ≥1.74's implicit command activation — we drop `onStartupFinished` entirely, commands register on-demand. Alternatives rejected: `workspaceContains:.context/cache.db` (no `**/`) would miss monorepos where the index lives in a subdirectory; `onLanguage:python` + six more would still fire for every non-LV_DCP Python project; pure `onCommand:` would lose the status-bar affordance entirely. The activity-bar icon stays always-visible on purpose — it's a `contributes.viewsContainers` declaration, not activation-gated, and making it conditional would hurt discoverability in freshly-scanned projects. The noisier status-bar item is the surface we actually care about narrowing. Contract-locked by 6 new `tests/unit/vscode/test_extension_manifest.py` asserts: required marketplace fields, exact `activationEvents` value, explicit negative on `onStartupFinished`, both commands still contributed, engine floor `>=1.74` (so implicit command activation stays valid), extension version `>=0.8.30`. Pure JSON parse — no `npm`, no `@vscode/test-electron`, 0.02s in CI. Pure manifest change, no TypeScript edit, no `out/` rebuild (the published `.vsix` rebuilds on `vsce publish` anyway). Extension version jumps 0.8.27→0.8.30 (v0.8.28/v0.8.29 were backend-only, no extension bump). Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.30-vscode-activation.md).

**v0.8.29 (2026-04-24)** — Obsidian sync observability on the project card. v0.8.28 shipped `ctx obsidian sync-all` but the dashboard still only reported `last scan: Xmin ago` — a user who armed the nightly sweep via `launchd`/`cron` had no way to confirm from the UI that last night's run actually fired. The `.context/obsidian_last_sync` marker was already on disk (one file, two writers: the after-scan daemon worker and `sync-all`), so this is a pure read-side follow-through: `HealthCard` gains two nullable fields (`obsidian_last_sync_at_iso`, `obsidian_sync_age_hours`) populated by `build_health_card()` through a new `_read_obsidian_sync()` helper that degrades gracefully on missing / unreadable / non-float markers (returns `(None, None)` instead of raising — a corrupt marker can't take down the status aggregation that renders every project card) and clamps future timestamps to zero so clock skew never produces `-0.3h ago`. The helper accepts an injected `now` so tests stay deterministic without `freezegun`. Two fields rather than one because the ISO timestamp goes into the `<time datetime=…>` attribute for browser localization while the precomputed `age_hours` keeps the Jinja template free of datetime math. The `apps/ui/templates/partials/health_card.html.j2` partial wraps the new row in `{% if card.obsidian_last_sync_at_iso %}` so projects that never synced render exactly like before — no CSS change, no layout change, one row appears under the existing `last scan` line when (and only when) there's data. Age formatter picks the right unit for the mental model: `<1h ago` / `Nh ago` (1–48h, whole hours) / `Nd ago` (≥48h, whole days); minute precision is noise when the sync is debounced at 1h anyway. `lvdcp_status` MCP tool gets the new fields free because `HealthCard` is shared — no MCP schema migration needed. No colour-coded staleness banner (unlike `last scan`'s 24h stale banner): different projects reasonably have different sync cadences (weekly vs daily) and a global 24h threshold would generate noisy banners on perfectly healthy projects. Ships as `libs/status/models.py` + `libs/status/health.py` + one Jinja partial + 6 new unit tests covering missing marker, fresh (~2h), old (~72h), garbage contents, future timestamp, injected-`now` helper. Full docs in [release note](docs/release/2026-04-24-v0.8.29-obsidian-observability.md).

**v0.8.28 (2026-04-24)** — Obsidian nightly sync (`ctx obsidian sync-all`). Closes the last Phase 10 non-parser item on the v0.8.27 roadmap. The Obsidian publisher has been live since Phase 2 wired two ways: manual (`ctx obsidian sync <project> --vault <vault>`) and after-scan (daemon's `apps.agent.obsidian_worker.run_obsidian_sync()`, debounced by `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml:obsidian.debounce_seconds`, default 1h, via `.context/obsidian_last_sync`). Missing was **nightly** — the case where a project was scanned yesterday, the debounce elapsed, but no scan fired today, so the vault drifts. This release ships `ctx obsidian sync-all` which walks every project in `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml:projects`, decides which ones need a sync via a single `--stale-hours N` gate (default 24h; `0` force-syncs everything; missing/corrupt marker counts as stale because "registered but never synced" is the common first-run case), and shells out to `ctx obsidian sync` per project via `subprocess.run` with a `--timeout SECS` isolation (default 300s). `--dry-run` prints the plan (`sync` / `skip: no cache.db` / `skip: fresh (Xh old)` per project) without invoking the inner CLI — essential for arming launchd/cron without silent misconfigurations. One flaky project doesn't block the others: the loop catches `CalledProcessError` / `TimeoutExpired` / `OSError` per project and continues; exit code is `1` iff any project failed, with "`Synced: N, skipped: N, failed: N`" on stdout. On success the same `.context/obsidian_last_sync` marker the after-scan worker uses gets advanced, so the daemon won't re-fire inside its own debounce window after the nightly run — one marker, two writers, same gate. Design choice lock: the repo ships the command, **not** the schedule. LV_DCP's constitution (§I.3 and CLAUDE.md Принцип 5) is "local-first, minimal moving parts, modular monolith not microservices, простота эксплуатации превыше модной архитектуры" — an in-process scheduler inside the daemon is an extra moving part that fires only when the daemon runs (laptop closed = no sync), while launchd/cron is the macOS-native way and already what every power user trusts for scheduled jobs. The release note documents the two canonical setups: a launchd `StartCalendarInterval` at 03:00 and a `0 3 * * *` crontab, both pointing at `/path/to/LV_DCP/.venv/bin/ctx obsidian sync-all`. Neither is installed by the LV_DCP installer — `ctx mcp install` touches `~/.claude/` because that's Claude's territory, a scheduled daemon touching `~/Library/LaunchAgents/` is a different trust level that the user should own explicitly. Helper shape: `_read_last_sync(project_root)` reads the marker as `float | None` (corrupt file → None, silently treated as stale), `_is_stale(project_root, stale_seconds, now)` combines the missing-marker-is-stale and `stale_seconds <= 0 = force` branches into one gate, `@app.command("sync-all")` validates config (missing file / disabled / empty `vault_path` / no projects all exit cleanly or with a typed error), builds a plan of `(root, reason)` tuples, branches on `--dry-run`, and for the live path writes the marker only after a zero-return-code `subprocess.run`. 18 new tests in `tests/unit/cli/test_obsidian_sync_all.py`: config validation (missing config file exits 1, disabled exits 0, empty vault_path exits 1, no projects exits 0), dry-run plan (fresh project shows `sync`, cacheless shows `skip: no cache.db`, recently-synced shows `skip: fresh (Xh old)`, `--stale-hours 0` forces sync even on fresh projects), live sync (subprocess invoked with correct args + marker advanced, fresh project skipped with `mock_run.assert_not_called()`, mixed stale/fresh respects the gate and calls subprocess exactly once with the stale project's path, subprocess failure on one of two projects exits 1 but both are attempted and the succeeded one gets its marker while the failed one doesn't, `TimeoutExpired` treated as failure, nonexistent-project-root skipped not crashed), plus a parametrized `_is_stale` invariant locking never-synced/fresh/stale/force-hours-zero semantics. Zero changes to the daemon, zero changes to the publisher, zero changes to the after-scan worker — all new code lives in `apps/cli/commands/obsidian_cmd.py`. Full Python suite: **1405 passing** (+18 vs v0.8.27 baseline 1388). Ruff clean, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean. Known limits: sequential not parallel (one subprocess at a time — 20-project sweeps run in well under a minute on warm SQLite, parallelization would need a shared vault-lock strategy, deferred until >60 registered projects); no per-project interval override (the `--stale-hours` gate is global — "small projects nightly, big project weekly" would need two launchd entries with two `--config` files, deemed low-priority); no built-in scheduler (deliberate — the day a Windows/Linux user hits this and the `launchd` path doesn't apply, a `ctx watch install-service`-style subcommand becomes the natural follow-up); exit-code granularity is `0` or `1`, no "`2` means partial" — scripts that care about failure counts parse the `"failed: N"` tail line; ~20 ms of Python startup per project via `subprocess.run` (irrelevant for nightly, a future in-process path would lose the timeout-isolation + error-isolation properties that are the whole point of the shelling-out design).

**v0.8.27 (2026-04-24)** — VS Code extension user-configurable settings. Follow-up to v0.8.26, which shipped the marketplace metadata but called out three explicit scope-locks as known gaps — one of them was "no extension settings (`lvdcp.cliPath`, backend URL — users running `ctx` via `uv run` need a wrapper shell for now, future increment will add `configuration` contribution points)". This release closes that gap. Three settings land under `lvdcp.*` in VS Code's Settings UI via a new `contributes.configuration` block on `apps/vscode/package.json`: `lvdcp.cliPath` (default `"ctx"`) — path to the `ctx` executable, unblocks users whose `ctx` isn't on `PATH` (e.g. running the CLI via `uv run python -m apps.cli` via a wrapper script); `lvdcp.defaultMode` (default `"navigate"`, enum `"navigate" | "edit"`) — default retrieval mode for `LV_DCP: Get Context Pack` (the separate `LV_DCP: Show Impact` command continues to force `"edit"` regardless, since that command's entire purpose is impact-aware ranking and overriding it would make the two commands indistinguishable); `lvdcp.cliTimeoutMs` (default `30000`, range `1000`–`300000`) — timeout for `ctx` subprocess calls, previously hardcoded to 30s in `getContextPack` and 15s in `getInspect` (now unified to one user-configurable value). `apps/vscode/src/ctxClient.ts` refactored to take an explicit `CtxConfig` interface `{cliPath: string; timeoutMs: number}` as a required parameter on both `getContextPack` and `getInspect` instead of implicit `ctx` PATH lookup and hardcoded timeouts — pure signature change, no behaviour drift at the defaults. `apps/vscode/src/extension.ts` gains two tiny readers `readCtxConfig()` and `readDefaultMode()` that call `vscode.workspace.getConfiguration("lvdcp")` per command invocation, so edits in VS Code's Settings UI take effect without extension reload (the `getConfiguration` call is cheap and returns a live view; caching would break the live-edit UX for zero wins). `readDefaultMode` narrows the string from the config to the literal union `"navigate" | "edit"` with a fallback to `"navigate"` on any unrecognised value, so a user who hand-edits `settings.json` and typos `"ediit"` doesn't crash the extension — they just get the default mode. Both commands pass the freshly-read config through; `Get Context Pack` uses `readDefaultMode()`, `Show Impact` keeps its hardcoded `"edit"`. No breaking change for anyone already on v0.8.26: all three settings have defaults that exactly reproduce the prior behaviour (`cliPath="ctx"`, `defaultMode="navigate"` was already the call-site default, `cliTimeoutMs=30000` matches the old `getContextPack` hardcode). `apps/vscode/README.md` gains a new "Settings" section with a three-row table and a concrete `uv run` wrapper-script example (`#!/usr/bin/env bash; exec uv run --project /path/to/LV_DCP python -m apps.cli "$@"` saved to `~/bin/ctx-lvdcp`, then `"lvdcp.cliPath": "/Users/you/bin/ctx-lvdcp"` in User Settings); the "Known limitations" section loses the "no extension settings" bullet since it's now false. `apps/vscode/CHANGELOG.md` gains a 0.8.27 entry. `npm run compile` clean; `npm run package` produces a **11.71 KB / 9-file** `.vsix` (up 0.69 KB from v0.8.26's 11.02 KB because `package.json` grew from 2.4 KB to 3.93 KB to carry the configuration schema — the only size driver, compiled JS grew by ~0.3 KB for the two readers). Full Python suite: **1388 passing** — unchanged vs v0.8.26 because this release touches only `apps/vscode/` TypeScript + root version files, no Python code. Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 380 files. Known limits: still no PNG marketplace icon (separate designer-gated increment); settings are read per-command-invocation, not subscribed-to — a user editing `cliPath` while a pack is mid-flight gets the old value for the in-flight call (rare corner case, not worth the `onDidChangeConfiguration` wiring complexity for v1); no `lvdcp.backendUrl` setting yet because the extension currently only shells out to `ctx` and `ctx` handles its own backend discovery via `.context/config.yaml` (the backend URL is a `ctx` concern, not an extension concern); not yet published to the Marketplace (requires user-level Publisher registration + PAT — same gate as v0.8.26).

**v0.8.26 (2026-04-24)** — VS Code extension marketplace-readiness prep. Pure metadata + packaging work; no backend or extension-runtime behaviour change. With the inheritance-edge axis closed across Java/Kotlin/Swift in v0.8.25, the next Phase 10 lane is VS Code Marketplace publication. The extension at `apps/vscode/` has been tracked in the repo since Phase 9 but has never been marketplace-ready — missing repository URL, keywords, categories, listing README, CHANGELOG, LICENSE file, and a tightened `.vscodeignore` (all required or surfaced by the Marketplace listing page). This release closes those gaps so that a future `vsce publish` is a one-command operation for the maintainer once the Publisher account is registered and a PAT is provisioned. Deliberately does **not** publish (requires creating a Publisher on the Microsoft Marketplace and an Azure DevOps Personal Access Token — both user-level actions outside the project) and deliberately does **not** add a PNG icon (needs a designer's call on branding; the activity-bar icon uses the built-in `$(symbol-structure)` codicon, sufficient for in-VS-Code UX). `apps/vscode/package.json` gained 9 new top-level fields: `license: "Apache-2.0"`, `homepage`, `repository` (with `directory: "apps/vscode"` hint so the Marketplace points at the extension subdir not the repo root), `bugs`, `keywords` (10 terms optimised for Marketplace search weighting), expanded `categories` from `["Other"]` to `["Programming Languages", "Machine Learning", "Other"]` because the bare `"Other"` bucket has 30k+ entries and gives near-zero discoverability, `galleryBanner` (dark theme matching VS Code default), `qna` (routes questions to GitHub Discussions instead of the Marketplace's built-in Q&A which we'd have to monitor separately), and two scripts: `vscode:prepublish: "npm run compile"` (vsce runs this hook before packaging — without it a stale `out/` could ship) and `publish: "npx @vscode/vsce publish --no-dependencies"` (convenience wrapper). `apps/vscode/README.md` (new, ~60 lines) is the Marketplace's primary marketing surface — it renders directly on the listing page — with three-bullet summary, requirements, commands, local-first design philosophy, known limitations, and links; kept separate from the 500-line root README because the Marketplace audience is deciding whether to install, not reading full project context. `apps/vscode/CHANGELOG.md` (new, ~25 lines) renders on the listing's Changelog tab; entries for v0.8.23–0.8.26, with earlier versions pointing at the main repo release notes directory to avoid duplicating 500 KB of history. `apps/vscode/LICENSE` (new, repo copy) — the Marketplace's License link requires the file inside the packaged `.vsix`; linking to the repo LICENSE is not sufficient. `apps/vscode/.vscodeignore` expanded from 4 lines to 12: added `.vscode-test/`, `package-lock.json`, `.claude/`, `.github/`, `**/.DS_Store`, `**/*.map`, `**/*.log`, `**/*.tsbuildinfo`, `*.vsix` — prevents the built `.vsix` from bloating with source maps, lockfiles, worktree `.claude/` dir, and recursive `.vsix` self-references. Verified with `npm run package`: the resulting artifact is **11.02 KB / 9 files** (CHANGELOG.md, LICENSE.txt, README.md, package.json, + three compiled .js files) — no source maps, no `node_modules`, no `.ts` sources. Full release note includes a maintainer publishing runbook (register publisher on marketplace.visualstudio.com/manage, generate PAT with `Marketplace: Manage` scope, `export VSCE_PAT=<token>`, `npm run publish`) and documents the `lv-dcp` publisher-name contingency (fall back to `lukinvit` or `lv-dcp-oss` if taken). Full suite: **1388 passing** (+1 vs v0.8.25 because the previously-flaking Qdrant SSL test passed cleanly this run). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 380 source files. No new Python tests — release touches only `apps/vscode/` metadata and root version/README. Known limits: no PNG icon (future increment needs a designer call); no extension settings (`lvdcp.cliPath`, backend URL — users running `ctx` via `uv run` need a wrapper shell for now, future increment will add `configuration` contribution points); no marketplace screenshots (future increment when UX is photogenic); not yet published (requires user-level Publisher registration + PAT).

**v0.8.25 (2026-04-24)** — Swift `INHERITS` edges (single-colon heritage). Third and final deepening-increment on the inheritance-edge axis after v0.8.23 (Java) and v0.8.24 (Kotlin). With this ship, every tree-sitter parser on the platform that targets a language with a nominal class hierarchy (Java, Kotlin, Swift) emits `INHERITS` edges; Go and Rust have structural conformance rather than nominal inheritance, and the Python parser treats call-graph as its primary edge type with inheritance as a separate future pass. So this release closes the **inheritance-edge axis across language coverage**, not a single-parser gap. `SwiftParser.parse()` now overrides the base, calls it, then walks the CST a second time with a scope-aware stack to emit `Relation(relation_type=INHERITS)` edges for every heritage clause — same structural shape as the Java and Kotlin ports (`_TYPE_DECLARATION_NODES` frozenset, `parse()` override, `_extract_inherits()`, `_collect_heritage()`, `_user_type_name()`). The one structural difference from the JVM pair is that Swift has **no heritage wrapper node**: unlike Java's `super_interfaces` and Kotlin's `delegation_specifiers`, Swift places each `inheritance_specifier` as a direct sibling of the type name inside `class_declaration` / `protocol_declaration`, separated by `,` tokens. `_collect_heritage` therefore iterates `type_node.children` directly and picks out `inheritance_specifier` kinds, naturally filtering out non-heritage siblings (`type_parameters` on the source type, `type_constraints` for `where` clauses, `class_body` / `enum_class_body` / `protocol_body`, `:` / `,` tokens). Swift overloads the `:` heritage syntax across an unusually broad set of declarations — `class` / `struct` / `enum` / `actor` / `extension` (all under one unified `class_declaration` grammar node) plus `protocol_declaration` — and all six forms can carry heritage; every case lands on the same `RelationType.INHERITS` edge (class inheritance, struct/enum/actor protocol conformance, protocol composition, extension conformance). **Extensions are the interesting case**: `class_declaration` for an `extension User: P` has its `name` field set to the *extended* type (so `child_by_field_name("name").text == b"User"`), and the base walker from v0.8.22 already emits a duplicate CLASS symbol named `User` for every extension. This release's heritage walker therefore produces `<module>.User INHERITS P` for the conformance, which correctly matches the duplicate symbol's `fq_name` — a graph query for "does this codebase conform `User` to `Equatable`?" now answers yes whether the conformance is declared in `User`'s primary definition or in a retroactive `extension User: Equatable {}`, regardless of which file the extension lives in. That is the shape Swift users actually reason about. Type-name extraction: Swift's `user_type` grammar uses `type_identifier` (not Kotlin's `identifier`) for each dotted-path segment, with an optional trailing `type_arguments` child for generics. `_user_type_name` walks only direct `type_identifier` children and joins them with `.`, so `Container<String>` emits `"Container"`, `Comparable<Box<T>>` emits `"Comparable"`, and scoped paths like `pkg.lib.Deep<T>` emit `"pkg.lib.Deep"`. The `test_generic_type_arguments_stripped` invariant asserts `String` and type-parameter substitutions never surface as bases, and adds a `src != dst` guard that catches the `Box<T>: Comparable<Box<T>>` failure mode where a type parameter could leak its own name back through generics recursion. `where` clauses must not leak: `class Constrained<T>: Base where T: Hashable {}` places `type_constraints` as a sibling after the last `inheritance_specifier`, with an inner `inheritance_constraint → user_type` (`Hashable`) that's *syntactically* identical to a heritage entry but *semantically* a generic-parameter constraint, not an inheritance edge. The node-type filter in `_collect_heritage` excludes `type_constraints` naturally, so no `Constrained INHERITS Hashable` edge leaks — `test_where_clause_does_not_leak` locks this. Scope-aware walker is a structural clone of v0.8.23 Java / v0.8.24 Kotlin: `stack: list[tuple[Node, str]]` tracks `(node, enclosing_fq)`, type-declaration nodes compute `type_fq = f"{scope}.{name}"`, emit edges with `src_ref=type_fq`, and propagate `type_fq` as child scope — so `class Outer { class Inner: pkg.lib.Deep {} }` emits `<module>.Outer.Inner INHERITS pkg.lib.Deep` matching the symbol walker's own fq_name output, locked by `test_inherits_src_ref_matches_symbol_fq`. Design lock: `INHERITS` still collapses class inheritance + protocol conformance + extension conformance + protocol composition + enum raw-value bases — same "one edge type" decision as v0.8.23 Java and v0.8.24 Kotlin, same downstream-consumer audit-cost rationale (a future `CONFORMS_TO` sub-type would force Obsidian sync, pack enrichment, dashboard graph rendering to all decide the split with no driving use case). 17 new tests in `TestInheritsEdges` (single class inheritance, multi-protocol class conformance, struct conformance, protocol inherits-many, enum raw-value+protocol, actor conformance, extension conformance uses extended type, generic stripping with `src != dst` guard, scoped path preservation, nested class uses outer fq, where-clause does-not-leak, plain class has none, `src_ref` resolves-to-symbol invariant, relation-shape invariant, SPM module-fq respect, empty file, pre-v0.8.25 fixture regression guard on the v0.8.22 `SWIFT_CODE` showing `ViewController INHERITS UIViewController` + `User INHERITS CustomStringConvertible`). Full suite: **1387 passing** (+17 vs v0.8.24 baseline 1370). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 380 files. Known limits: `dst_ref` is a bare type name, not a fully-qualified symbol, so `: Data` after `import Foundation` emits `dst_ref="Data"` not `"Foundation.Data"` (import-based resolution is a separate graph-enrichment pass — same gap as Java / Kotlin); `typealias` and `associatedtype` declarations are not in `_symbol_type_map` and therefore cannot be INHERITS sources (future sub-increment); `deinit_declaration` has no name and is excluded from symbol emission; no `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges (same gap as Java / Kotlin / Go / Rust); `where`-clause conformances deliberately do not emit edges (constraint on `T`, not inheritance of `C`).

**v0.8.24 (2026-04-24)** — Kotlin `INHERITS` edges. Second deepening-increment after v0.8.23 closed the inheritance-edge gap for Java. v0.8.23 explicitly named Kotlin `INHERITS` as the next plausible sub-increment (shares the JVM parser family with Java, clearest heritage shape of the remaining two, TypeScript + Java already shipped the pattern in-codebase); this release delivers it. `KotlinParser.parse()` now overrides the base, calls it, then walks the CST a second time with a scope-aware stack to emit `Relation(relation_type=INHERITS)` edges for every heritage clause. Kotlin's single-colon syntax (`class Dog : Animal()`, `interface MyList : Collection<Int>, Iterable<Int>`, `object Singleton : Base(), Trait`) collapses Java's `extends` + `implements` onto one production — `delegation_specifiers` under `class_declaration` or `object_declaration` — and the grammar distinguishes three shapes inside each `delegation_specifier`: `user_type` directly (plain interface conformance, `: Trainable`), `constructor_invocation → user_type` (class extension with mandatory parentheses, `: Animal()`), and `explicit_delegation → user_type` (Kotlin-specific "implements by delegation", `: Iface by impl`). All three collapse onto a single `RelationType.INHERITS` edge — Kotlin has no syntactic class-vs-interface distinction at the heritage position (the declaration keyword carries it), so the graph consumer cannot distinguish them anyway, and keeping one edge type mirrors the v0.8.23 Java design. Explicit delegation deliberately emits INHERITS: impact-analysis queries like "what conforms to `Iface`?" should include `class Impl : Iface by x` — the delegation mechanism is a Kotlin implementation detail, but the is-a relation is real. Type-name extraction is simpler than Java's because Kotlin uses `user_type` uniformly — a flat sequence of `identifier` + `.` tokens with an optional trailing `type_arguments` child; `_user_type_name` walks only direct `identifier` children and joins them with `.`, so `type_arguments` is naturally ignored (no special-case filter needed) and `Container<String>` emits `"Container"` while `pkg.lib.Deep<String>` emits `"pkg.lib.Deep"`. The `test_generic_type_arguments_stripped` invariant asserts `String` / `Int` never surface as bases and adds a second guard — no edge has `src == dst` — which catches the specific failure mode where `Box<T>` could leak its own name through type-argument recursion. Scope-aware walker is a structural clone of v0.8.23 Java: `stack: list[tuple[Node, str]]` tracks `(node, enclosing_fq)`, type-declaration nodes compute `type_fq = f"{scope}.{name}"`, emit edges with `src_ref=type_fq`, and propagate `type_fq` as child scope — so `class Outer { class Inner : Base {} }` emits `<module>.Outer.Inner INHERITS Base` matching the symbol walker's own fq_name output, locked by `test_inherits_src_ref_matches_symbol_fq`. Intentional exclusions: **companion objects** (`class K { companion object : Holder }`) are excluded from `_TYPE_DECLARATION_NODES` because `companion_object` has no `name` field and the base walker does not emit a Symbol for it — emitting an edge would violate the `src_ref → symbol.fq_name` invariant; graph queries that want "which companions inherit from Holder?" are out of v1 scope and require first-classing companion objects as symbols. **Annotation classes** (`annotation class MyAnn`) are still `class_declaration` in the grammar with `annotation` inside `modifiers`, but Kotlin annotation classes cannot legally carry delegation specifiers and naturally produce zero edges with no explicit filter needed — `test_annotation_class_never_source` locks this as a positive regression test. Design lock: `INHERITS` still collapses class extension + interface conformance + explicit delegation — same "one edge type" decision as v0.8.23, same downstream-consumer audit-cost rationale. 20 new tests in `TestInheritsEdges` (single class extension, mixed extends+implements, interface multi-heritage, object heritage, enum class implements, data class heritage, sealed class heritage, explicit-delegation emits INHERITS, mixed extends+delegation+bare, generic stripping with `src != dst` guard, scoped path preservation, plain class has none, annotation class never source, nested class uses outer fq, companion object excluded, `src_ref` resolves-to-symbol invariant, relation-shape invariant, Gradle module-fq respect, empty file, pre-v0.8.24 fixture regression guard tolerating the `sealed class State` subclasses). Full suite: **1370 passing** (+20 vs v0.8.23 baseline 1350). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 173 source files. Known limits: only Kotlin closes in this release — Swift uses a different AST (`inheritance_specifier` under `class_declaration` / `protocol_declaration`) and is the next plausible sub-increment; `dst_ref` is a bare type name, not a fully-qualified symbol, so `: List<String>` after `import kotlin.collections.List` emits `dst_ref="List"` not `"kotlin.collections.List"` (import-based resolution is a separate graph-enrichment pass); companion-object heritage excluded per the fq-invariant; no `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges (same gap as Java / Swift / Go / Rust); typealiases (`typealias StringList = List<String>`) not tracked as inheritance (don't surface as symbols today).

**v0.8.23 (2026-04-24)** — Java `INHERITS` edges (`extends` / `implements`). First deepening-increment after Phase 10 closed its language-coverage axis in v0.8.22 (Java / Kotlin / Swift parsers all live). The three parsers all shipped with the same explicit v1 scope-lock — **no inheritance edges** — which was the right call at the time (kept each release reviewable, one language per commit) but left a concrete capability gap: without `extends` / `implements` edges the relation graph can tell you "file A imports file B" but not "class Child specialises class Parent", so impact analysis can't answer "what concrete subclasses of `AbstractHandler` exist?" or "if I change `AbstractHandler.process()`, what subclasses override it?" — the two questions where an inheritance edge is the only signal. Java is the natural first language to close the gap: oldest parser (shipped first in v0.8.20), most common JVM target, clearest tree-sitter heritage-clause structure of the three, and the TypeScript parser already emits `INHERITS` edges from `extends_clause` / `implements_clause` nodes — the pattern is proven in-codebase, not borrowed from a spec. `JavaParser` now overrides `parse()` to call the base `TreeSitterParser.parse()` first, then walks the CST a second time with a scope-aware stack to emit `Relation(relation_type=INHERITS)` edges for every `extends` / `implements` clause. Three heritage-clause shapes handled — `superclass` (class, single, `extends`), `super_interfaces` (class / enum / record, multi, `implements`), `extends_interfaces` (interface, multi, `extends`); `annotation_type_declaration` (`@interface`) cannot inherit and never appears as a source, kept off the allowlist explicitly. `_heritage_type_name(node)` handles the three type shapes the grammar produces inside a heritage clause: `type_identifier` → `"Parent"`, `scoped_type_identifier` → `"pkg.Outer.Inner"` (full dotted path preserved because the grammar exposes the whole chain as one node), `generic_type` → strip `type_arguments` and recurse on the first `type_identifier` / `scoped_type_identifier` child so `Container<String>` emits `"Container"` (not `"String"` or `"Container<String>"`) and `pkg.Box<Integer>` emits `"pkg.Box"`; the `test_generic_type_arguments_stripped` invariant asserts `String` / `Integer` never surface as bases, guarding against the naive "flatten all type_identifiers" mistake the TypeScript parser happens to use because TS type arguments are less commonly nested. Scope-aware source-ref: walker tracks `enclosing_fq` alongside each CST node on its work stack, so `class Outer { class Inner extends Base {} }` emits `<module>.Outer.Inner INHERITS Base` — crucially matching the `Symbol.fq_name` the base walker stores for `Inner` (the same `parent_fq.name` convention), locked by `test_inherits_src_ref_matches_symbol_fq` which asserts every INHERITS `src_ref` resolves to a symbol in the same file. This is an improvement over the TypeScript parser's current `module_fq.name` uniform shape (fine for flat TS files, incorrect for nested classes) — Java has a much stronger cultural habit of static nested classes (Builder patterns, sealed hierarchies), so the extra scope-tracking is worth the correctness. **Design lock: `INHERITS` collapses `extends` + `implements`.** Java distinguishes them at the syntax level (Kotlin unifies under `:`, Swift unifies under `:`) but in `libs.core.entities.RelationType` they all land on one `INHERITS` variant — the graph consumer asks "is-a" questions and treats interface conformance as inheritance for impact-analysis purposes. Adding an `IMPLEMENTS` enum variant is a plausible future refinement if a consumer asks "strictly-subclass" vs. "strictly-implements" separately, but doing so now forces downstream consumers (Obsidian wiki sync, context pack enrichment, dashboard graph rendering) to decide the same split with no driving use case. 17 new tests in a new `TestInheritsEdges` class in `tests/unit/parsers/test_java_parser.py`: single `extends`, multi `implements`, generic stripping, scoped path preservation, scoped generic stripping, interface multi-`extends`, enum multi-`implements`, record `implements`, plain-class has-none, annotation-type never-source, nested-inner + nested-static class uses-outer-fq, src_ref-resolves-to-symbol invariant, relation-shape invariant, maven-module-fq respect, empty file, pre-v0.8.23 fixture regression guard. Full suite: **1350 passing** (+17 vs v0.8.22 baseline 1333). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 173 source files. Known limits for v0.8.23 (explicit scope locks): only Java is ported — Kotlin (`class Foo : Base()`, `object X : Interface`) and Swift (`class Foo: Base, P`, `struct S: P, Q`) use different heritage syntax and are separate sub-increments (next plausible increments); `dst_ref` is a bare type name, not a fully-qualified symbol, so `extends List<String>` after `import java.util.List` emits `dst_ref="List"` not `"java.util.List"` — resolving bare names against the file's import list is a separate graph-enrichment pass; no `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges yet (same gap as all non-Python parsers); record components (`record Point(int x, int y)`) still don't surface as individual `VARIABLE` symbols (live under `formal_parameters`, not `field_declaration` — orthogonal to inheritance edges).

**v0.8.22 (2026-04-24)** — Swift tree-sitter parser. Third shipped increment of Phase 10 and the one that closes the phase's language-coverage axis: v0.8.20 brought Java, v0.8.21 brought Kotlin, and Swift — the third language named in the Phase 10 opener — was the remaining parser target. `libs/parsers/swift.py` is a ~130-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "swift"` and hook overrides for `_get_ts_language` (binds `tree_sitter_swift.language()` via the published `tree-sitter-swift>=0.0.1` wheel — the low version number reflects packaging age, not grammar maturity; the upstream alex-pinkus grammar is well-maintained), `_symbol_type_map` (six node kinds — `class_declaration` collapses `class` / `struct` / `actor` / `enum` / `extension` onto `SymbolType.CLASS` because the Swift grammar uses one unified AST node for all five declaration forms and distinguishes them via leading-keyword children; `protocol_declaration` is a distinct node kind → `SymbolType.CLASS`; `function_declaration`, `init_declaration`, and `protocol_function_declaration` — the grammar uses a separate node kind for method declarations inside protocol bodies vs. regular function declarations elsewhere — all map to `SymbolType.METHOD`;
