`property_declaration` → `SymbolType.VARIABLE`), `_import_node_types` (`{"import_declaration"}`), `_detect_role` (directory signals walked first — SPM conventions `Sources/` and `Tests/` as path fragments and prefixes, plus generic `/Tests/` / `/tests/` / `/Test/` / `/test/` fallbacks for Xcode project layouts — then filename fallback strips `.swift` before checking `*Tests` / `*Test` suffix or `Test*` prefix so `MyAppTests/LoginTest.swift` and bare `LoginTest.swift` both classify as `test` without relying on the directory), `_extract_import_ref` (walks children for the first `identifier` and returns its text — naturally handles both plain `import Foundation` → `Foundation` and scoped `import class Foundation.NSData` → `Foundation.NSData` because the grammar exposes the full dotted path on a single identifier node regardless of whether the `import` keyword is followed by a declaration-kind modifier; emitted as `dst_type="module"`), and static `_module_fq` (strips `.swift`, then finds `/Sources/` or `/Tests/` anywhere in the path or as a startswith prefix, skips one target-name segment because SPM nests files under `Sources/<TargetName>/...` and the target name is a build-system convention not part of the symbol's module identity, and dots the remainder — so `Sources/MyLib/Utils/Parser.swift` correctly derives `Utils.Parser`, `modules/foo/Sources/MyLib/Parser.swift` correctly derives `Parser`, and bare / Xcode-style paths like `MyApp/Foo.swift` fall back to `MyApp.Foo` and a standalone `Foo.swift` falls back to `Foo`). Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains `.swift → swift` extension map and `"swift": SwiftParser()` in `_PARSERS`; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"swift"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES` so indexed Swift files count toward symbol-extraction coverage metrics; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"swift"` to `_SRC_LANGS` so Swift files count toward the parseable-source-files denominator in per-project coverage percentages. Design choices locked by test for v1: extensions emit an apparent duplicate `CLASS` symbol for the extended type (`extension User: Codable { ... }` yields a symbol named `"User"`), chosen over overriding `_extract_name` to suppress the duplicate because it's semantically correct — the graph then records every file touching `User` and methods inside the extension correctly land with `parent_fq_name = <module>.User`, with `test_extension_emits_duplicate_class_symbol` and `test_extension_method_parent_is_extended_type` locking the invariant; `static let MAX_SIZE = 1024` maps to `VARIABLE` uniformly rather than `CONSTANT` (parity with the Java v1 decision for `static final` and the Kotlin v1 decision for `const val` — promoting either requires modifier-child inspection at parse time, documented as a deliberate v1 scope limit so a future promotion is an explicit contract break); protocol methods use the distinct `protocol_function_declaration` node kind and are explicitly mapped to `METHOD` so protocol body method signatures surface identically to class methods; `protocol_property_declaration` is intentionally **not** in the map for v1 — the grammar returns an awkward name including the `var` keyword that would need post-processing, documented as a plausible sub-increment; the parser does not yet emit `INHERITS` edges for inheritance / protocol conformance (`class Foo: Base, P`, `struct Bar: P, Q`) nor `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges for function invocations — same v1 posture as the Java and Kotlin parsers, same rationale (not yet generalized from the Python parser), listed as plausible future sub-increments if a driving use case arrives; `typealias`, `deinit`, and `enum_case` nodes are also out of scope for v1. 43 new tests across six classes in `tests/unit/parsers/test_swift_parser.py`: **15 symbol-extraction** (struct / class / enum / protocol / actor / extension-duplicate-invariant / top-level function / method-inside-class / `init` / protocol method / property / top-level property / `static let` → `VARIABLE` / extension-member parent-fq-name invariant / enum-method nesting), **3 import-relations** (plain imports / scoped imports surface the full dotted path / `dst_type == "module"` invariant), **10 role-detection** (SPM `Sources/` / bare repo root / SPM `Tests/` / nested multi-package `Tests/` / lowercase `tests/` / `*Test.swift` suffix / `*Tests.swift` suffix / `Test*.swift` prefix / Xcode `AppNameTests/` companion-directory layout / source-wins fallback when nothing matches), **8 module-FQ derivation** (SPM `Sources/<Target>/` strip / SPM `Tests/<Target>/` strip / nested subdir dotting / nested multi-package `modules/foo/Sources/MyLib/...` strip / `Sources/` without target subdir graceful degradation / bare dotted path / bare root / `.swift` extension strip), **3 edge cases** (minimal single-struct file / empty file emits zero symbols without tree-sitter errors — asserted via `list(result.symbols) == []` because `symbols` is a tuple / `ParseResult.language == "swift"`), and **4 registry-wiring tests** (bare `.swift` / SPM-pathed `.swift` / `get_parser("swift")` returns a `SwiftParser` instance / `SwiftParser().language == "swift"`). Full suite: **1334 passing** (+43 vs v0.8.21 baseline 1291). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 380 files. With Java (v0.8.20), Kotlin (v0.8.21), and Swift (v0.8.22) shipped, Phase 10's language-coverage axis is complete; remaining Phase 10 work is VS Code marketplace publication and Obsidian nightly sync. Sub-increments deepening language support (inheritance edges for Java / Kotlin / Swift, record / data-class / primary-constructor / property-declaration component extraction, call-graph edges for non-Python languages) are available as targeted follow-ups driven by concrete signals rather than a fixed order.

**v0.8.21 (2026-04-24)** — Kotlin tree-sitter parser. Second shipped increment of Phase 10: with v0.8.20's Java parser in, Kotlin is the natural next step — shares the JVM story, extends language coverage into Android apps, Spring / Ktor backends, Gradle build scripts, and pure-JVM libraries without touching the indexing / graph / retrieval layers. `libs/parsers/kotlin.py` is a 116-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "kotlin"` and hook overrides for `_get_ts_language` (binds `tree_sitter_kotlin.language()` via the published `tree-sitter-kotlin>=1.1` wheel), `_symbol_type_map` (four node kinds — `class_declaration` collapses class / interface / enum / annotation / data / sealed classes onto `SymbolType.CLASS` since the Kotlin grammar uses one AST node for all of them and distinguishes via modifier children; `object_declaration` → `CLASS` because named singletons compile to classes-with-one-instance at runtime; `function_declaration` → `METHOD`; `property_declaration` → `VARIABLE`), `_import_node_types` (`{"import"}`), `_detect_role` (directory signals walked first — `src/test/kotlin/` / `src/androidTest/kotlin/` for standard Gradle and Android instrumented tests, plus `src/test/java/` / `src/androidTest/java/` so Kotlin files inside mixed Java/Kotlin projects classify correctly, plus the generic `/tests/` / `/test/` fallbacks — then a filename fallback that first strips `.kt` / `.kts` before checking `*Test` / `*Tests` suffix or `Test*` prefix so `app/src/ConfigTest.kt` classifies as test even outside a dedicated test dir; Gradle Kotlin DSL scripts `.kts` intentionally stay `source` so `build.gradle.kts` is still indexed), `_extract_name` (Kotlin's `property_declaration` doesn't carry a `name` field directly — the identifier lives inside a `variable_declaration` child, so the override walks children for `variable_declaration` → `identifier`, parity with Java's `field_declaration > variable_declarator` dance), `_extract_import_ref` (reads the `qualified_identifier` sibling before `.*` and `as Alias` tokens — wildcard `import java.util.Map.*` naturally reads as `java.util.Map` because the grammar places `.` and `*` as sibling tokens, alias `import com.example.Foo as FooAlias` surfaces the original module path since the graph tracks real dependencies, not local aliases, all emitted as `dst_type="module"`), and static `_module_fq` (strips the first recognised source root — `src/main/kotlin/` / `src/test/kotlin/` / `src/androidTest/kotlin/` plus the Java-rooted variants for mixed projects — encountered anywhere in the path so nested Gradle multi-module projects `modules/foo/src/main/kotlin/com/example/Bar.kt` correctly derive `com.example.Bar`; both `.kt` and `.kts` extensions stripped before the source-root logic runs). Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains `.kt → kotlin` and `.kts → kotlin` extension maps plus a `"kotlin": KotlinParser()` entry in `_PARSERS`; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"kotlin"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES` so indexed Kotlin files count toward symbol-extraction coverage metrics; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"kotlin"` to `_SRC_LANGS` so Kotlin files count toward the parseable-source-files denominator. Design choices locked by test for v1: **`companion_object` intentionally not in the symbol-type map** — the grammar gives companion objects no `name` field (they're implicitly called `Companion`) so the base walker naturally skips them for symbol emission but still recurses into the body, and methods / properties inside a companion land with `parent_fq_name = EnclosingClass` which matches Kotlin semantics where companion members are addressed as `EnclosingClass.member` without an explicit `Companion` hop; `const val MAX_SIZE: Int = 1024` maps to `VARIABLE` rather than `CONSTANT` uniformly (parity with the Java v1 decision to map `static final` to `VARIABLE`), with `test_extracts_const_val_inside_companion` locking the behaviour so a future promotion is an explicit contract break; alias imports surface the original module path, not the local alias; the parser does not yet emit `INHERITS` edges for delegation specifiers (`class Loaded : State()`, `object Loading : State()`, `class Foo : Interface, OtherInterface`) nor `SAME_FILE_CALLS` — Java has the same v1 gap, both listed as plausible future sub-increments; primary constructor properties (`class Config(val name: String)`) and data class components (`data class Point(val x: Int, val y: Int)`) don't yet surface as separate symbols — they live inside `primary_constructor > class_parameters` as `class_parameter` nodes, not `property_declaration`, and adding them requires a dedicated walker. 43 new tests across six classes in `tests/unit/parsers/test_kotlin_parser.py`: **15 symbol-extraction** (class / interface / enum class / annotation class / data class / sealed class with nested object + data class / object declaration / top-level function / method-inside-class / interface-method / property / top-level property / `const val` inside companion object landing as `VARIABLE` / companion-member `parent_fq_name` invariant / enum-method nesting), **4 import-relations** (scoped / wildcard drops `.*` to package / alias surfaces original module path / `dst_type == "module"` invariant across all import edges), **10 role-detection** (Gradle main / bare repo root / Gradle test / Android test / Kotlin file under Java test root in mixed project / `tests/` dir / `*Test.kt` suffix / `*Tests.kt` suffix / `Test*.kt` prefix / Gradle `.kts` build script stays `source`), **8 module-FQ derivation** (Gradle `src/main/kotlin` / `src/test/kotlin` / `src/androidTest/kotlin` / mixed-project `src/main/java` / nested multi-module Gradle / bare dotted path / `.kt` extension strip / `.kts` extension strip), **3 edge cases** (minimal single-function file, empty file emits no symbols and no tree-sitter errors, `ParseResult.language == "kotlin"`), and **3 registry-wiring tests** (`.kt` / `.kts` / Gradle-path detection all resolve to `"kotlin"`, `get_parser("kotlin")` returns a `KotlinParser` instance, `KotlinParser().language == "kotlin"`). Full suite: **1291 passing** (+43 vs v0.8.20 baseline 1245). Ruff clean on 378 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean. With Java (v0.8.20) and Kotlin (v0.8.21) done, the JVM pair is complete; next language target is Swift, after which sub-increments deepening language support (inheritance edges for Java / Kotlin, data class / record component extraction, call-graph edges) start to compete with VS Code marketplace / Obsidian nightly sync on prioritisation.

**v0.8.20 (2026-04-24)** — Java tree-sitter parser. Phase 10 opener: the `wiki_refresh` arc closed in v0.8.19 and the next growth axis is language coverage — parser support for JVM / systems languages not yet indexed. Java is the natural first step: a self-contained deliverable, `tree-sitter-java>=0.23` is a stable published wheel, and Java follows the same `TreeSitterParser` hook-method shape as the Go and Rust parsers that shipped in Phase 6, so no new infrastructure — just a new grammar + symbol-type map + role rules. `libs/parsers/java.py` is a ~150-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "java"` and hook overrides for `_get_ts_language` (binds `tree_sitter_java.language()`), `_symbol_type_map` (five type-declaration node kinds — `class_declaration` / `interface_declaration` / `enum_declaration` / `annotation_type_declaration` / `record_declaration` — all collapse to `SymbolType.CLASS`; `method_declaration` + `constructor_declaration` → `METHOD`; `field_declaration` → `VARIABLE`), `_import_node_types` (`{"import_declaration"}`), `_detect_role` (directory signals `/src/test/java/` / `/tests/` / `/test/` plus filename fallbacks `*Test.java` / `*Tests.java` / `Test*.java` for JUnit 3-4+ conventions — `role="test"` otherwise `"source"`), `_extract_name` (field names live nested inside `variable_declarator` children, not directly on `field_declaration`, so the default base hook returns `None` — the override walks children, finds the first declarator, reads its `name` field), `_extract_import_ref` (reads whichever of `scoped_identifier` or plain `identifier` appears inside an `import_declaration` — wildcard `import java.util.*;` naturally reads as `java.util` because the grammar places `*` as a sibling token, static `import static java.util.Arrays.asList` surfaces the full symbol path, emitted as `dst_type="module"`), and static `_module_fq` (strips the first `src/main/java/` or `src/test/java/` source root encountered anywhere in the path so nested Gradle multi-module projects `modules/foo/src/main/java/com/example/Bar.java` correctly derive `com.example.Bar`, then dots the remainder). Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains a `.java → java` extension map and a `"java": JavaParser()` entry; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"java"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES` so indexed Java files count toward coverage metrics; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"java"` to `_SRC_LANGS` so Java files count toward the parseable-source-files denominator in per-project coverage percentages. Design choices locked by test: static-final fields map to `VARIABLE` (not `CONSTANT`) uniformly in v1 — promoting them requires inspecting modifier children, documented as a deliberate v1 scope limit with `test_extracts_static_final_field` locking the behaviour so a future promotion is an explicit contract break; multi-declarator fields `int a, b, c;` surface only the first name (matches the base class's one-node-one-symbol contract); wildcard imports drop the `.*` suffix (graph consumers care about modules, not whether every symbol is pulled); v1 does not emit `INHERITS` / `IMPLEMENTS` edges for `extends` / `implements` clauses nor `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges for method invocations (follows Go / Rust parser shape, not the richer Python parser). 33 new tests in `tests/unit/parsers/test_java_parser.py`: 10 symbol-extraction (class / interface / enum / annotation-type / record / method / constructor / interface-method / field / static-final-field plus enum-method nesting contract), 4 import-relations (scoped / wildcard-as-package / static / `dst_type` invariant), 7 role-detection (Maven main / bare repo root / Maven test / tests dir / `*Test.java` suffix / `*Tests.java` suffix / `Test*.java` JUnit 3 prefix), 5 module-FQ derivation (Maven main-root / test-root / nested Gradle / bare dotted / extension strip), 3 edge cases (minimal single-class, empty file emits no symbols and no tree-sitter errors, `ParseResult.language == "java"`), and 3 registry-wiring tests (extension detection, parser lookup, language attribute). Full suite: **1245 passing** (+33 vs v0.8.19 baseline 1212). First shipped increment of Phase 10 (Java / Kotlin / Swift parsers, VS Code marketplace, Obsidian nightly sync); next plausible increments along the same axis are Kotlin (shares the JVM story) and Swift, with Java inheritance / call-graph edges as possible sub-increments if a driving use case arrives.

**v0.8.19 (2026-04-24)** — outage-duration signal on the `wiki_refresh` recovery toast. Since v0.8.11 the green recovery toast has read "Wiki refresh status recovered — `<slug>` is reachable again. Resuming normal polling." — the copy told the user *that* recovery happened but never *how long* they were looking at the yellow degraded card, a gap explicitly documented when v0.8.15 added `trigger=manual|poll` telemetry but left the user-facing duration story untouched. This release closes it: a user returning to their dashboard after lunch now sees "reachable again after 1h 14m" instead of a generic "reachable again", short blips read "after 47s" / "after 2m 17s", and the distinction between a 30-second hiccup and an hour-long outage — exactly the signal the recovery toast was meant to carry — is finally visible. Design: the route holds **no server-side state** (no session, no cookie, no Redis entry) tracking outage starts — the dashboard stays stateless HTMX end-to-end. The outage-start timestamp instead rides on the browser via an HTMX `hx-headers` round-trip, identical to the v0.8.11 `X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded` marker and the v0.8.15 `X-LV-DCP-Retry-Source` classifier. On the first degraded render the `except` branch stamps `degraded_since = int(time.time())` into the template context and the degraded wrapper's `hx-headers` JSON includes `"X-LV-DCP-Degraded-Since": "<ts>"` alongside the was-degraded marker. On every subsequent degraded tick HTMX echoes the header back, the route parses it via `_parse_degraded_since(request)`, and the new degraded render re-stamps the **same** value — so the original start time is preserved indefinitely across a long outage rather than resetting every tick. On the recovery tick the same echo is translated into `outage_seconds = now - since`, formatted via `_format_outage_duration(seconds)` as a short human label (`"<1s"` / `"47s"` / `"2m 17s"` / `"1h 23m"` — only the two largest non-zero units, so `1h 23m` not `1h 23m 47s` for scannability), and the template splices it into the toast copy via `{% if outage_duration_label %}is reachable again after {{ outage_duration_label }}. {% else %}is reachable again. {% endif %}` — a missing / malformed / future header collapses cleanly to the pre-v0.8.19 copy so browser tabs that opened on older builds still get the recovery toast on rolling upgrades, they just don't get the duration suffix. The Retry button's `hx-headers` JSON now carries all three markers (was-degraded + retry-source + degraded-since) so manual-retry recoveries surface the duration identically to poll-initiated recoveries — no split UX where one path flashes "recovered after 2m" and the other flashes a generic "recovered". Parser is defensive: absent / non-integer / non-positive / future values all collapse to `None`, which is safe because the downstream branch falls back to the pre-v0.8.19 copy. The `ui.wiki_refresh.toast.rendered` log event gains an `outage_seconds` field (integer or `None`) alongside the v0.8.15 `trigger` field — field shape stays stable so downstream structured-log consumers parse both code paths identically. Closes the recovery-duration item that was documented as future work in the v0.8.15 release notes; the v0.8.x `wiki_refresh` arc is now complete across visibility (v0.8.9 crash, v0.8.11 recovery), interactivity (v0.8.14 retry), telemetry (v0.8.15 trigger + v0.8.19 outage_seconds), and accessibility (v0.8.13 reduced-motion / v0.8.16 forced-colors / v0.8.17 pulse dot / v0.8.18 progress bar). 8 new integration tests covering fresh-stamp on first degraded render, verbatim preservation across multi-tick outages, malformed-input fresh restamp, Retry button carrying all three markers, end-to-end "reachable again after 2m 17s" copy from a 137-second simulated outage, pre-v0.8.19 backwards-compatible fallback, malformed-value fallback (four garbage values in a sweep — garbled / `0` / `-42` / future), and two telemetry tests locking the log-event field shape (integer for a 42-second outage, `None` when the header is absent). 14 parametrized unit tests on `_format_outage_duration` covering every boundary (0 / 1 / 59 / 60 / 3599 / 3600 / 86400) plus representative midrange values. 1212 tests passing.

**v0.8.18 (2026-04-24)** — a11y parity for the `wiki_refresh` progress bar. Closes the final a11y debt on the `wiki_refresh` subsystem: the horizontal module-progress bar (6 px track + fill with `transition:width 0.3s` that animates on every 2 s poll tick as modules advance) had two broken scenarios — under `forced-colors: active` both the `#bbdefb` track and `#1976d2` fill remap to system `Canvas` (the page background), so the whole bar becomes an invisible sliver; under `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` the width transition fires on every tick of a possibly 100-module refresh (~100 repeating slide animations). The track and fill `<div>`s now carry `lvdcp-progress-track` / `lvdcp-progress-fill` class hooks, and the existing `<style>` block (already housing v0.8.17's pulse-dot rules) grows three sibling rules: a `border: 1px solid CanvasText` on the track (borders survive the forced-colors remap), `background: CanvasText` on the fill so it's a solid dense shape against the remapped track, and a `transition: none` cancel that fires under both `prefers-reduced-motion` and `forced-colors` (consistent with v0.8.17 — when in doubt, stay static in any a11y mode). All rules stay scoped inside `{% if wr.in_progress %}` — idle / clean / crashed / degraded responses ship zero progress-bar CSS. Reused the existing pulse-dot `<style>` block rather than opening a second one — same outer guard, shared `@media` blocks, ~150 extra bytes of CSS on running responses where `modules_total` is still unknown but that's a cheap payload trade for one less style block. With this release the `wiki_refresh` subsystem is a11y-complete on all four animated / coloured elements: recovery toast fade (v0.8.13 + v0.8.16), crash toast container (v0.8.16), running-status pulse dot (v0.8.17), progress bar (v0.8.18). 7 new integration tests. 1192 tests passing.

**v0.8.17 (2026-04-24)** — a11y parity for the `lvdcp-pulse` running indicator. Closes the last carry-forward a11y gap left after v0.8.16: the pulsing blue dot on the Running card has been cycling opacity 1↔0.4 every 1.5 s via `@keyframes lvdcp-pulse` since v0.8.7, and two scenarios were still broken — users with `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` were subjected to the infinite animation (fixed for the recovery toast in v0.8.13 but not the dot), and users on `forced-colors: active` had the dot's inline `background:#1976d2` remapped to `Canvas` (the page background), rendering it invisible (fixed for toasts in v0.8.16 but not the dot). This release gives the span a new `lvdcp-pulse-dot` class hook and hangs two sibling media-query rules inside the existing `<style>` block: `prefers-reduced-motion` cancels the animation and pins opacity to 1; `forced-colors: active` additionally paints the dot with the `CanvasText` system-color token, which survives the UA remap (author RGB values are overridden, system tokens aren't). Chose solid-fill over a border because the dot is 10×10 — a 1 px border would be ~40 % of the visual mass with an inner area still matching `Canvas`, a hollow ring that reads poorly as a status indicator. All rules stay scoped inside `{% if wr.in_progress %}` — idle/clean/crashed responses ship zero pulse CSS. With this release the `wiki_refresh` subsystem is a11y-complete across all three animated elements: recovery toast fade (v0.8.13 + v0.8.16), crash toast container (v0.8.16), and running-status dot (v0.8.17). The running card's nested progress bar is the only remaining a11y debt and is documented as a known gap. 5 new integration tests covering class-hook presence, exact rule bodies under both media queries, absence on non-running responses, and a regression guard that the default animation is still shipped for non-a11y users. 1185 tests passing.

**v0.8.16 (2026-04-24)** — `forced-colors: active` adaptation on the `wiki_refresh` crash + recovery toasts. Closes the last carry-forward a11y gap on the toast subsystem: Windows high-contrast mode (and equivalent OS-level palettes on macOS/Linux) remaps the solid red/green backgrounds to system `Canvas` and forcibly drops `box-shadow`, leaving the banner text visible but with no visual container — it reads as free-floating text pasted onto the dashboard. Two scoped `<style>` blocks now hang `@media (forced-colors: active)` rules off a new `lvdcp-crash-toast` class and the existing `lvdcp-recovery-toast` class: `border: 1px solid CanvasText` restores the "container" frame (borders are exempt from the color remap per spec), `box-shadow: none` silences the UA shadow-drop, `<code>` slug chip gets the same frame, button opacity pins to 1 so it can't look disabled. The recovery toast additionally cancels the v0.8.12 fadeout animation in forced-colors mode — matches the v0.8.13 `prefers-reduced-motion` logic (a user on high-contrast is almost certainly an a11y user, banners on timers are hostile). Both rules scoped inside the same `{% if show_*_toast %}` guards that carry the other a11y CSS, so idle polls still ship zero forced-colors CSS. 4 new integration tests, 1180 tests passing.

**v0.8.15 (2026-04-24)** — Toast-render telemetry on the `wiki_refresh` panel. The v0.8.9 crash toast and v0.8.11 recovery toast have been shipping for five releases without a single metric about whether they actually fire — so this release adds the minimum viable signal: one structured log event per toast render. The route emits `log.info("ui.wiki_refresh.toast.rendered", extra={"event": "ui.wiki_refresh.toast.rendered", "slug": ..., "kind": "crash"|"recovery", "trigger": "poll"|"manual"})` via stdlib logging, so a future structlog / OTel adapter picks it up without a template change. The v0.8.14 Retry button grows a second header, `X-LV-DCP-Retry-Source: manual`, and the new `_classify_recovery_trigger` helper splits recoveries into auto-poll vs. manual-click — answers whether the Retry button is invisible (near-zero manual share) or the 30 s poll is too slow (90 %+ manual share). Idle polls emit zero telemetry; the event fires only when a toast actually reaches the user's DOM. Zero JS, no new deps, 5 new integration tests via pytest `caplog`, one v0.8.14 test updated to count the marker substring instead of the full `hx-headers` attribute. 1176 tests passing.

**v0.8.14 (2026-04-24)** — "Retry now" escape hatch on the `wiki_refresh` degraded card. The yellow "refresh status unavailable" card (v0.8.10) now carries a small Retry button that fires the same polling endpoint on click — identical `hx-get` / `hx-target="#wiki-refresh-panel"` / `hx-swap="outerHTML"` as the auto-poll, plus `hx-headers='{"X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded": "true"}'` so a successful manual retry triggers the green recovery toast exactly like an auto-recovery would. `hx-disabled-elt="this"` prevents double-click races. A user who knows (restarted infra, migration finished, etc.) that the service is back no longer has to wait up to 30 s for the next tick. No new route, no new JS, button scoped strictly to `{% if degraded %}` so it never appears on healthy responses. Closes the "Retry now" carry-forward gap from v0.8.10-v0.8.13.

**v0.8.13 (2026-04-24)** — Accessibility + hover polish on the recovery toast fade. Two carry-forward gaps from v0.8.12 closed in one pure-CSS patch: (a) `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` cancels the fadeout animation entirely for users who've opted out of OS-level motion — the toast then stays sticky like the crash toast, manual dismiss only; (b) `.lvdcp-recovery-toast:hover { animation-play-state: paused !important }` freezes the fade while the cursor is over the toast — moving off resumes from the current opacity, no re-triggering. Both rules hang off a new `lvdcp-recovery-toast` class and live inside the same `{% if show_recovery_toast %}` guard as v0.8.12's keyframes, so idle polls still ship zero a11y CSS. `!important` needed because the v0.8.12 inline `animation:` shorthand has specificity 1000 — justified vs the alternative of breaking the shorthand into longhand or updating the v0.8.12 test. No JS, no new deps.

**v0.8.12 (2026-04-24)** — Auto-dismiss for the recovery toast. The green "wiki refresh status recovered" banner (v0.8.11) now carries an inline `animation: lvdcp-toast-fadeout 8s forwards` so it fades and disappears ~8 s after it appears (6 s visible + 2 s fade). The red crash toast stays sticky — bad news needs acknowledgment, good news does not. Zero JS, no new deps; the `@keyframes` block is scoped to the `{% if show_recovery_toast %}` guard so normal idle polls ship zero fadeout CSS. The final keyframe flips `pointer-events: none` so the invisible end-state doesn't intercept clicks. Closes the top UX gap from v0.8.11 (transient good-news toast required a manual click).

**v0.8.11 (2026-04-24)** — Recovery toast on the `wiki_refresh` degraded → normal transition. Symmetric to v0.8.9's red crash toast: on the exact polling tick that flips the panel out of degraded mode (v0.8.10), the fragment response also carries a green `hx-swap-oob` banner into `#toast-region` so scrolled-away users notice the self-heal. Detection is pure-HTMX: the degraded wrapper echoes `hx-headers='{"X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded": "true"}'`, HTMX sends the marker on the next poll, the route sees the header on a now-successful assembly and flips a one-shot toast on. The new successful wrapper omits the marker so the toast fires exactly once per recovery event. No cookies, no session store, no JS state. Closes the top known gap from v0.8.10 (silent self-heal).

**v0.8.10 (2026-04-24)** — Error-backoff shell on the `wiki_refresh` polling endpoint. The `/api/project/{slug}/wiki-refresh` route now wraps its status-assembly path in a try/except: on any internal failure it returns a 200 response carrying the partial in degraded mode — a yellow "refresh status unavailable" card with `hx-trigger="every 30s"` instead of `every 2s`. Closes two failure modes that predated the contract: (a) a 500 during polling caused HTMX to hammer the endpoint at the original 2 s cadence; (b) a `build_wiki_refresh` returning `None` silently stripped `hx-get` from the wrapper, freezing the panel until a full page reload. The 404-for-unknown-slug contract is preserved via `except HTTPException: raise`, and full-page `/project/<slug>` still 500s on genuine errors — the degraded shell is scoped to the polling endpoint only. Closes the first operational known gap from v0.8.8.

**v0.8.9 (2026-04-24)** — One-shot crash toast on the `wiki_refresh` panel. The HTMX polling tick that flips the panel from *running* → *FAILED* now also carries an `hx-swap-oob` flash banner that HTMX appends into a new fixed-position `#toast-region` drop zone added to `base.html.j2`. Four predicates gate the emission — `HX-Request` header, refresh finished and non-live, `last_exit_code` a real crash (not `0`/`143`), `last_completed_at` within 15 s of now — so the toast fires exactly once per crash event, never on full page reload, never on SIGTERM cancellation, never on a manual `curl`. No new JS, no new deps, no route changes — fragment endpoint just adds a `show_crash_toast` flag to the template context. Closes the second known gap from v0.8.8 (no transition notification).

**v0.8.8 (2026-04-24)** — HTMX live-polling on the `wiki_refresh` panel. The dashboard's bg-refresh panel (v0.8.7) now updates in place every ~2 s while a refresh is running — no page reload, no new CSS, no new JS beyond the HTMX script that was already loaded since phase 7. New public helper `libs.status.aggregator.build_wiki_refresh` lets the polling endpoint skip the full `build_project_status` pipeline, keeping each tick cheap. A new fragment route `GET /api/project/<slug>/wiki-refresh` re-renders just the partial; the outer wrapper's presence-or-absence of `hx-get` is the cancellation signal, so polling self-cancels the moment the refresh transitions to idle.

**v0.8.7 (2026-04-24)** — Dashboard renders `wiki_refresh` panel. The FastAPI/HTMX per-project page (`/project/<slug>`) now draws a new "Wiki background refresh" section between scan coverage and the dependency graph: blue "Running" card with phase + progress bar + current module + pid when a refresh is in flight, green "clean", gray "cancelled (SIGTERM)", or red "FAILED" card (with collapsible log tail) otherwise. Hidden for projects that have never run a refresh. Closes the #1 known gap from v0.8.6: data model was ready, just needed rendering. No route change — `ProjectStatus.wiki_refresh` from v0.8.6 was already passed to the template; v0.8.7 adds one `{% include %}` plus a partial.

**v0.8.6 (2026-04-24)** — MCP `lvdcp_status` surfaces bg refresh state. `ProjectStatus` gains `wiki_refresh: WikiBackgroundRefresh | None` — a nested block that mirrors `CopilotCheckReport.wiki_refresh_*` / `wiki_last_refresh_*` (live progress + last-run outcome + crash tail). Agents calling `lvdcp_status(path=…)` now see the same bg-refresh state `ctx project check` shows on the CLI, so they can decide "refresh or pack" without shelling out. Lazy import of `libs.copilot` keeps non-wiki consumers from paying the cost. No new deps.

**v0.8.5 (2026-04-24)** — Error log tail. On a non-clean, non-SIGTERM exit the runner seeks past its startup offset in `.refresh.log` and persists the current run's last ~20 lines as `log_tail` in `.refresh.last`. `ctx project check` renders them as an indented `log tail:` block under the `FAILED exit=…` last-run hint, so diagnosing a crashed refresh no longer requires a second `cat .refresh.log` step. Suppressed on clean / SIGTERM exits and while a refresh is in progress. Closes the *"No error-tail surface"* gap from v0.8.4. No new deps.

**v0.8.4 (2026-04-24)** — `.refresh.last` outcome record. After every background wiki refresh finishes (cleanly, via SIGTERM, or crash), the runner's `finally` block writes `.context/wiki/.refresh.last` with `{completed_at, exit_code, modules_updated, elapsed_seconds}`. `ctx project check` then renders `bg_refresh=false (last: ok 12 modules 47s, 3 min ago)` — or `FAILED exit=1 … — see .refresh.log` for crashes. Closes the *"No transition-to-error surface"* gap from v0.8.3: the watcher now tells you *why* the refresh stopped, not just *that* it stopped. No new deps, no new process.

**v0.8.3 (2026-04-24)** — `ctx project check --watch`. Live-tail the background wiki refresh: re-prints the full `check` snapshot every `--interval` seconds (default 2 s) until the refresh transitions to idle, then exits. `--json` mode streams consecutive `CopilotCheckReport` objects separated by blank lines — grep- and `jq -c`-friendly. Closes the *"No live tail"* gap from v0.8.2. No new deps; generator-based polling, not threads.

**v0.8.2 (2026-04-24)** — Wiki background progress & cancellation. The `.refresh.lock` now carries `phase` + `modules_total`/`modules_done` + `current_module`; `ctx project check` renders it as `bg_refresh=true (generating 3/12 "libs/foo" pid=1234)`. New `ctx project wiki <path> --stop` sends SIGTERM, cleans up stale locks, and reports the PID. Closes both "Known gaps" called out in v0.8.1: binary-only status and no cancellation primitive. No new deps, no daemon — still a single atomic-write lock file.

**v0.8.1 (2026-04-24)** — Async wiki refresh. `ctx project refresh --wiki-background` (and `ctx project wiki --background --refresh`) detaches the wiki LLM pipeline into a subprocess so the CLI returns immediately on large projects. `ctx project check` surfaces `bg_refresh=<bool>`; the lock file is crash-safe (dead-PID and >1h age are auto-cleared). Closes the "sync wiki blocks the terminal for minutes" gap called out in the v0.8.0 release notes. No new deps.

**Phase 9 complete (2026-04-23, v0.8.0)** — Project Copilot Wrapper (spec-011): new `ctx project` command group (`check`, `refresh`, `wiki`, `ask`) that orchestrates the existing scan/pack/wiki/status primitives into single user-facing actions. Detects and explains the four canonical degraded modes — not scanned, stale index, wiki missing/stale, Qdrant off, ambiguous retrieval — so the common "is the index fresh enough for my question?" and "refresh everything and ask" flows become one command each. No new storage, queue, or LLM dependency — strictly a composition layer over the primitives from previous phases.

**Phase 8 complete (2026-04-23, v0.7.0)** — Symbol Timeline Index (spec-010): append-only event store answering "when was X implemented?", "what disappeared after release Y?", "what regressed between v1 and v2?" with indexed lookups instead of git-log walks. Four new MCP tools (`lvdcp_when`, `lvdcp_removed_since`, `lvdcp_diff`, `lvdcp_regressions`), new `ctx timeline` CLI, Claude Code hooks for auto-reconciliation after rebase/amend, release snapshots tied to git tags, context-pack enrichment with `## Timeline facts` section (≤ 3 KB, EN + RU marker detection). **SC-001** empirical: 31×–88× token-footprint savings vs `git log -p --follow`, well beyond the 15× target. **SC-003** perf-gated: scan overhead ≤ 10 %.

**Phase 7c complete (2026-04-21)** — PageRank centrality boost (Aider parity), adaptive vector/FTS fusion, disambiguation suggestions on ambiguous packs, Go `tests_for` inference, directory-aware ancestor path boost, recency-aware centrality, reusable `libs/eval` wheel package, Claude Code skill, ByteRover-style reviewable engineering memory (proposed → accepted lifecycle). Five new MCP tools (`lvdcp_neighbors`, `lvdcp_history`, `lvdcp_cross_project_patterns`, `lvdcp_memory_propose`, `lvdcp_memory_list`) + two new CLI commands (`ctx eval`, `ctx memory`).

**Phase 7b complete (2026-04-16)** — TypeScript/JS graph enrichment: `tests_for` relations, tighter path-filter rejecting unresolved module specifiers and npm subpaths. Verified on a 926-file Next.js codebase.

**Phase 7a complete (2026-04-13)** — Identifier-aware path retrieval ships path aliases into the FTS index (camelCase/snake_case tokenization), lifting precision@3 from 0.568 to 0.693. Wiki knowledge module gets a post-scan background hook. Cyrillic support in pack enrichment. Real-project eval harness added.

Stabilization 0.6.1 baseline: mandatory GitHub Actions quality gates, green `ruff` / `mypy`, runtime-hardened embeddings and Qdrant.

### Retrieval quality (LV_DCP synthetic, 32 queries)

| Metric | Value | Threshold | Delta from Phase 2 |
|---|---|---|---|
| recall@5 files | **0.964** | ≥ 0.92 | +0.073 |
| precision@3 files | **0.693** | ≥ 0.63 | +0.073 |
| recall@5 symbols | 0.880 | ≥ 0.80 | +0.047 |
| impact_recall@5 | **0.931** | ≥ 0.85 | +0.112 |

### Multi-project retrieval (9 advisory queries, 4 projects)

| Metric | Value |
|---|---|
| Global recall@5 | **0.500** |
| Large project (1200+ files) | 0.200 |
| Medium projects (100-500 files) | 0.750–1.000 |

> Multi-project retrieval on large projects needs further tuning in Phase 7.

### Test suite

1050 tests passing, 0 failures. Eval harness: 32 synthetic queries; multi-project eval currently covers 9 advisory queries across 4 registered projects.

For advisory real-project eval setup and report commands, see [docs/eval/real-project-eval.md](docs/eval/real-project-eval.md).

## Dashboard

Local project status dashboard:

```bash
uv run ctx ui                      # multi-project overview at http://127.0.0.1:8787
uv run ctx ui /path/to/project     # open a specific project detail view
```

Features:
- **Value metrics**: packs served, compression ratio, coverage quality
- **Multi-project grid** with add/remove buttons, file/symbol/relation counts
- **Adaptive dependency graph**: module clustering (click to expand), zoom+pan, hover tooltips
- **Hotspots table**: top-10 riskiest files (fan_in x churn x test coverage)
- **Scan coverage**: per-project symbol coverage %, language/relation breakdown
- **Sparklines**: queries/day, scans/day, pack latency p95, coverage (rolling 7 days)
- **Claude Code token usage** totals (rolling 7d + 30d)

The same data is available programmatically via the new `lvdcp_status` MCP resource:

```python
# From Claude Code:
lvdcp_status()                  # workspace summary across all registered projects
lvdcp_status(path="/abs/p")     # single project detail including dependency graph
```

Upgrading: `git pull && uv sync --extra dev && uv run ctx mcp install`.

## Phase 3c.1 — LLM Summaries (new in 0.3.2)

Pluggable LLM provider with file-level summaries:

```bash
# Configure provider (default: OpenAI)
export OPENAI_API_KEY=sk-...                  # or ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, etc.
uv run ctx ui                                  # open http://127.0.0.1:8787/settings
# toggle "Enable LLM summaries", save

# Generate summaries for a project
uv run ctx summarize /path/to/project
```

Summaries are cached in `~/.lvdcp/summaries.db` keyed on file content hash + prompt version + model name, so re-running on unchanged files has zero cost.

Supported providers out of the box:
- **OpenAI** (default): `gpt-4o-mini`, `gpt-5-mini`, `gpt-5`
- **Anthropic**: `claude-haiku-4-5`, `claude-sonnet-4-6`
- **Ollama** (local, zero-cost): `qwen2.5-coder:7b`, `qwen2.5-coder:32b`, `llama3.3:70b`

### Rate limits on OpenAI tier-1

OpenAI tier-1 accounts have a 200K TPM (tokens per minute) limit. Cold-scanning a
large project with the default concurrency (4) stays under this limit for most
projects. If you hit HTTP 429 errors, re-run `ctx summarize` — already-completed
files will be cached and only the failed ones will retry. Tier-2+ users can use
`--concurrency 10` for faster cold scans.

The `openai_client` adapter honors `Retry-After` headers automatically and retries
up to 3 times per file before giving up.

### Cost tracking

Dashboard topbar shows `$X.XX / $25 monthly` budget usage. `ctx mcp doctor` now runs 9 checks (was 7) — the new check 8 verifies provider connectivity, check 9 warns at 80% and fails at 100% of monthly budget.

### Settings UI

`/settings` page lets you switch provider, model, and budget without editing config files. API keys are stored as environment variables only — the UI displays the env var *name* and its set/unset status, never the key value itself.

See [docs/adr/006-llm-provider-abstraction.md](docs/adr/006-llm-provider-abstraction.md) for the pluggable design rationale.

Upgrading: `git pull && uv sync --extra dev && uv run ctx mcp install`.

## Prerequisites

- macOS (primary target) or Linux
- Python 3.12+
- [uv](https://github.com/astral-sh/uv) package manager
- [Claude Code](https://docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/claude-code) (CLI and/or VS Code extension) — optional but the main use case

## Installation

### One-time setup

```bash
git clone https://github.com/lukinvit/LV_DCP.git
cd LV_DCP
uv sync --all-extras
make lint typecheck test  # verify toolchain
```

### Global `ctx` CLI (optional)

To run `ctx` from any directory without `uv run`:

```bash
mkdir -p ~/bin
ln -sf "$(pwd)/.venv/bin/ctx" ~/bin/ctx
# ensure ~/bin is on PATH (add to ~/.zshrc or ~/.bashrc if missing):
#   export PATH="$HOME/bin:$PATH"
```

Then from any project directory:

```bash
cd /path/to/your-project
ctx scan .                 # incremental index
ctx scan --full .          # full re-parse
ctx pack . "your question"
ctx inspect .              # index stats
ctx wiki update .          # refresh dirty wiki articles
```

Do **not** put `uv run` in front of a wrapper-installed `ctx` — the venv already
knows its interpreter, and `uv run` inside another project's directory will try
to resolve a non-existent local environment and recurse.

### Project onboarding

```bash
# One guided command for a new project
uv run ctx setup /absolute/path/to/your/project --open-ui
```

`ctx setup` reuses the existing install/scan/wiki/watch/UI primitives and ends
with a readiness summary:

- `base mode` = local scan/index/packs/UI baseline
- `full mode` = hybrid/vector retrieval quality

For `full mode`, LV_DCP requires:

- `Qdrant`
- a real embedding provider/API key (for example `OPENAI_API_KEY`)

For wiki generation, LV_DCP also requires:

- `claude` CLI on `PATH`

### Register with Claude Code (recommended)

```bash
# Register the MCP server so Claude Code calls it automatically
claude mcp add --scope user lvdcp -- \
  uv run --directory /absolute/path/to/LV_DCP python -m apps.mcp.server

# Verify
claude mcp list
# Should show: lvdcp: ... - ✓ Connected
```

Replace `/absolute/path/to/LV_DCP` with your actual clone path.

After this, restart your Claude Code session (or VS Code if using the extension). Claude will now see `lvdcp_pack`, `lvdcp_scan`, `lvdcp_inspect`, `lvdcp_explain`, `lvdcp_neighbors`, `lvdcp_history`, `lvdcp_cross_project_patterns`, `lvdcp_memory_propose`, `lvdcp_memory_list` as available tools and will call them automatically per the behavioral rules in `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`.

## Usage

### Basic workflow

```bash
# Index a project (first time)
cd ~/dev/my-python-project
uv run --directory /path/to/LV_DCP ctx scan .

# Ask questions — get ranked file/symbol packs
uv run --directory /path/to/LV_DCP ctx pack . "authentication middleware"
uv run --directory /path/to/LV_DCP ctx pack . "add rate limit to login" --mode edit

# Inspect the index
uv run --directory /path/to/LV_DCP ctx inspect .
```

### Commands

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `ctx scan <path>` | Walk, parse, index. Incremental by default (skips unchanged files by content hash). Use `--full` to force reparse. |
| `ctx setup <path>` | One-command onboarding: scan, MCP/hooks best-effort install, wiki enablement/build attempt, readiness summary, optional UI launch. |
| `ctx pack <path> "<query>" [--mode navigate\|edit]` | Build a retrieval pack. Navigate mode for questions, edit mode for changes. |
| `ctx inspect <path>` | Print index statistics (file count, symbols, relations by type). |
| `ctx mcp serve` | Run the MCP server via stdio (called by Claude Code, not humans). |
| `ctx mcp install --scope {user\|project\|local}` | Patch `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` with a behavioral rule (⚠ currently writes to wrong file — see Phase 3 backlog M8). Use `claude mcp add` directly for now. |
| `ctx watch add/remove/list/start` | Manage the auto-indexing daemon (watchdog + FSEvents, incremental scan on file change). |
| `ctx eval <path> [--queries <file>]` | Run the retrieval eval harness against a project and print recall/precision/MRR metrics. |
| `ctx memory list <path> [--status proposed\|accepted\|rejected]` | List reviewable engineering memories for a project. |
| `ctx memory propose <path> --topic <topic> --body <body>` | Persist a non-obvious project fact for human review. |

### What gets indexed

Supported languages:
- **Python** — via stdlib `ast`, extracts classes, functions, methods, constants, imports, same-file calls
- **TypeScript / JavaScript** — via tree-sitter, extracts classes, functions, interfaces, enums, imports, constants
- **Go** — via tree-sitter, extracts functions, methods, types, imports
- **Rust** — via tree-sitter, extracts functions, structs, traits, enums, use declarations
- **Markdown** — heading extraction as navigation anchors
- **YAML / JSON / TOML** — syntax validation, config role detection

Automatic ignore list: `.git/`, `.venv/`, `node_modules/`, `__pycache__/`, `.mypy_cache/`, `.ruff_cache/`, `.pytest_cache/`, `dist/`, `build/`, `.context/`, `secrets/`, `credentials/`, plus `.env`, `.env.local/production/staging/development`, `credentials.json`, `secrets.json`.

### Privacy model

- **All processing is local.** LV_DCP never makes network calls on its own. The only outbound data is what your LLM client (e.g. Claude Code) sends to its own API — and LV_DCP reduces that payload rather than expanding it.
- **Secret pattern detection** — 12 regex patterns for AWS keys, OpenAI/Stripe/GitHub/Slack tokens, JWTs, PEM private key headers. Files matching these are indexed by path only; their content is excluded from the full-text index and context packs.
- **Deny list** — env files and credentials files are ignored at the path level before any content is read.
- **Nothing leaves the machine.** Indexes live in `.context/` directories inside each project root. Delete the directory to remove the index.

## Architecture in one diagram

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  Claude Code (CLI or VS Code extension)         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                   ↕ stdio (MCP)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  apps/mcp/server.py — FastMCP server            │
│  Tools: scan, pack, inspect, explain            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                   ↕
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  libs/project_index — ProjectIndex wrapper      │
│  (consolidates cache + fts + symbols + graph)   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                   ↕
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  libs/retrieval/pipeline.py — 4-stage retrieval │
│   1. Symbol match (token scoring)               │
│   2. SQLite FTS5 (full-text)                    │
│   3. Graph expansion (depth 2, decay 0.7)       │
│   4. Score decay cutoff + final rank            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                   ↕ per-project SQLite
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  .context/cache.db   (files, symbols, relations,│
│                       retrieval_traces)         │
│  .context/fts.db     (FTS5 full-text index)     │
│  .context/project.md, symbol_index.md           │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Parallel:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  apps/agent/daemon.py — watchdog + debounce     │
│  Auto-rescan on FS changes (2s debounce)        │
│  Managed by launchd on macOS (plist generator)  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```
