## Development

```bash
make install       # uv sync --all-extras
make lint          # ruff check + ruff format --check
make typecheck     # mypy strict
make test          # pytest, excluding eval and llm markers
make eval          # retrieval evaluation harness
```

Current: 798 tests (798 collected, 1 deselected), eval harness with 32 synthetic queries, plus 9 advisory multi-project queries. Phase 6 feature baseline tagged `phase-6-complete`.

### Running the daemon

```bash
# Register a project
uv run ctx watch add /absolute/path/to/your/project

# Start the daemon in foreground (for debugging)
uv run ctx watch start
```

The daemon uses `watchdog.observers.Observer` which auto-selects `FSEventsObserver` on macOS and `InotifyObserver` on Linux. Debounce window is 2 seconds; mass changes trigger a batched incremental scan rather than N individual ones.

## Roadmap

- **Phase 3** (done, v0.3.0–0.3.4) — LLM summaries with content-hash cache, dashboard UI (D3 graph, sparklines, health cards), cost tracking, settings UI, role-weighted retrieval fusion, config boost, graph depth tuning.
- **Phase 4** (done, v0.4.0) — pymorphy3 Russian stemmer, git intelligence (churn/blame), static impact analysis + hotspot widget, adaptive graph clustering, UI project management, diff-aware edit packs.
- **Phase 5** (done, v0.5.0) — Hook enforcement (PreToolUse/PostToolUse), dual-language retrieval (80+ ru↔en terms), 5 new relation types (tests_for, inherits, specifies), value metrics dashboard, scan coverage widget, 457 tests (0 failures).
- **Phase 6** (done, v0.6.0) — Cross-language parsers (TypeScript/JS, Go, Rust via tree-sitter), Qdrant vector store with hybrid retrieval (RRF fusion), Obsidian vault sync, VS Code extension MVP, cross-project pattern detection, wiki knowledge module (LLM-synthesized articles, lint, architecture page).
- **Stabilization 0.6.1** (done) — GitHub Actions quality gates, repository-wide green `ruff` / `mypy`, warning-free embeddings and Qdrant runtime, 684 tests at release.
- **Phase 7a** (done) — Identifier-aware path retrieval (path aliases in FTS index, camelCase/snake_case tokenization), wiki post-scan hook with ThreadPoolExecutor, Cyrillic tokenization in pack enrichment, real-project eval harness, precision@3 improved 0.568→0.693.
- **Phase 7b** (done) — TypeScript/JavaScript graph enrichment: `tests_for` and `inherits` relations ported from Python parser. TS module resolution supports `./`, `../`, `@/` alias, FSD-style `@shared/` / `@entities/` / `@widgets/` / `@features/` / `@app/` / `@pages/` / `@processes/` aliases, rooted paths, and DDD-style roots (`domains`, `services`, `backend`, `frontend`). Test-path heuristic extended for `.test.ts` / `.spec.tsx` / `__tests__/` conventions. Graph-expansion filter tightened to reject unresolved import specifiers and npm package subpaths (`./flow-engine`, `@/lib/foo`, `next-auth/jwt`, `@playwright/test`). Verified on three real projects: Next.js app (82 tests_for, 29 inherits), large TS monorepo (440 tests_for, 26 inherits), DDD frontend (131 tests_for via DDD heuristic).
- **Phase 7c** (done) — PageRank centrality boost, adaptive vector/FTS fusion, `lvdcp_neighbors` tool for agentic graph follow-ups, disambiguation suggestions on ambiguous packs, Go `tests_for` inference, directory-aware ancestor path boost, `lvdcp_history` git-history MCP tool, recency-aware centrality, `ctx eval` CLI + reusable `libs/eval` wheel package, Claude Code skill. Round-4: `lvdcp_memory_propose` + `lvdcp_memory_list` MCP tools, `ctx memory` CLI, ByteRover-style reviewable engineering memory (proposed → accepted lifecycle).
- **Phase 8** (done, v0.7.0) — Symbol Timeline Index (spec-010): append-only event store, 4 new MCP tools (`lvdcp_when` / `lvdcp_removed_since` / `lvdcp_diff` / `lvdcp_regressions`), `ctx timeline` CLI, Claude Code hooks, release snapshots, pack enrichment, Prometheus metrics, doctor check. SC-001: 31×–88× token savings vs git-log walk.
- **Phase 9** (done, v0.8.0) — Project Copilot Wrapper (spec-011): new `ctx project` CLI group (`check` / `refresh` / `wiki` / `ask`) that orchestrates existing primitives. Composition layer only — no new storage — so the user has a human-friendly surface above the low-level `lvdcp_*` tools.
- **v0.8.1** (done) — Async wiki refresh: `--wiki-background` detaches the wiki LLM pipeline into a subprocess so `ctx project refresh` returns immediately on large projects. Crash-safe lock file, `check` surfaces `bg_refresh=<bool>`. No new deps.
- **v0.8.2** (done) — Wiki background progress + cancellation. Lock payload carries `phase` / `modules_total`/`_done` / `current_module`; `ctx project check` renders `bg_refresh=true (generating 3/12 "libs/foo" pid=1234)`. New `--stop` flag sends SIGTERM and cleans up stale locks. Closes both known gaps from v0.8.1. No new deps.
- **v0.8.3** (done) — `ctx project check --watch`: generator-based live-tail that polls the lock and re-prints the snapshot until the refresh settles. `--json` mode streams consecutive reports separated by blank lines. Closes the "no live tail" gap from v0.8.2. No threads, no new deps.
- **v0.8.4** (done) — `.refresh.last` outcome record: the runner writes `{completed_at, exit_code, modules_updated, elapsed_seconds}` in its `finally` block (clean / SIGTERM / crash all covered), and `ctx project check` renders `bg_refresh=false (last: ok 12 modules 47s, 3 min ago)` or `FAILED exit=1 … — see .refresh.log`. Closes the "no transition-to-error surface" gap from v0.8.3. No new deps, no new process.
- **v0.8.5** (done) — Error log tail: on a non-clean, non-SIGTERM exit the runner captures the current run's last ~20 lines of `.refresh.log` into `.refresh.last.log_tail`, and `ctx project check` renders them as an indented block under the `FAILED exit=…` last-run hint — so diagnosing a crashed refresh no longer needs a second `cat .refresh.log`. Closes the "no error-tail surface" gap from v0.8.4. No new deps.
- **v0.8.6** (done) — MCP `lvdcp_status` surfaces bg refresh state. `ProjectStatus.wiki_refresh` (nested) mirrors the `CopilotCheckReport.wiki_refresh_*` / `wiki_last_refresh_*` fields so agents and dashboards see the same bg-refresh snapshot the CLI shows (live progress, last-run outcome, crash tail). Lazy import of `libs.copilot` keeps non-wiki consumers cost-free. No new deps.
- **v0.8.7** (done) — Dashboard renders `wiki_refresh` panel. New partial `apps/ui/templates/partials/wiki_refresh.html.j2` draws the v0.8.6 `ProjectStatus.wiki_refresh` field in four visually distinct shapes (running / clean / SIGTERM / FAILED-with-log-tail) on `/project/<slug>`. Hidden for projects that never ran a refresh. Closes the #1 known gap from v0.8.6 (data model ready, no UI). One `{% include %}`, no route change, no new deps.
- **v0.8.8** (done) — HTMX live-polling on the `wiki_refresh` panel. New public helper `libs.status.aggregator.build_wiki_refresh` + new fragment route `GET /api/project/<slug>/wiki-refresh` let the panel update in place every ~2 s while a refresh runs. Outer wrapper's `hx-get` absence after completion self-cancels polling — no JS, no SSE, no `hx-swap-oob`. Cadence matches `ctx project check --watch` (v0.8.3). Closes the #1 known gap from v0.8.7.
- **v0.8.9** (done) — One-shot crash toast on the `wiki_refresh` panel. New fixed-position `#toast-region` drop zone in `base.html.j2`; the polling fragment endpoint emits an `hx-swap-oob="beforeend:#toast-region"` red flash banner on the exact tick that flips the panel to `FAILED`. Gated by four predicates (`HX-Request` + non-live + real-crash exit + `last_completed_at` within 15 s) so the toast fires exactly once per crash event and stays silent on full page reload, SIGTERM cancel, clean completion, and manual `curl`. Closes the second known gap from v0.8.8.
- **v0.8.10** (done) — Error-backoff shell on the `wiki_refresh` polling endpoint. `/api/project/{slug}/wiki-refresh` now wraps its status-assembly path in try/except: on any internal exception it returns 200 with the partial in degraded mode (yellow "refresh status unavailable" card + `hx-trigger="every 30s"` instead of `every 2s`). `except HTTPException: raise` preserves the 404-for-unknown-slug contract. Full-page `/project/<slug>` still 500s on real errors, so the degraded shell is scoped to continuous polling only. Closes the first operational known gap from v0.8.8 (500 mid-poll → HTMX hammers at 2 s; silent `None` → polling stops forever).
- **v0.8.11** (done) — Recovery toast on `wiki_refresh` degraded → normal. Symmetric to v0.8.9's red crash toast: on the exact poll that flips the panel out of degraded mode, the fragment carries a green `hx-swap-oob` banner into `#toast-region`. Detection is pure-HTMX: the degraded wrapper sets `hx-headers='{"X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded": "true"}'`; the route sees the marker on a now-successful assembly and flips `show_recovery_toast=True` for exactly one response. The new successful wrapper omits the marker → no replay. No cookies, no session store, no JS. Closes the top known gap from v0.8.10 (silent self-heal).
- **v0.8.12** (done) — Auto-dismiss for the recovery toast. Inline `animation: lvdcp-toast-fadeout 8s forwards` on the green toast only (crash toast stays sticky) — 6 s at full opacity, 2 s fade to `opacity: 0` + `pointer-events: none`. Zero JS, no new deps, ~200 bytes of inline CSS added only when the toast renders. Locks in the red/sticky vs green/transient UX asymmetry: bad news demands acknowledgment, good news fades. Closes the top UX gap from v0.8.11.
- **v0.8.13** (done) — Accessibility + hover polish on the v0.8.12 fade. New `lvdcp-recovery-toast` class hook hangs two rules off the toast: `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) { animation: none !important; opacity: 1 !important; pointer-events: auto !important; }` cancels the fade for users who've opted out of OS-level motion (toast then stays sticky like the crash toast); `:hover { animation-play-state: paused !important; }` freezes the fade while the cursor is over the toast, resuming from the current opacity on mouse-out. `!important` needed to beat the inline `animation:` shorthand's specificity-1000. Both rules scoped to `{% if show_recovery_toast %}` so idle polls still ship zero a11y CSS. 1168 tests passing.
- **v0.8.14** (done) — "Retry now" escape hatch on the degraded card. Adds a small button inside `{% if degraded %}` that hits `GET /api/project/<slug>/wiki-refresh` via `hx-get` + `hx-target="#wiki-refresh-panel"` + `hx-swap="outerHTML"` + `hx-disabled-elt="this"`, echoing the same `X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded` marker the polling wrapper sends. Marker parity means a successful manual click flips `show_recovery_toast=True` and fires the green recovery toast exactly like an auto-recovery would — identical success UX regardless of trigger source. Scoped to degraded mode only, no new route, no JS. Closes the user-agency gap carried from v0.8.10. 1171 tests passing.
- **v0.8.15** (done) — Toast-render telemetry on the `wiki_refresh` panel. Closes the five-release observability gap: the crash toast (v0.8.9) and recovery toast (v0.8.11) have been shipping without any server-side signal about whether they actually fire. Route now emits `log.info("ui.wiki_refresh.toast.rendered", extra={"event": ..., "slug": ..., "kind": "crash"|"recovery", "trigger": "poll"|"manual"})` via stdlib logging exactly when a toast reaches the user's DOM; idle polls emit zero telemetry. The v0.8.14 Retry button grows a second header, `X-LV-DCP-Retry-Source: manual` (the auto-poll wrapper stays unchanged — its absence classifies the trigger as `"poll"`), and the new `_classify_recovery_trigger` helper splits recoveries into auto vs. manual. Answers three questions that used to require UI instrumentation: which projects flap refresh often enough to hit the crash toast, whether users click Retry vs. wait for the 30 s poll, and whether crash toasts land while the dashboard is actually open. `extra={}` pattern means a future structlog / OTel adapter picks the events up with zero template changes. 5 new `caplog`-based integration tests, one v0.8.14 test updated to count the `"X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded": "true"` substring instead of the full `hx-headers` attribute (the button JSON now carries two keys). 1176 tests passing.
- **v0.8.16** (done) — `forced-colors: active` adaptation on the `wiki_refresh` crash + recovery toasts. Closes the last carry-forward a11y gap on the toast subsystem. In Windows high-contrast mode (and equivalent OS-level palettes on macOS/Linux) the UA remaps solid colors to `Canvas`/`CanvasText` and forcibly drops `box-shadow`, leaving the banner text visible but with no visual container — free-floating text pasted onto the dashboard. Two scoped `<style>` blocks now hang `@media (forced-colors: active)` rules off the existing `lvdcp-recovery-toast` class and a new `lvdcp-crash-toast` class: `border: 1px solid CanvasText` restores the container frame (borders are exempt from color remap per spec), `box-shadow: none` silences UA shadow-drop, `<code>` slug chip gets the same frame, button opacity pins to 1 so it doesn't read as disabled. The recovery toast additionally cancels the v0.8.12 fadeout in forced-colors — matches the v0.8.13 `prefers-reduced-motion` logic (a user on high-contrast is almost certainly an a11y user; banners on timers are hostile). Both rules scoped inside their existing `{% if show_*_toast %}` guards; idle polls still ship zero forced-colors CSS. 4 new integration tests covering presence/absence and per-toast scoping. 1180 tests passing.
- **v0.8.17** (done) — a11y parity for the `lvdcp-pulse` running indicator on the `wiki_refresh` panel. Closes the last carry-forward a11y gap left after v0.8.16. The 10×10 blue dot on the Running card has been cycling opacity 1↔0.4 via `@keyframes lvdcp-pulse 1.5s infinite ease-in-out` since v0.8.7, and two scenarios were still broken: users with `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` were subjected to the infinite animation (v0.8.13 fixed this for the recovery toast fadeout but not the pulse), and users on `forced-colors: active` had the dot's inline `background:#1976d2` remapped to `Canvas` — the page background — making it invisible (v0.8.16 fixed this for crash + recovery toasts but not the pulse). Template now attaches a new `lvdcp-pulse-dot` class hook to the span and the existing `<style>` block grows two sibling media-query rules: `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` cancels the animation and pins opacity to 1; `forced-colors: active` does the same plus paints the dot with the `CanvasText` system-color token (system tokens survive the UA color remap, author RGB values don't). Chose solid `CanvasText` fill over a 1 px border because on a 10×10 element the border would be ~40 % of the visual mass with an inner area still matching `Canvas` — a hollow ring reads poorly as a status indicator. Animation cancel in forced-colors is technically optional (the animation only mutates opacity, which isn't remapped), but a user on forced-colors is almost certainly an a11y user and the adjacent "Running · phase: X" label conveys state regardless — same trade-off as v0.8.13 / v0.8.16. All rules stay scoped inside `{% if wr.in_progress %}`: idle/clean/crashed responses ship zero pulse CSS, zero keyframes, zero media queries. With this release the `wiki_refresh` subsystem is a11y-complete on all three animated elements — recovery toast fade (v0.8.13 + v0.8.16), crash toast container (v0.8.16), running-status dot (v0.8.17). The running card's nested progress bar is the only remaining a11y debt and is explicitly documented as a known gap for v0.8.18 or v0.8.19. 5 new integration tests covering the `class="lvdcp-pulse-dot"` hook, exact rule bodies under both media queries, absence on non-running responses, and a regression guard that the default `animation:lvdcp-pulse 1.5s infinite ease-in-out` still ships for non-a11y users. 1185 tests passing.
- **v0.8.18** (done) — a11y parity for the `wiki_refresh` progress bar. Closes the final a11y debt on `wiki_refresh`: the horizontal module-progress bar (6 px track with `background:#bbdefb` + fill with `background:#1976d2` and a `transition:width 0.3s` that animates the width change on every 2 s poll tick as `modules_done` advances) had two broken scenarios. Under `forced-colors: active` (Windows high-contrast mode and equivalent accessibility palettes) the UA remaps both `#bbdefb` and `#1976d2` to system `Canvas` — identical to the page background — so the 6 px bar becomes an invisible sliver and the entire module-progress signal is lost. Under `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` (vestibular sensitivity, screen-reader users) the `transition:width 0.3s` fires on every poll tick for the duration of the refresh, which on a 100-module project is ~100 repeating slide animations at 2 s intervals — exactly the kind of repeating motion the preference is meant to suppress. v0.8.17 closed both gaps for the pulse dot but explicitly deferred the progress bar as a known gap with "different class of element" reasoning. This release closes it: the track and fill `<div>`s now carry `lvdcp-progress-track` / `lvdcp-progress-fill` class hooks, and the existing `<style>` block (already housing v0.8.17's pulse-dot rules) grows three sibling rules — `border: 1px solid CanvasText` on the track (borders survive the forced-colors remap per spec, giving the container a visible frame even when the fill colour becomes `Canvas`), `background: CanvasText` on the fill (so the indicator itself is a solid dense shape against the remapped track), and `transition: none` on the fill under both `prefers-reduced-motion` and `forced-colors` (consistency with v0.8.17 — a11y mode users shouldn't pay a motion tax for a decorative transition). All rules stay scoped inside `{% if wr.in_progress %}` — idle / clean / crashed / degraded responses ship zero progress-bar CSS. Chose to reuse the existing pulse-dot `<style>` block rather than open a second one: same outer guard, shared `@media` declarations, ~150 bytes of inert selectors on running responses where `modules_total` is still unknown but still cheaper than the duplicated `@media` blocks a split would need. With this release the `wiki_refresh` subsystem is a11y-complete on all four animated / coloured interactive elements: recovery toast fade (v0.8.13 + v0.8.16), crash toast container (v0.8.16), running-status pulse dot (v0.8.17), progress bar (v0.8.18). No more a11y debt on this subsystem. 7 new integration tests covering class-hook presence on both divs, exact rule bodies under both media queries, absence on pre-`modules_total` responses (DOM contract only — the CSS block still ships but inert), absence on non-running responses (full CSS-and-DOM absence), and a regression guard that the default `transition:width 0.3s` still ships for non-a11y users. 1192 tests passing.
- **v0.8.19** (done) — outage-duration signal on the `wiki_refresh` recovery toast. Since v0.8.11 the green recovery toast has read "Wiki refresh status recovered — `<slug>` is reachable again. Resuming normal polling." — the copy told the user *that* recovery happened but never *how long* they were looking at the yellow degraded card, a gap explicitly documented when v0.8.15 added `trigger=manual|poll` telemetry. This release closes it: a user returning to their dashboard after lunch now sees "reachable again after 1h 14m" instead of a generic "reachable again", short blips read "after 47s" / "after 2m 17s". Design: the route holds **no server-side state** tracking outage starts — no session, no cookie, no Redis entry, the dashboard stays stateless HTMX end-to-end. The outage-start timestamp instead rides on the browser via an HTMX `hx-headers` round-trip, identical to the v0.8.11 `X-LV-DCP-Was-Degraded` marker and the v0.8.15 `X-LV-DCP-Retry-Source` classifier. On the first degraded render the route's `except` branch stamps `degraded_since = int(time.time())` into the template context and the degraded wrapper's `hx-headers` JSON includes `"X-LV-DCP-Degraded-Since": "<ts>"` alongside the was-degraded marker; on every subsequent degraded tick HTMX echoes the header back, the route parses it via `_parse_degraded_since(request)`, and the new degraded render re-stamps the **same** value — so the original start time is preserved indefinitely across a long outage rather than resetting every tick. On the recovery tick the same echo is translated into `outage_seconds = now - since`, formatted via `_format_outage_duration(seconds)` as a short human label (`"<1s"` / `"47s"` / `"2m 17s"` / `"1h 23m"` — only the two largest non-zero units, so `1h 23m` not `1h 23m 47s` for scannability), and the template splices it into the toast copy via `{% if outage_duration_label %}is reachable again after {{ outage_duration_label }}. {% else %}is reachable again. {% endif %}`. A missing / malformed / future header collapses cleanly to the pre-v0.8.19 copy so browser tabs that opened on older builds still get the recovery toast on rolling upgrades — they just don't get the duration suffix. The Retry button's `hx-headers` JSON now carries all three markers (was-degraded + retry-source + degraded-since) so manual-retry recoveries surface the duration identically to poll-initiated recoveries — no split UX where one path flashes "recovered after 2m" and the other flashes a generic "recovered". Parser is defensive: absent / non-integer / non-positive / future values all collapse to `None`, which is safe because the downstream branch falls back to the pre-v0.8.19 copy. Future-dated timestamps are rejected in the parser, but a very-old real timestamp is technically accepted — outage length is a telemetry hint, not a security boundary, so a malicious client at worst inflates its own label. The `ui.wiki_refresh.toast.rendered` log event gains an `outage_seconds` field (integer or `None`) alongside the v0.8.15 `trigger` field — field shape stays stable across both paths so downstream structured-log consumers parse both code paths identically and can plot mean/p95 outage duration directly from the field without re-deriving it from tick counts. Closes the recovery-duration item that was documented as future work in the v0.8.15 release notes; the v0.8.x `wiki_refresh` arc is now complete across four axes — visibility (v0.8.9 crash, v0.8.11 recovery), interactivity (v0.8.14 retry), telemetry (v0.8.15 trigger + v0.8.19 outage_seconds), and accessibility (v0.8.13 reduced-motion / v0.8.16 forced-colors / v0.8.17 pulse dot / v0.8.18 progress bar). 8 new integration tests covering fresh-stamp on first degraded render (within the ±1 s request window), verbatim preservation across multi-tick outages (137-second-old timestamp echoed back byte-for-byte), malformed-input fresh restamp (three representative failure modes), Retry button carrying all three markers, end-to-end "reachable again after 2m 17s" copy from a 137-second simulated outage, pre-v0.8.19 backwards-compatible fallback copy when the header is absent, malformed-value fallback sweep (four garbage values — garbled / `0` / `-42` / future — each collapsing to fallback copy without crash), and two telemetry tests locking the log-event field shape (integer for a 42-second outage with ±1 tolerance, `None` when the header is absent so downstream consumers see a stable key). 14 parametrized unit tests on `_format_outage_duration` covering every boundary (0 / 1 / 59 / 60 / 3599 / 3600 / 86400) plus representative midrange values (42 / 137 / 180 / 3660 / 5025). 1212 tests passing.
- **v0.8.20** (done) — Java tree-sitter parser. First shipped increment of Phase 10 (Java / Kotlin / Swift parsers, VS Code marketplace, Obsidian nightly sync): the `wiki_refresh` arc closed in v0.8.19 and the next growth axis is language coverage — parser support for JVM / systems languages not yet indexed. Java was chosen as Phase 10's opener because it's a self-contained deliverable (grammar is a stable published wheel, already a transitive dep) and follows the same `TreeSitterParser` hook-method shape as the Go and Rust parsers that shipped in Phase 6 — so no new infrastructure, just a new grammar + symbol-type map + role rules. `libs/parsers/java.py` is a ~150-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "java"` and hook overrides for `_get_ts_language` (binds `tree_sitter_java.language()`), `_symbol_type_map` (five type-declaration nodes — `class_declaration` / `interface_declaration` / `enum_declaration` / `annotation_type_declaration` / `record_declaration` — all collapse to `SymbolType.CLASS`; `method_declaration` + `constructor_declaration` → `METHOD`; `field_declaration` → `VARIABLE`), `_import_node_types` (`{"import_declaration"}`), `_detect_role` (directory signals `/src/test/java/` / `/tests/` / `/test/` plus filename fallbacks `*Test.java` / `*Tests.java` / `Test*.java` covering JUnit 3 and 4+ conventions — `role="test"` otherwise `"source"`), `_extract_name` (Java field names live nested inside `variable_declarator` children, not directly on `field_declaration`, so the default base hook returns `None` — the override walks the children, finds the first declarator, reads its `name` field; multi-declarator `int a, b, c;` surfaces only the first name, matching the base's one-node-one-symbol contract), `_extract_import_ref` (reads whichever of `scoped_identifier` or plain `identifier` appears inside an `import_declaration` — wildcard `import java.util.*;` naturally reads as `java.util` because the grammar places `*` as a sibling token, static `import static java.util.Arrays.asList` surfaces the full symbol path, all emitted as `dst_type="module"`), and static `_module_fq` (strips the first `src/main/java/` or `src/test/java/` source root encountered anywhere in the path so nested Gradle multi-module projects `modules/foo/src/main/java/com/example/Bar.java` correctly derive `com.example.Bar`, then dots the remainder). Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains a `.java → java` extension map and a `"java": JavaParser()` entry in `_PARSERS`; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"java"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES` so indexed Java files count toward symbol-extraction coverage metrics; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"java"` to `_SRC_LANGS` so Java files count toward the parseable-source-files denominator in per-project coverage percentages. Design choices locked by test for v1: static-final fields (`public static final int MAX_SIZE = 1024`) map to `VARIABLE` uniformly rather than `CONSTANT` — promoting them requires inspecting modifier children at parse time, documented as a deliberate v1 scope limit with `test_extracts_static_final_field` locking the behaviour so a future promotion becomes an explicit contract break rather than a silent flip; wildcard imports drop the `.*` suffix (graph consumers care about modules, not whether every symbol is pulled); the parser does not yet emit `INHERITS` / `IMPLEMENTS` edges for `extends` / `implements` clauses nor `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges for method invocations — follows the Go / Rust parser shape (the Python parser's richer call-graph is not yet generalized to non-Python languages), with both listed as plausible future sub-increments if a driving use case arrives. 33 new tests across six classes in `tests/unit/parsers/test_java_parser.py`: **10 symbol-extraction** (class / interface / enum / annotation-type / record / method / constructor / interface-method / field / static-final-field plus the enum-method nesting contract asserting `parent_fq_name` carries the enum declaration), **4 import-relations** (scoped imports surface as `java.util.List` / `java.util.Map`, wildcard drops `.*` to `java.util`, static imports surface the full `java.util.Arrays.asList` path, `dst_type == "module"` for every import edge), **7 role-detection** (Maven `src/main/java` / bare repo root / Maven `src/test/java` / `tests/` dir / `*Test.java` suffix outside tests dir / `*Tests.java` suffix / JUnit 3 `Test*.java` prefix), **5 module-FQ derivation** (Maven main-root / test-root / nested Gradle multi-module / bare dotted / `.java` extension stripping), **3 edge cases** (minimal single-class file, empty file emits zero symbols and zero tree-sitter errors, `ParseResult.language == "java"`), and **3 registry-wiring tests** (extension detection resolves bare and Maven paths to `"java"`, `get_parser("java")` returns a `JavaParser` instance, `JavaParser().language == "java"`). Full suite: **1245 passing** (+33 vs v0.8.19 baseline 1212). Ruff clean on 376 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 171 files. Next plausible increments along the same axis: Kotlin (shares the JVM story), then Swift; Java inheritance / call-graph edges remain possible follow-ups.
- **v0.8.21** (done) — Kotlin tree-sitter parser. Second shipped increment of Phase 10: v0.8.20 opened Phase 10 with Java and committed to Kotlin as the natural next step (shares the JVM story); this release follows through. `libs/parsers/kotlin.py` is a 116-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "kotlin"` following the exact hook-method shape established by Java. `_symbol_type_map` collapses `class_declaration` (regular / interface / enum / annotation / data / sealed — Kotlin uses one AST node for all and distinguishes via modifier children) and `object_declaration` onto `SymbolType.CLASS`; `function_declaration` → `METHOD`; `property_declaration` → `VARIABLE`. `companion_object` is intentionally **not** in the map — the grammar gives companion objects no `name` field so the base walker naturally skips them for symbol emission but still recurses into the body, so methods and properties defined inside a companion land with `parent_fq_name = EnclosingClass`, matching Kotlin's `EnclosingClass.member` access semantics. `_extract_name` overrides the `property_declaration` case because Kotlin buries the identifier inside a `variable_declaration` child rather than exposing it on the property node — parity with Java's `field_declaration > variable_declarator` dance. `_import_node_types = {"import"}` and `_extract_import_ref` reads the `qualified_identifier` sibling before the `.*` and `as Alias` tokens: wildcard `import java.util.Map.*` naturally reads as `java.util.Map` because the grammar places `.` and `*` as sibling tokens after the qualified_identifier, and alias `import com.example.Foo as FooAlias` surfaces the original module path since the graph tracks real dependencies, not compile-time-local aliases; all emitted as `dst_type="module"`. `_detect_role` walks directory fragments first (`src/test/kotlin/`, `src/androidTest/kotlin/` for standard Gradle and Android instrumented tests, plus `src/test/java/` / `src/androidTest/java/` for Kotlin files in mixed Java/Kotlin projects, plus generic `/tests/` / `/test/`) then filename fallback (strips `.kt` / `.kts` first before checking `*Test` / `*Tests` suffix or `Test*` prefix so `ConfigTest.kt` outside a dedicated test dir still classifies as test); Gradle Kotlin DSL scripts `.kts` intentionally stay `source` so `build.gradle.kts` is still indexed. Static `_module_fq` strips the first recognised source root (`src/main/kotlin/` / `src/test/kotlin/` / `src/androidTest/kotlin/` plus the Java-rooted variants) encountered anywhere in the path, so nested Gradle multi-module projects `modules/foo/src/main/kotlin/com/example/Bar.kt` derive `com.example.Bar`; both `.kt` and `.kts` extensions are stripped before the source-root logic runs. Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains `.kt → kotlin` and `.kts → kotlin` extension maps plus `"kotlin": KotlinParser()` in `_PARSERS`; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"kotlin"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES`; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"kotlin"` to `_SRC_LANGS`. Design choices locked by test for v1: `const val MAX_SIZE: Int = 1024` maps to `VARIABLE` rather than `CONSTANT` uniformly (parity with the Java v1 decision to map `static final` to `VARIABLE`) — promoting requires inspecting the `modifiers` child at parse time, documented as a deliberate v1 scope limit with `test_extracts_const_val_inside_companion` locking the behaviour so a future promotion is an explicit contract break; the parser does not yet emit `INHERITS` edges for delegation specifiers (`class Loaded : State()`, `object Loading : State()`, `class Foo : Interface, OtherInterface`) — Java has the same v1 gap, both listed as plausible future sub-increments; primary constructor properties (`class Config(val name: String)`) and data class components (`data class Point(val x: Int, val y: Int)`) don't surface as separate symbols — they live inside `primary_constructor > class_parameters` as `class_parameter` nodes, not `property_declaration`, adding them requires a dedicated walker. 43 new tests across six classes in `tests/unit/parsers/test_kotlin_parser.py`: **15 symbol-extraction** (class / interface / enum class / annotation class / data class / sealed class with nested object + data class / object declaration / top-level function / method-inside-class / interface-method / property / top-level property / `const val` inside companion / companion-member parent-fq-name invariant / enum-method nesting), **4 import-relations** (scoped / wildcard-as-package / alias-as-original-module / `dst_type == "module"` invariant), **10 role-detection** (Gradle main / bare repo root / Gradle test / Android test / Kotlin under Java test root in mixed project / `tests/` dir / `*Test.kt` suffix / `*Tests.kt` suffix / `Test*.kt` prefix / `.kts` Gradle script stays `source`), **8 module-FQ derivation** (main-kotlin / test-kotlin / androidTest-kotlin / mixed-project java-root / nested multi-module Gradle / bare dotted / strip `.kt` / strip `.kts`), **3 edge cases** (minimal / empty / `ParseResult.language == "kotlin"`), and **3 registry-wiring tests** (`.kt` / `.kts` / Gradle-path detection all resolve to `"kotlin"`; `get_parser("kotlin")` returns a `KotlinParser` instance; `KotlinParser().language == "kotlin"`). Full suite: **1291 passing** (+43 vs v0.8.20 baseline 1245). Ruff clean on 378 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean. With Java (v0.8.20) and Kotlin (v0.8.21) shipped, the JVM pair is complete; next language target is Swift, after which sub-increments deepening language support (inheritance edges for Java / Kotlin, data class / record component extraction, call-graph edges) start to compete with VS Code marketplace / Obsidian nightly sync on prioritisation — driven by concrete user signals rather than a fixed order.
- **v0.8.22** (done) — Swift tree-sitter parser. Third shipped increment of Phase 10 and the one that closes the phase's language-coverage axis: with v0.8.20 (Java) and v0.8.21 (Kotlin) delivering the JVM pair, Swift — the third language named in the Phase 10 opener — was the remaining parser target. `libs/parsers/swift.py` is a ~130-line `TreeSitterParser` subclass with `language = "swift"` following the hook-method shape established by the Java and Kotlin parsers. `_symbol_type_map` collapses `class_declaration` (which the Swift grammar uses unified for `class` / `struct` / `actor` / `enum` / `extension` declarations, distinguishing them via leading-keyword children) and `protocol_declaration` onto `SymbolType.CLASS`; `function_declaration`, `init_declaration`, and `protocol_function_declaration` (the grammar uses a distinct node kind for methods inside protocol bodies) all map to `SymbolType.METHOD`; `property_declaration` → `SymbolType.VARIABLE`. `_import_node_types = {"import_declaration"}` and `_extract_import_ref` walks children for the first `identifier` — this naturally handles both plain `import Foundation` → `Foundation` and scoped `import class Foundation.NSData` → `Foundation.NSData` because the grammar exposes the full dotted path on a single identifier node regardless of declaration-kind modifier; all emitted as `dst_type="module"`. `_detect_role` walks directory fragments first — SPM's `Sources/` and `Tests/` as both path fragments (contains-match) and prefixes (startswith-match), plus generic `/Tests/` / `/tests/` / `/Test/` / `/test/` fallbacks for Xcode project layouts where flat app-name folders and companion `<Name>Tests/` directories replace SPM's rigid structure — then filename fallback strips `.swift` before checking `*Tests` / `*Test` suffix or `Test*` prefix so both `MyAppTests/LoginTest.swift` and bare `LoginTest.swift` classify as `test`. Static `_module_fq` strips `.swift`, then finds `/Sources/` or `/Tests/` anywhere in the path or as a startswith prefix, skips one target-name segment because SPM's `Sources/<TargetName>/...` target name is a build-system convention not part of the symbol's module identity, and dots the remainder — so `Sources/MyLib/Utils/Parser.swift` derives `Utils.Parser`, nested multi-package `modules/foo/Sources/MyLib/Parser.swift` derives `Parser`, and non-SPM paths gracefully fall back to dotted directory segments (`MyApp/Foo.swift` → `MyApp.Foo`, `Foo.swift` → `Foo`). Wiring: `libs/parsers/registry.py` gains `.swift → swift` and `"swift": SwiftParser()`; `libs/status/aggregator.py` adds `"swift"` to `_EXPECT_SYMBOLS_LANGUAGES`; `libs/status/value_metrics.py` adds `"swift"` to `_SRC_LANGS`. Design choices locked by test for v1: extensions emit an apparent duplicate `CLASS` symbol for the extended type (`extension User: Codable` yields a symbol named `"User"`), chosen over overriding `_extract_name` to suppress the duplicate because it's semantically correct — the graph records every file touching `User`, methods inside the extension correctly land with `parent_fq_name = <module>.User`, with `test_extension_emits_duplicate_class_symbol` and `test_extension_method_parent_is_extended_type` locking the invariant; `static let` maps to `VARIABLE` uniformly rather than `CONSTANT` (parity with Java `static final` and Kotlin `const val` — promoting requires modifier-child inspection); `protocol_property_declaration` is intentionally **not** in the symbol map for v1 — the grammar returns an awkward name including the `var` keyword that needs post-processing, plausible sub-increment; the parser does not yet emit `INHERITS` edges for inheritance / protocol conformance (`class Foo: Base, P`, `struct Bar: P, Q`) nor `SAME_FILE_CALLS` edges — same v1 posture as Java and Kotlin parsers, same rationale (not yet generalized from the Python parser); `typealias`, `deinit`, and `enum_case` nodes are out of scope for v1. 43 new tests across six classes in `tests/unit/parsers/test_swift_parser.py`: **15 symbol-extraction** (struct / class / enum / protocol / actor / extension-duplicate-invariant / top-level function / method-inside-class / `init` / protocol method / property / top-level property / `static let` → `VARIABLE` / extension-member parent-fq-name invariant / enum-method nesting), **3 import-relations** (plain / scoped surface full dotted path / `dst_type == "module"` invariant), **10 role-detection** (SPM `Sources/` / bare repo root / SPM `Tests/` / nested multi-package `Tests/` / lowercase `tests/` / `*Test.swift` suffix / `*Tests.swift` suffix / `Test*.swift` prefix / Xcode `AppNameTests/` layout / source-wins fallback), **8 module-FQ derivation** (SPM `Sources/<Target>/` / SPM `Tests/<Target>/` / nested subdir / nested multi-package strip / `Sources/` without target subdir graceful degradation / bare dotted / bare root / `.swift` strip), **3 edge cases** (minimal / empty asserted via `list(result.symbols) == []` because `symbols` is a tuple / `ParseResult.language == "swift"`), and **4 registry-wiring tests** (bare `.swift` / SPM-pathed `.swift` / `get_parser("swift")` returns a `SwiftParser` / `SwiftParser().language == "swift"`). Full suite: **1334 passing** (+43 vs v0.8.21 baseline 1291). Ruff clean on 380 files, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean on 380 files. Phase 10's language-coverage axis is now complete; remaining Phase 10 work is VS Code marketplace publication and Obsidian nightly sync, with language-depth sub-increments (inheritance edges, call-graph edges, primary-constructor / record-component extraction) as targeted follow-ups driven by concrete signals.
- **v0.8.24** (done) — Kotlin `INHERITS` edges. Second deepening-increment after v0.8.23 closed the gap for Java. Kotlin's single-colon syntax collapses Java's `extends` + `implements` onto one production (`delegation_specifiers` under `class_declaration` / `object_declaration`), with three shapes inside each `delegation_specifier`: plain `user_type` (interface conformance, `: Trainable`), `constructor_invocation → user_type` (class extension, `: Animal()`), and `explicit_delegation → user_type` (Kotlin-specific delegation, `: Iface by impl`). All three collapse onto a single `RelationType.INHERITS` — Kotlin has no syntactic class-vs-interface distinction at the heritage position, and keeping one edge type mirrors the v0.8.23 Java design. Explicit delegation deliberately emits INHERITS so impact-analysis queries like "what conforms to `Iface`?" include delegation users. Type-name extraction walks only direct `identifier` children of `user_type` and joins with `.` — `type_arguments` naturally ignored (no special-case filter), `pkg.Outer.Inner` preserved, `Container<String>` emits `Container`. Scope-aware walker is a structural clone of v0.8.23 Java so `class Outer { class Inner : Base }` emits `<module>.Outer.Inner INHERITS Base`, locked by `test_inherits_src_ref_matches_symbol_fq`. Intentional exclusions: **companion objects** (excluded from type-declaration set because `companion_object` has no `name` field and the base walker doesn't emit a Symbol for it — emitting an edge would violate the fq-invariant; first-classing companions is out of v1 scope); **annotation classes** (still `class_declaration` in the grammar but cannot legally carry delegation specifiers, so they naturally produce zero edges with no explicit filter). 20 new tests in `TestInheritsEdges`. Full suite: **1370 passing** (+20 vs v0.8.23 baseline 1350). Swift remains — different AST (`inheritance_specifier` under `class_declaration` / `protocol_declaration`), same concept — and is the next plausible sub-increment.
- **v0.8.23** (done) — Java `INHERITS` edges (`extends` / `implements`). First deepening-increment after Phase 10 closed its language-coverage axis in v0.8.22. The JVM / Swift parsers all shipped without inheritance edges by design (v1 scope lock); this release closes the gap for Java. `JavaParser.parse()` overrides the base, calls it, then walks the CST a second time with a scope-aware stack to emit `Relation(relation_type=INHERITS)` edges for every `extends` / `implements` clause. Heritage shapes covered: `superclass` (class, single, `extends`), `super_interfaces` (class / enum / record, multi, `implements`), `extends_interfaces` (interface, multi, `extends`). Annotation types (`@interface`) explicitly off the allowlist — cannot inherit. Type-name extraction handles `type_identifier` → `"Parent"`, `scoped_type_identifier` → `"pkg.Outer.Inner"` (full dotted path), `generic_type` → strip `type_arguments` and recurse so `Container<String>` emits `"Container"` and `pkg.Box<Integer>` emits `"pkg.Box"` — `test_generic_type_arguments_stripped` asserts `String` / `Integer` never surface as bases. Scope-aware walker tracks `enclosing_fq` alongside each CST node on its work stack so `class Outer { class Inner extends Base {} }` emits `<module>.Outer.Inner INHERITS Base` — matching the `Symbol.fq_name` the base walker stores for `Inner`, locked by `test_inherits_src_ref_matches_symbol_fq` which asserts every INHERITS `src_ref` resolves to a symbol in the same file. Design lock: `INHERITS` collapses `extends` + `implements` onto one `RelationType` variant — interface conformance is treated as inheritance for impact-analysis purposes, adding an `IMPLEMENTS` variant would force downstream consumers (Obsidian wiki sync, pack enrichment, dashboard graph rendering) to decide the split with no driving use case. 17 new tests in `TestInheritsEdges`. Full suite: **1350 passing** (+17 vs v0.8.22 baseline 1333). Kotlin (`class Foo : Base()`) and Swift (`class Foo: Base, P`) use different heritage syntax — same concept, different AST — and are the next plausible sub-increments.
- **v0.8.25** (done) — Swift `INHERITS` edges. Third and final deepening-increment on the inheritance-edge axis after v0.8.23 (Java) and v0.8.24 (Kotlin) — closes the inheritance-edge axis across all three languages with nominal class hierarchies. `SwiftParser.parse()` overrides the base, calls it, then walks the CST a second time with a scope-aware stack. Unlike the JVM pair, Swift has no heritage wrapper node — `inheritance_specifier` nodes are direct siblings of the type name inside `class_declaration` / `protocol_declaration`, separated by `,` tokens; `_collect_heritage` iterates `type_node.children` directly. One `:` syntax covers class inheritance (`class Dog: Animal`), struct conformance (`struct User: CustomStringConvertible`), protocol composition (`protocol P: Q, R`), enum raw-value + protocol (`enum Color: Int, Serializable`), actor conformance (`actor Counter: Sendable`), and extension conformance (`extension User: Equatable, Hashable`) — all collapse onto `RelationType.INHERITS`. Extensions route naturally through the existing duplicate-CLASS-symbol-per-extension shape from v0.8.22: `child_by_field_name("name")` returns the extended type, so `extension User: P` emits `<module>.User INHERITS P` matching the symbol fq the base walker already writes. `where` clauses deliberately do not leak — `class Constrained<T>: Base where T: Hashable` places `type_constraints` as a sibling that's not `inheritance_specifier`, so no `Constrained INHERITS Hashable` edge surfaces. Type-name extraction walks direct `type_identifier` children of `user_type` and joins with `.`, so `Container<String>` emits `Container` and `pkg.lib.Deep<T>` emits `pkg.lib.Deep`. 17 new tests in `TestInheritsEdges`. Full suite: **1387 passing** (+17 vs v0.8.24 baseline 1370). With this ship the inheritance-edge axis across Java/Kotlin/Swift is complete.
- **v0.8.26** (done) — VS Code extension marketplace-readiness prep. Pure metadata + packaging work; no backend or extension-runtime behaviour change. `apps/vscode/package.json` gained `license`, `homepage`, `repository` (with `directory: "apps/vscode"` hint), `bugs`, `keywords`, expanded `categories` from `["Other"]` to `["Programming Languages", "Machine Learning", "Other"]`, `galleryBanner`, `qna`, and `vscode:prepublish` + `publish` scripts. New files: `apps/vscode/README.md` (Marketplace listing content — what, requirements, commands, limitations, links), `apps/vscode/CHANGELOG.md` (Marketplace Changelog tab), `apps/vscode/LICENSE` (Apache 2.0, required inside the `.vsix` for the listing's License link). Expanded `apps/vscode/.vscodeignore` from 4 lines to 12 to exclude source maps, lockfiles, the `.claude/` worktree dir, and recursive `.vsix` self-references. Verified with `npm run package`: 11.02 KB / 9 files (no source maps, no node_modules, no .ts sources). Full release note includes a maintainer publishing runbook and documents the `lv-dcp` publisher-name contingency. Deliberately not done: actual `vsce publish` (requires Publisher account + PAT — user-level actions outside the project), PNG icon (needs designer call), extension settings. Full suite: 1388 passing.
- **v0.8.27** (done) — VS Code extension user-configurable settings. Closes the "no extension settings" gap explicitly scope-locked by v0.8.26. Three settings added via a new `contributes.configuration` block on `apps/vscode/package.json`: `lvdcp.cliPath` (default `"ctx"`, path to the `ctx` executable — unblocks users whose `ctx` isn't on `PATH`, e.g. running via a `uv run python -m apps.cli` wrapper script); `lvdcp.defaultMode` (default `"navigate"`, enum `"navigate" | "edit"` — default retrieval mode for `LV_DCP: Get Context Pack`; `LV_DCP: Show Impact` continues to force `"edit"`); `lvdcp.cliTimeoutMs` (default `30000`, range `1000`–`300000` — unifies the previously-split 30s pack / 15s inspect hardcodes into one user-configurable value). `apps/vscode/src/ctxClient.ts` refactored to take an explicit `CtxConfig` interface as a required parameter on both exported functions, replacing the implicit `"ctx"` PATH lookup and hardcoded timeouts — pure signature change, no behaviour drift at defaults. `apps/vscode/src/extension.ts` adds two tiny readers (`readCtxConfig` and `readDefaultMode`) called per-command-invocation, so edits in Settings UI take effect without extension reload; `readDefaultMode` narrows the string to the literal union with a fallback to `"navigate"` so typos in hand-edited `settings.json` don't crash the extension. No breaking change for anyone on v0.8.26: all defaults reproduce the prior behaviour exactly. README + CHANGELOG gain a Settings section with a `uv run` wrapper example. `npm run compile` + `npm run package` clean; `.vsix` grew from 11.02 KB / 9 files to **11.71 KB / 9 files** — package.json is the only size driver (2.4 KB → 3.93 KB carrying the configuration schema). Full Python suite: **1388 passing** — unchanged (release touches only `apps/vscode/` TypeScript + root version files). Known limits: settings are read per-command-invocation rather than subscribed-to (rare corner case: edits mid-flight don't affect in-flight calls); no `lvdcp.backendUrl` yet (backend discovery is a `ctx` concern via `.context/config.yaml`, not an extension concern); still not published to the Marketplace (same user-gated Publisher + PAT requirement as v0.8.26).
- **v0.8.28** (done) — Obsidian nightly sync (`ctx obsidian sync-all`). Closes the remaining Phase 10 non-parser item. The Obsidian publisher had two invocation paths (manual `ctx obsidian sync <project> --vault <vault>` and after-scan `apps.agent.obsidian_worker.run_obsidian_sync()` debounced by `obsidian.debounce_seconds`) but no scheduled sweep for projects that aren't being actively scanned — so yesterday's scanned projects would drift their Obsidian mirror indefinitely. `ctx obsidian sync-all` walks every project in `~/.lvdcp/config.yaml:projects`, applies a single `--stale-hours N` gate (default 24, `0` = force-sync, missing/corrupt marker = stale because "registered but never synced" is the common first-run case), and shells to `ctx obsidian sync` per project via `subprocess.run` with `--timeout SECS` isolation (default 300). `--dry-run` prints the plan (`sync` / `skip: no cache.db` / `skip: fresh (Xh old)`) without invoking the inner CLI. Failures are per-project: one flaky project doesn't block the rest; exit code `1` iff any failed, with `"Synced: N, skipped: N, failed: N"` on stdout. On success the same `.context/obsidian_last_sync` marker the after-scan worker writes gets advanced, so the daemon's auto-sync won't re-fire inside its own debounce window after the nightly run — one marker, two writers, same gate. Design choice lock: the repo ships the command, not the schedule — LV_DCP's "local-first, minimal moving parts" constitution disfavours an in-process scheduler inside the daemon (extra moving part, fires only when the daemon runs, laptop-closed = no sync), while launchd/cron is the macOS-native way and already what every power user trusts for scheduled jobs. The release note documents the two canonical setups (launchd `StartCalendarInterval` and a `0 3 * * *` crontab) but the LV_DCP installer touches neither — `ctx mcp install` writes to `~/.claude/` because that's Claude's territory, a scheduled daemon writing to `~/Library/LaunchAgents/` is a different trust level the user should own explicitly. 18 new tests in `tests/unit/cli/test_obsidian_sync_all.py` covering config validation (missing / disabled / empty vault_path / no projects), dry-run plan (fresh / cacheless / recently-synced / `--stale-hours 0` force), live sync (subprocess invoked with correct args + marker advanced, fresh skipped, mixed stale/fresh respects gate, one failure doesn't block others, `TimeoutExpired` treated as failure, nonexistent root skipped not crashed), plus parametrized `_is_stale` invariants. All new code lives in `apps/cli/commands/obsidian_cmd.py`: `_read_last_sync` returns `float | None`, `_is_stale` combines missing-marker-is-stale and force-hours-zero into one gate, `@app.command("sync-all")` validates config → builds plan → branches on dry-run → shells out per project → writes marker only on zero-return-code. Zero changes to the daemon, publisher, or after-scan worker. Full suite: **1405 passing** (+18 new sync-all tests). Ruff clean, ruff format clean, mypy strict clean. Known limits: sequential not parallel (20-project sweeps run in <1 min on warm SQLite, parallelization would need vault-lock strategy); no per-project interval override (global `--stale-hours`, "small nightly, big weekly" needs two launchd entries with two `--config` files); no built-in scheduler (deliberate — Windows/Linux users who can't `launchd` would need a `ctx watch install-service`-style follow-up); exit code `0` or `1` not `2`-means-partial (scripts parse the `"failed: N"` tail).
- **Phase 10** (next) — actual marketplace publication (pending Publisher + PAT — user action); VS Code extension `@vscode/test-electron` integration tests; optional dead-code prune pass on `lvdcp_*` MCP tools with zero 30-day usage.
